Ta'zir for Defamatory Insults Beyond Zina Accusations
Ruling that non-zina insults incur ta'zir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that verbal insults causing harm (adha) and attaching disgrace (shayn) incur ta'zir, and distinguish this from qadhf.

Core Idea
Any insult that causes harm and attaches disgrace requires ta'zir, not just zina accusations.

This passage clarifies that in Hanafi law, the scope of punishable defamation extends beyond the specific hadd of qadhf (false accusation of zina). The text lists examples like 'O sinner!', 'O unbeliever!', 'O wicked one!', and 'O thief!' — all of which cause harm and attach disgrace to the victim. Therefore, the offender is subject to discretionary punishment (ta'zir). The rationale is based on the harm (adha) caused, not on a specific textual proof for each insult.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage lists specific insults: ya fasiq, ya kafir, ya khabith, ya sariq. For each, the ruling is that ta'zir is wajib (obligatory) upon the judge to deter such behavior.
Note that the ruling here is for insults that do not imply zina; otherwise, it would be qadhf with hadd.
2
Locate the reasoning (talil)
The text says 'because he harmed him and God attached disgrace to him'. The reasoning is that the insult causes tangible harm and attaches a mark of disgrace to the victim's reputation.
The phrase 'and God attached disgrace' indicates that the disgrace is recognized by Sharia, even if not explicitly mentioned in Quran.
3
Apply the principle to other insults
The principle is general: any insult that causes adha and shayn is subject to ta'zir. This includes words not listed, as long as they are defamatory and harmful.
The judge determines the severity of ta'zir based on the context.
4
Distinguish from qadhf
If the insult explicitly accuses someone of zina (e.g., 'O fornicator'), it falls under qadhf and incurs the hadd punishment. Otherwise, it falls under ta'zir.
This distinction is crucial because the burden of proof and the punishment differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَا إِذَاقَذَفَ مُسْلِمًا بِغَيْرِ الزِّنَاءِ فَقَالَ يَافَاسِقُ اَوْيَا كَافِرُ أَوْ يَا خَبِيْتُ اَوْ يَا سَارِقُ لِأَنَّهُ آذَاهُ وَالْحَ اللَّهُ الشَّيْنَ بِهِ وَلَا
And likewise, when he slanders a Muslim with something other than zina, so he says: 'O sinner!' or 'O unbeliever!' or 'O wicked one!' or 'O thief!', because he harmed him and God attached disgrace to him... and not...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage begins a ruling on ta'zir for verbal insults that do not amount to an accusation of zina. The words mentioned—'O sinner' (ya fasiq), 'O unbeliever' (ya kafir), 'O wicked one' (ya khabith), 'O thief' (ya sariq)—are considered harmful and defamatory (adha) and attach disgrace (shayn) to the victim. Therefore, the offender is subject to discretionary punishment (ta'zir) to deter such behavior and protect the dignity of Muslims. The text cuts off, but the implication is that ta'zir is mandatory. This falls under the broader category of qadhf but without the specific accusation of zina. The difference is that if the insult implies zina, it is full qadhf with hadd; otherwise, it is ta'zir.

Key Terms
آذى (ādhā): Caused harm or offense; in this context, verbal insults that cause emotional or reputational harm.
الشين (al-shayn): Disgrace, dishonor; the insult attaches disgrace to the victim's reputation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, someone who calls a Muslim 'O thief!' without accusing him of zina:
A) Receives the hadd of qadhf.
B) Receives ta'zir.
C) Is not punished because it is not qadhf.
D) Must prove his statement or receive hadd.

Key Takeaway
Verbal insults that cause harm and attach disgrace to a Muslim incur ta'zir, even if they do not constitute an accusation of zina.

Tadakhul of Hadd Punishments: Hanafi v Shafi'i
Ruling on whether one hadd suffices for multiple slanders, zina, or drinking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tadakhul of hadd punishments for repeated same-type offenses and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding slander.

Core Idea
One hadd can suffice for repeated same-type offenses because deterrence may already be achieved; slander overlaps with zina and drinking in Hanafi law.

This passage from a Hanafi manual tackles a crucial question: when do multiple criminal offenses require multiple hadd punishments, and when does one punishment cover them all? The core principle is tadakhul—overlap of penalties. The author explains the Hanafi stance, rooted in the purpose of hadd as deterrence (inzijar), and contrasts it with Imam al-Shafi'i's view, especially regarding slander (qadhf). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how differing premises about whose right predominates lead to divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage discusses: (a) repeated same-type offenses (multiple slanders, multiple zina, multiple drinks); (b) different-type offenses (zina, slander, theft, drinking); (c) slander specifically as overlapping with zina and drinking. List each scenario and the ruling.
Distinguish between same-type and cross-type applications.
2
Extract the Hanafi rationale
For same-type offenses: the purpose of hadd (deterrence) may be achieved by the first punishment, creating a doubt (shubha) about the need for a second. For different-type offenses: each type has a distinct purpose, so no tadakhul. For slander: the right of Allah is predominant, so it is attached to zina and drinking.
The key term is shubha (doubt), which prevents additional punishment.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees on slander: if the slandered person or the alleged act (zina) differs, no tadakhul, because the right of the slave (individual honor) is predominant. This leads to separate punishments for each distinct slander.
Note the difference in taghlib (predominance of right).
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi – one punishment for multiple slanders of different people, or multiple zina acts. Shafi'i – separate punishments for each distinct slander victim or alleged act.
This affects how judges apply hudud.
5
Evaluate the basis of ikhtilaf
The dispute hinges on whether slander is predominantly a right of Allah (Hanafi) or a right of the slave (Shafi'i). This affects both tadakhul within slander and its overlap with other hadd offenses. Both positions are based on valid legal reasoning.
Respect the ikhtilaf as a legitimate difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ قَذَفَ اَوزَنَى اَوْ شَرِبَ غَيْرَ مَرَّةٍ فَحُدَّ فَهُوَ لِذَالِكَ كُلِهِ أَمَّا الْآخَرَان فَلانَّ الْمَقْصِدَ مِنْ إِقَامَةِ الْحَدِ حَقًّا لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى الْإِنْزِ جَارُ وَ اِحْتِمَالُ حُصُولِهِ بِالْاَوَّلِ قَائِمٌ فَيَتَمَكَّنُ شُبْهَةُ فَوَاتِ الْمَقْصُودِ فِي الثَّانِي هَذَا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَازَنَى وَقَذَفَ وَسَرِقَ وَشَرِبَ لِاَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنْ كُلَّ جِنْسِ غَيْرُ الْمَقْصُودِ مِنَ الْأَخَر فَلَا يَتَدَاخَلُ وَأَمَّا الْقَذْقُ فَالْمُغْلَبُ فِيْهِ عِنْدَنَا حَقُّ اللَّهِ فَيَكُونُ مُلْحَقًا بِهِمَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيِّ إِنِ اخْتَلَفَ الْمَقْذُوفَ اَوِ الْمَقْذُوقَ بِهِ وَهُوَ الزِّنَاءُ لَا يَتَدَاخَلُ لِاَنَّ الْمُغْلَبَ فِيهِ حَقُّ الْعَبْدِ عِنْدَهُ
He said: Whoever slanders, or commits zina, or drinks repeatedly, and then receives one hadd, it suffices for all of that. As for the other two (i.e., zina and drinking), the purpose of establishing hadd as a right of Allah is deterrence, and the possibility of achieving it with the first is present, so a doubt of missing the purpose arises in the second. This is contrary to when one commits zina, slanders, steals, and drinks, because the purpose of each type is different from the purpose of the other, so they do not overlap. As for slander, with us the right of Allah is predominant, so it is attached to them (zina and drinking). And al-Shafi'i said: If the slandered person or the thing slandered (i.e., zina) differs, they do not overlap, because with him the right of the slave is predominant.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle of tadakhul (overlap) of hadd punishments. It is a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The ruling states that if a person repeatedly commits the same type of offense (e.g., multiple slanders, or multiple acts of zina, or multiple drinks), and then receives one hadd punishment, that single punishment suffices for all offenses of that same type. The reason is that the purpose of hadd as a right of Allah is deterrence (inzijar), and that purpose may be achieved by the first punishment; thus, repeating the punishment might miss the purpose. However, if the offenses are of different types (e.g., zina, slander, theft, drinking), then each has a distinct purpose, so no tadakhul occurs. For slander specifically, the Hanafi position is that the right of Allah (the public interest) is predominant, so it is treated like zina and drinking (and can overlap with them). Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees: he holds that if either the person slandered or the act alleged (zina) is different, there is no tadakhul, because he considers the right of the slave (individual) predominant in slander.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadākhul): Overlap or merging of punishments, where one penalty suffices for multiple offenses.
حق الله (ḥaqq Allāh): A right that primarily belongs to Allah, relating to public interest and deterrence.
حق العبد (ḥaqq al-ʿabd): A right of the individual, such as personal honor in slander cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does one hadd punishment suffice for a person who commits multiple acts of zina with different partners?
A) Yes, because the purpose of deterrence may be achieved with one punishment.
B) No, because each act involves a different partner, so the right of the individual is violated.
C) Yes, but only if the person repents after the first act.
D) No, because zina is a sin that requires a separate hadd for each act.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that one hadd suffices for repeated same-type offenses due to the doubt of achieving deterrence, and that slander overlaps with zina and drinking because Allah's right is predominant.

Tazir for Slandering a Slave or Kafir
Ruling on tazir for slandering those lacking ihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for slandering a non-muhsan person and explain why tazir applies instead of hadd.

Core Idea
Slander of a slave or kafir incurs tazir, not hadd, because ihsan is lacking.

In Hanafi law, the prescribed punishment (hadd) for false accusation of zina (qadhf) is only applicable when the victim is muhsan—free, Muslim, and chaste. But what happens when the victim is a slave, a female slave, an umm walad, or a disbeliever? The text provides a clear ruling: the accuser receives a discretionary punishment (tazir). This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this distinction and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the victim categories
Note the four categories of victims mentioned: slave (ʿabd), female slave (amah), umm walad (slave mother of her master's child), and kafir (disbeliever). All of these are considered non-muhsan for the purpose of qadhf.
The text uses the phrase 'man qadhafa...' to introduce the ruling.
2
Recognize the condition that triggers hadd
Hadd al-qadhf (80 lashes) requires that the victim be muhsan. Muhsan here means free, Muslim, and chaste. Slaves and kafirs do not meet this condition, so hadd is not obligatory.
The word 'iḥṣān' is the key term.
3
Apply the consequence: tazir becomes wajib
Since the act (qadhf) is still a crime (jinaya), and hadd is prevented, the judge imposes a discretionary punishment (tazir). The text explicitly says 'fa-wajaba al-taʿzīr' — tazir becomes obligatory.
Tazir is a wajib ruling here, not simply permitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَذَفَ عَبْدًا أَوْ آمَةً اَوْهُمْ وَلَدٍ وَ كَافِرًا بِالزِّنَاءِ عُزِرَلَانَّهُ جِنَايَةُ قَذْفِ وَقَدْ امْتَنَعَ وُجُوبُ الْحَدِ لِفَقْدِ الْإِحْصَانِ فَوَجَبَ التعزير
Whoever slanders a slave, or a female slave, or an umm walad, or a disbeliever with zina, he is given tazir, because it is a crime of slander, and the obligation of hadd is prevented due to lack of ihsan, so tazir becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling from the Hanafi school. Hadd al-qadhf (the prescribed punishment for false accusation of zina) requires that the accuser be muhsan (free, Muslim, chaste, etc.). When the victim is a slave (male or female), an umm walad (a slave mother of her master's child), or a disbeliever, they are not considered muhsan in the context of qadhf, so the full hadd punishment cannot be applied. However, the act is still a crime (jinaya) that violates the honor of the person. Therefore, the judge imposes a discretionary punishment called tazir, which is less severe than hadd. This ensures that the wrongdoer is punished without exceeding the limits of the law.

Key Terms
إحصان (iḥṣān): The condition of being free, Muslim, chaste, and married (for zina hadd); for qadhf, it means being free, Muslim, and chaste.
تعزير (taʿzīr): A discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd or kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person falsely accuses a slave of zina, what punishment does the accuser receive according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Hadd of 80 lashes
B) Tazir (discretionary punishment)
C) No punishment because the slave is not Muslim
D) Diyat (blood money)

Key Takeaway
Slander of a non-muhsan person (slave or kafir) results in tazir, not hadd, because the condition of ihsan is absent.

Tazir for Calling a Muslim a Fasiq, Kafir, Khabith, or Thief
Ruling on tazir for insulting a Muslim with non-zina accusations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tazir for non-zina insults, identify the illa of harm and disgrace, and explain why qiyas cannot extend hadd to such insults.

Core Idea
Non-zina insults harm and disgrace but cannot trigger hadd by analogy; they oblige tazir instead.

In the Hanafi fiqh of hudud, the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf) is specific to zina. But what about calling someone a thief or kafir? This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that while such insults cause real harm and disgrace, they cannot be analogized to qadhf to impose hadd. Instead, they incur tazir, a discretionary punishment whose severity in some cases is left to the imam's judgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the insult and the ruling
Determine what the speaker said (e.g., 'O fasiq', 'O kafir', 'O khabith', 'O thief'). The Hanafi ruling is that tazir becomes obligatory (wajib).
The act is slander with something other than zina.
2
Extract the illa (cause)
The text gives two reasons: the speaker harmed the victim (idha) and attached disgrace (shayn) to him. These are the effective causes for tazir.
Without these elements, tazir may not be required.
3
Apply the usul principle
The text states 'there is no room for analogy in hudud'. This means we cannot use qiyas to establish a hadd punishment for these insults by analogy to the hadd of qadhf.
This principle blocks extension of fixed punishments to new offenses.
4
Classify the tazir
Two scenarios: first, if the insult is of the same genus as what obliges hadd (i.e., slander with zina against a non-muhsan), the tazir reaches its maximum. Second, for these other insults, the severity is left to the imam's discretion.
The first scenario is akin to a hadd offense but mitigated, so maximum tazir; the second is fully discretionary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَا إِذَاقَذَفَ مُسْلِمًا بِغَيْرِ الزِّنَاءِ فَقَالَ يَافَاسِقُ اَوْيَا كَافِرُ أَوْ يَا خَبِيْتُ اَوْ يَا سَارِقُ لِأَنَّهُ آذَاهُ وَالْحَقَ الشَّيْنَ بِهِ وَلَا مَدْخَلَ لِلْقِيَاسِ فِي الْحُدُودِ فَوَجَبَ التَّعْزِيرُ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ يَبْلُغُ بِالتَّعْزِيرِ غَايَتَهُ فِي الْجِنَايَةِ الْأُولَى لِأَنَّهُ مِنْ جِنْسِ مَا يَجِبُ بِهِ الْحَدُّوَفِي الْوَجْهِ الثَّانِيَةِ الرَّائُ إِلَى الْإِمَامِ
And similarly, when one slanders a Muslim with something other than zina, saying: O fasiq! or O kafir! or O khabith! or O thief, because he harmed him and attached disgrace to him, and there is no room for analogy in hudud, so tazir becomes obligatory. However, he reaches the maximum with tazir in the first crime (slander with zina) because it is of the same genus as that which requires hadd, and in the second situation (these insults), the opinion is left to the imam.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage explains that insulting a Muslim with names like fasiq (sinner), kafir (disbeliever), khabith (wicked), or sariq (thief) is a punishable offense. The reason is that it causes harm (idha) and attaches disgrace (shayn) to the victim. Importantly, qiyas (analogical reasoning) cannot be applied in hadd punishments, meaning we cannot extend the hadd of qadhf to these insults by analogy; thus, a fixed hadd is not established. Instead, tazir (discretionary punishment) becomes obligatory. The passage further distinguishes two levels: the first type (slander with zina against a non-muhsan) merits the maximum tazir because it is akin to the offense that would require hadd if the victim were muhsan. The second type (insults like fasiq, etc.) is left to the imam's discretion to determine the severity of tazir.

Key Terms
قذف بالغير الزناء (qadhf bi ghayr al-zinā): Accusing a person of something other than zina, such as theft or disbelief.
الشين (al-shayn): Disgrace or dishonor attached to a person by insult.
تعزير (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have fixed hadd or kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does calling a Muslim 'O thief!' incur tazir and not hadd?
A) Because theft is not a sin comparable to zina
B) Because qiyas cannot be used to establish hadd for insults not mentioned in the Quran
C) Because the victim must be a slave
D) Because the imam must first warn the accuser

Key Takeaway
Calling a Muslim a fasiq, kafir, khabith, or thief incurs tazir because it causes harm and disgrace, and qiyas cannot extend hadd to such insults.

Tazir for Calling Someone a Donkey or Pig: Three Hanafi Opinions
Ruling on whether calling someone 'donkey' or 'pig' incurs tazir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on tazir for calling someone a donkey or pig and apply the best (ahsan) opinion based on the victim's social status.

Core Idea
Calling someone 'donkey' may or may not require tazir — the best opinion distinguishes between nobles and commoners.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya presents a case of verbal insult (sabb) that is not qadhf (false accusation of zina) because it does not literally attach disgrace. The author examines three opinions: no tazir, universal tazir based on custom, and a nuanced view that considers the victim's social standing. The last is declared the 'ahsan' (best) opinion, showing how tazir adapts to context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first opinion and its rationale
The base text states no tazir because the insult does not literally attach disgrace – the person is not actually a donkey or pig, so it is not considered defamation.
2
Identify the second opinion and its basis
Some scholars say tazir is given because in our custom (urf) such words are considered insults, regardless of literal meaning.
3
Identify the third opinion and its distinguishing factor
This opinion differentiates between nobles (ashraf) like jurists and Alawis, and commoners. Tazir is imposed for nobles because it causes them discomfort, but not for commoners.
4
Determine which opinion is considered 'ahsan' and why
The author declares the third opinion the best because it accounts for the degree of harm – the insult affects nobles more severely due to their social standing.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
In fatwa, the relied-upon view is the ahsan opinion: tazir for nobles, none for commoners. This is based on the tarjih of later Hanafi scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ يَا حِمَارُا وَيَا خِنْزِيرُ لَمْ يُعَزِّرُ لأَنَّهُ مَا الْحَقَ الشَّيْنَ بِهِ لِلتَّيَقُنِ بِنَفْيِهِ وَقِيلَ فِي عُرْفِنَا يُعَزَّرُ لَانَّهُ يُعَدُّ سَبًّا وَقِيلَ إِنْ كَانَ الْمَسْبُوبُ مِنَ الْأَشْرَافِ كَالْفُقَهَاءِ وَالْعَلْوِيَّةِ يُعَزَّرُ لِاَنَّهُ يُلْحِقُهُمُ الْوَحْشَةَ بِذَالِكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ مِنَ الْعَامَّةِ لَا يُعَزَّرُ و هَذَا أَحْسَنُ
And if he said: O donkey! and O pig! he is not given tazir, because he did not attach disgrace to him, due to the certainty of its negation. And it is said in our custom that he is given tazir because it is considered an insult. And it is said: If the insulted person is from the nobles, like the jurists and the Alawis, he is given tazir because it causes them discomfort, and if he is from the common people, he is not given tazir. And this is the best opinion.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents three opinions regarding calling someone 'donkey' or 'pig' (ya himar, ya khinzir). The first opinion (from the text's author) is that no tazir is required because such words do not literally attach disgrace—since the person is not actually a donkey or pig, the insult is so obviously false that it is not considered defamation. The second opinion is that in our custom (urf), these words are considered insults (sabb), so tazir is imposed. The third opinion, which the author says is the best (ahsan), distinguishes based on the status of the victim: if the victim is a noble person (ashraf) such as a jurist or a sayyid (descendant of Ali), then tazir is given because it causes them great discomfort (wahsha). If the victim is a common person (amma), then no tazir is given. This ruling shows the flexibility of tazir and the role of custom and social status in determining punishment.

Key Terms
أشراف (ashrāf): Nobles or people of high social standing, such as jurists and descendants of Ali (Alawis).
سب (sabb): Insult or verbal abuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the best (ahsan) opinion in the Hanafi school, when is tazir given for calling someone 'donkey'?
A) Always, because it is an insult in custom
B) Never, because it does not attach disgrace
C) Only if the victim is a noble person like a jurist or sayyid
D) Only if the victim is a common person

Key Takeaway
The best Hanafi opinion on tazir for calling someone 'donkey' or 'pig' distinguishes between nobles and commoners, applying tazir only when the victim is of high social standing and the insult causes harm.

Maximum and Minimum of Tazir Punishment: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on the number of lashes for tazir and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum tazir lashes according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, explain the reasoning based on the lowest hadd (adna al-hadd), and compare with Abu Yusuf's position.

Core Idea
Tazir must always be less than the lowest fixed hadd; the Hanafi maximum is 39 lashes (Abu Hanifa) or 75 (Abu Yusuf).

This passage clarifies the parameters of tazir punishment within the Hanafi school. While all agree tazir must be less than a fixed hadd, they differ on the baseline. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists derive punishments by analogy and the priority given to avoiding confusion with hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on maximum and minimum
State the numbers given in the base text: maximum 39 lashes, minimum 3 lashes.
These are the default positions in the book.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The hadith 'Whoever reaches a hadd in other than [the prescribed] is from the transgressors' teaches that tazir cannot equal or exceed a fixed hadd.
This principle is agreed upon by all.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning for 39
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad took the lowest fixed hadd (40 lashes, the slave's punishment for slander) and reduced one lash to avoid equality.
They prioritized caution and clarity.
4
Compare with Abu Yusuf's reasoning for 75
Abu Yusuf considered the lowest hadd for free persons (also 40? But he reduced to 35 or 75 in different narrations, following a narration from Ali).
His method is considered qiyas by the author.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالتَّعْزِيْرُ اكْثَرُهُ تِسْعَةٌ وَثَلَكُوْنَ سَوْطًا وَاقَلَهُ ثَلْتُ جَلْدَاتٍ وَ قَالَ اَبُوْ يُوْسُفَ يَبْلُغُ التَّغْزِيرُ خَمْسًا وَسَبْعِينَ سَوْطًا وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ بَلَغَ حَدَّا فِى غَيْرِ حَةٍ فَهُوَمِنَ الْمُعْتَدِينَ وَإِذَا تَعَدَّرَ تَبْلِيغُهُ حَدَّا فَابُوْ حَنِيفَةَ وَ مُحَمَّدٌ نَظَرَ إِلَى أدْنَى الْحَدِ وَهُوَ حَدَ الْعَبْدِ فِي الْقَذْفِ فَصَرَفَاهُ إِلَيْهِ وَذَالِكَ أَرْبَعُونَ فَنَقَصَامِنْهُ سَوْطًا وَاَبُويُوسُفَ اعْتَبَارَاقَلَّ الْحَدِفِي الْأَحْرَارِ إِذَا لَأَصْلُ هُوَ الْحُرِّيَّةُ ثُمَّ نَقَصَ سَوْطًا فِي رِوَايَةٍ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ زُفَرٌ وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ وَفِي هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَةِ نَقَصَ خَمْسَةٌ وَهُوَ مَا تُوَرٌ عَنْ عَلِيٌّ فَقَلَّدَهُ ثُمَّ قَدَّرَ الْأَدْنَى فِي الْكِتَابِ بِثَلَثِ جَلْدَاتٍ لِأَنَّ مَا دُونَهَايَقَعُ بِهِ الزَّجْرُ وَذَكَرَ مَشَايِخُنَّا اَنَّ اَدْنَاهُ عَلَى مَا يَرَاهُ الْإِمَامُ يُقَدِرُ بِقَدْرِ
And tazir: its maximum is thirty-nine lashes, and its minimum is three lashes. And Abu Yusuf said: Tazir reaches seventy-five lashes. The basis for this is his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Whoever reaches a hadd in other than [the prescribed] is from the transgressors.' And when it is not possible to apply a hadd, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad looked at the lowest hadd, which is the hadd of a slave in slander, and they applied it, and that is forty, so they reduced one lash. And Abu Yusuf considered the lowest hadd for free persons, because the original status is freedom, then he reduced one lash in one narration, and this is the opinion of Zufar, and it is the qiyas. And in this narration he reduced five, and it is what was narrated from Ali, so he followed him. Then he determined the minimum in the book as three lashes, because whatever is less than that does not effect deterrence. And our mashayikh mentioned that its minimum is according to what the imam sees, he determines it to the extent...
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage details the disagreement within the Hanafi school on the maximum number of lashes for tazir. The base text states that the maximum is 39 lashes and the minimum is 3. Abu Yusuf holds that it can reach 75 lashes. The reasoning behind the 39-lash maximum is that the lowest fixed hadd is the hadd for slander of a slave, which is 40 lashes (since the free person's hadd is 80, but a slave gets half). Since tazir should be less than the lowest hadd, they subtract one lash to avoid confusion with hadd, making it 39. Abu Yusuf, however, argues that the baseline should be the lowest hadd for a free person, which is 40 (again, slave slander half of 80), but then he subtracts either one or five lashes in different narrations. The narration subtracting five is attributed to Imam Ali. The minimum of three lashes is established because fewer than three would not achieve deterrence (zajr). The passage concludes that some mashayikh (later scholars) say the minimum is left to the imam's discretion. This shows the nuance in Hanafi jurisprudence: tazir is flexible but must always be less than the lowest hadd of that type.

Key Terms
تعزير (taʿzīr): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd.
أدنى الحد (adnā al-ḥadd): The lowest fixed hadd punishment, used as a benchmark for tazir maximum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why is the maximum tazir set at 39 lashes?
A) Because the hadd for a free person is 80, and half of that is 40, so tazir is one less.
B) Because the lowest hadd is 40 (slave's qadhf), and tazir must be less to avoid confusion with hadd.
C) Because the Prophet's hadith set it at 39.
D) Because the imam can increase it up to 75 if needed.

Key Takeaway
Tazir must be less than the lowest fixed hadd; the Hanafi maximum is 39 lashes (Abu Hanifa) or 75 (Abu Yusuf), with 39 being the mufta bihi.

Ta'zeer for Insults: Calling Someone 'O Donkey' or 'O Pig'
Ruling with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'zeer for non-zina insults and explain the three opinions on calling someone a donkey or pig, identifying the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Not every insult triggers ta'zeer — the harm depends on custom and the status of the insulted.

In this passage, the author shifts from hadd punishments to ta'zeer. While false accusation of zina incurs hadd, other insults that cause disgrace are punishable by ta'zeer. However, for calling someone an animal, the ruling becomes nuanced: three opinions exist within the school. The preferred view differentiates between the elite and commoners. Let's walk through the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage first states that ta'zeer is due for any insult that causes harm and disgrace, even if not a false accusation of zina. Examples: 'O sinner', 'O disbeliever', 'O wicked one'.
2
Understand the default ruling for animal insults
For 'O donkey' or 'O pig', the default ruling is no ta'zeer because these are not real attributes of a human, so no disgrace is attached with certainty.
The reasoning is based on certainty of negation of disgrace.
3
Examine the three Hanafi opinions
Three views: (1) No ta'zeer at all. (2) Ta'zeer in all cases because custom considers it abuse. (3) Ta'zeer only if the insulted person is from the elite (fuqaha, Alawids) because they feel intense distress; otherwise no ta'zeer.
The third view is the preferred one.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The author states 'وهذا أحسن' (this is best), indicating the third view is the relied-upon position.
This preference is based on equitable reasoning considering the sensitivity of notables.
5
Apply the rule
Given a scenario with an insulted person's status and local custom, decide if ta'zeer applies according to the mufta bihi view.
The key factors are the custom (urf) and the status of the insulted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَا إِذَا قَذَفَ مُسْلِمًا بِغَيْرِ الزِّنَاءِ فَقَالَ يَا فَاسِقُ أَوْ يَا كَافِرُ أَوْ يَا خَبِيثُ. وَلَوْ قَالَ يَا حِمَارُ وَيَا خِنْزِيرُ لَمْ يُعَزَّرْ لِأَنَّهُ مَا أَلْحَقَ الشَّيْنَ بِهِ لِلتَّيَقُّنِ بِنَفْيِهِ. وَقِيلَ فِي عُرْفِنَا يُعَزَّرُ لِأَنَّهُ يُعَدُّ سَبًّا. وَقِيلَ إِنْ كَانَ الْمَسْبُوبُ مِنَ الْأَشْرَافِ كَالْفُقَهَاءِ وَالْعَلَوِيَّةِ يُعَزَّرُ لِأَنَّهُ يُلْحِقُهُمُ الْوَحْشَةَ بِذَلِكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ مِنَ الْعَامَّةِ لَا يُعَزَّرُ وَهَذَا أَحْسَنُ
And similarly, if he slanders a Muslim with something other than zina and says 'O sinner' or 'O disbeliever' or 'O wicked one'. And if he says 'O donkey' and 'O pig', he is not to be given ta'zeer because he did not attach disgrace to him due to the certainty of its negation. And it was said in our custom he is given ta'zeer because it is considered abuse. And it was said if the one abused is from the notables like the jurists and the Alawids, he is given ta'zeer because it causes them distress by that; and if he is from the common people, he is not given ta'zeer. And this is best.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on ta'zeer (discretionary punishment) for slander. The author first establishes that ta'zeer is due for any insult that causes harm and disgrace to a Muslim, even if it is not a false accusation of zina (which would incur a hadd punishment). The proof is that the principle 'قياس لا يدخل في الحدود' means that qiyas is not applied in hudud punishments, so ta'zeer is based on harm caused. Then the passage addresses the specific case of calling someone 'donkey' or 'pig'. Since these are not literal qualities of a human, the basic ruling is no ta'zeer. However, three opinions are presented within the Hanafi school: (1) According to our custom (urf), these words are considered abuse, so ta'zeer applies. (2) Ta'zeer applies only if the insulted person is from the elite (e.g., scholars and sayyids), because they feel intense distress; if from the common people, no ta'zeer. (3) The preferred opinion (هذا أحسن) is the latter: it differentiates based on the status of the insulted, which is the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zeer): Discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a specified hadd punishment; it is left to the judge's discretion in amount and type.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina or other defamatory statement; when with zina it incurs hadd; otherwise ta'zeer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, when is ta'zeer given for calling someone 'ya himar' (O donkey)?
A) Always, because it is considered abuse in custom.
B) Never, because it is not a real attribute.
C) Only if the insulted person is from the elite (fuqaha, Alawids).
D) Only if the insulted person is from the common people.

Key Takeaway
Calling someone a donkey or pig incurs ta'zeer only when it causes disgrace — according to custom and the victim's status, with the mufta bihi view limiting it to notables.

Quantity of Ta'zeer: Maximum and Minimum, and Combining with Imprisonment
States the maximum and minimum lashes for ta'zeer and rules on adding imprisonment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maximum and minimum for ta'zeer lashes and explain the evidence (dalil) and qiyas used to derive them.

Core Idea
Ta'zeer must be less than any hadd; the maximum is 39 lashes by qiyas on the slave's hadd of qadhf.

Ta'zeer is a discretionary punishment for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd. The Hanafi school sets a maximum and minimum based on a hadith and analogical reasoning. This lesson presents the main position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the alternative views of Abu Yusuf and Zufar, and the rule on adding imprisonment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the maximum (39 lashes) and minimum (3 lashes) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
This is the position of the Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'Whoever reaches a hadd in other than a hadd is a transgressor.' Understand how this prohibits ta'zeer from equaling a hadd.
The hadith is reported by Bayhaqi and Muhammad as mursal.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith leads to the 39-lashes maximum: the lowest hadd (slave's qadhf) is 40; ta'zeer must be less, hence 39.
Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa chose the slave's hadd as the lowest.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
State that Abu Yusuf and Zufar argue for a higher maximum (75/79) based on the free person's hadd and qiyas.
The qiyas of Zufar is mentioned but not relied upon.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Identify that the mufta bihi position is the 39-lashes view because it is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the most cautious.
The author notes that the qiyas is with Zufar, but the matn gives 39.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالتَّعْزِيرُ أَكْثَرُهُ تِسْعَةٌ وَثَلَاثُونَ سَوْطًا وَأَقَلُّهُ ثَلَاثُ جَلْدَاتٍ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يَبْلُغُ التَّعْزِيرُ خَمْسًا وَسَبْعِينَ سَوْطًا. وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ: مَنْ بَلَغَ حَدًّا فِي غَيْرِ حَدٍّ فَهُوَ مِنَ الْمُعْتَدِينَ. وَإِذَا تَعَذَّرَ تَبْلِيغُهُ حَدًّا فَأَبُو حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ نَظَرَا إِلَى أَدْنَى الْحَدِّ وَهُوَ حَدُّ الْعَبْدِ فِي الْقَذْفِ فَصَرَفَاهُ إِلَيْهِ وَذَلِكَ أَرْبَعُونَ فَنَقَصَا مِنْهُ سَوْطًا. وَأَبُو يُوسُفَ اعْتَبَرَ أَقَلَّ الْحَدِّ فِي الْأَحْرَارِ إِذِ الْأَصْلُ هُوَ الْحُرِّيَّةُ، ثُمَّ نَقَصَ سَوْطًا فِي رِوَايَةٍ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ زُفَرَ وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ، وَفِي هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَةِ نَقَصَ خَمْسَةً وَهُوَ مَأْثُورٌ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ فَقَلَّدَهُ. ثُمَّ قَدَّرَ الْأَدْنَى فِي الْكِتَابِ بِثَلَاثِ جَلْدَاتٍ لِأَنَّ مَا دُونَهَا يَقَعُ بِهِ الزَّجْرُ. وَذَكَرَ مَشَايِخُنَا أَنَّ أَدْنَاهُ عَلَى مَا يَرَاهُ الْإِمَامُ يُقَدِّرُ بِقَدْرِ مَا يَعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ يَنْزَجِرُ لِأَنَّهُ يَخْتَلِفُ بِاخْتِلَافِ النَّاسِ. وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى قَدْرِ عِظْمِ الْجُرْمِ وَصِغَرِهِ. وَعَنْهُ أَنَّهُ يُقَرِّبُ كُلَّ نَوْعٍ مِنْ بَابِهِ فَيُقَرِّبُ الْمَسَّ وَالْقُبْلَةَ مِنْ حَدِّ الزِّنَاءِ، وَالْقَذْفَ بِغَيْرِ الزِّنَاءِ مِنْ حَدِّ الْقَذْفِ. قَالَ: وَإِنْ رَأَى الْإِمَامُ أَنْ يَضُمَّ إِلَى الضَّرْبِ فِي التَّعْزِيرِ الْحَبْسَ فَعَلَ لِأَنَّهُ صَلَحَ تَعْزِيرًا وَقَدْ وَرَدَ الشَّرْعُ بِهِ فِي الْجُمْلَةِ حَتَّى جَازَ أَنْ يَكْتَفِيَ بِهِ فَجَازَ أَنْ يَضُمَّ إِلَيْهِ، وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يُشْرَعْ فِي التَّعْزِيرِ بِالتُّهْمَةِ قَبْلَ ثُبُوتِهِ كَمَا شُرِعَ فِي الْحَدِّ لِأَنَّهُ مِنَ التَّعْزِيرِ
And ta'zeer: most of it is thirty-nine lashes, and least of it is three lashes. And Abu Yusuf said: ta'zeer reaches seventy-five lashes. And the basis in it is his statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever reaches a hadd in other than a hadd, he is among the transgressors.' And when it is impossible to reach a hadd, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad looked at the lowest hadd, which is the hadd of the slave in qadhf, and they directed it to that, and that is forty, so they decreased from it one lash. And Abu Yusuf considered the least hadd among free persons, since the original is freedom, then he decreased one lash in one narration, and that is the saying of Zufar and it is the analogy, and in this narration he decreased five, and it is transmitted from Ali, so he followed him. Then he estimated the least in the book as three lashes, because less than that does not achieve deterrence. And our mashayikh mentioned that its least is what the imam sees, he estimates to the extent that he knows that the person will be deterred, because it varies with the variation of people. And from Abu Yusuf that it is according to the size of the crime, great or small. And from him that he brings each type close to its category: he brings touching and kissing close to the hadd of zina, and qadhf with other than zina close to the hadd of qadhf. He said: And if the imam sees that he should add to flogging in ta'zeer imprisonment, he may do so, because it is valid as ta'zeer and the Law has prescribed it in general, so that it is permissible to suffice with it, so it is permissible to add it to flogging. And for this, ta'zeer for suspicion is not prescribed before its proof, just as it is prescribed in the hadd, because it is from ta'zeer.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage details the quantity of ta'zeer (discretionary lashes). The main Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) sets the maximum at 39 lashes because they reason from the lowest hadd punishment (the slave's hadd for qadhf is 40) and subtract one lash so that ta'zeer does not reach the level of a hadd. Their proof is the hadith: 'Whoever reaches a hadd (punishment) in other than a hadd is a transgressor' — meaning ta'zeer cannot equal a hadd. Abu Yusuf argues that the maximum should be 75 lashes, reasoning from the free person's lowest hadd (80 for qadhf) and subtracting 5 (or 1 in another narration) based on a narration from Ali. Zufar also uses qiyas. The minimum ta'zeer is 3 lashes, as fewer than 3 would not serve as a deterrent. However, later mashayikh (scholars of Transoxiana) say the minimum is left to the imam's discretion based on the individual's temperament. Abu Yusuf also has a view that the amount depends on the severity of the crime, and that one should analogize the nature of the crime to its closest hadd (e.g., inappropriate touching to zina hadd, false accusation not of zina to qadhf hadd). Finally, the passage states that the imam may combine flogging with imprisonment if appropriate, because imprisonment is a valid form of ta'zeer and can be added to flogging. This is different from hadd punishments, where imprisonment before proof is not prescribed.

Key Terms
تعزير (ta'zeer): A discretionary corporal punishment (flogging) for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd; its quantity is set by the jurists to be less than the nearest hadd.
سوط (sawt): A lash or whip; the instrument of flogging in ta'zeer and hadd punishments.
جلدات (jaldat): Strikes of the whip; used interchangeably with 'aswāṭ' for counting lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum number of ta'zeer lashes according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad?
A) 75
B) 39
C) 40
D) 3

Key Takeaway
Ta'zeer lashes range from 3 to 39, based on the principle that it must be less than any hadd, and imprisonment may be added at the imam's discretion.

Maximum Lashes in Ta'zir: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains maximum and minimum ta'zir lashes and the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum ta'zir lashes according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, explain their proofs, and apply the rule that ta'zir must be less than the minimum hadd.

Core Idea
Ta'zir lashes must be less than the minimum hadd; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ on which hadd to benchmark.

This passage from the chapter on qadhf (false accusation) delves into the discretionary punishment (ta'zir). The core issue is the maximum number of lashes the imam may administer. Abu Hanifa and his leading students disagree based on which hadd is taken as the reference point: the slave's hadd for qadhf (40 lashes) or the free person's hadd (80 lashes). Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi jurists balance textual evidence (a hadith warning against exceeding hadd) with the need for effective deterrence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Question
What is the maximum lash count for ta'zir? The passage presents two positions within the Hanafi school.
The question arises because ta'zir is discretionary but bounded by the principle that it cannot equal a hadd punishment.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Proof
Abu Hanifa sets the maximum at 39 lashes. He reasons that ta'zir must be less than the minimum hadd, which for a slave in qadhf is 40 lashes, so he deducts one lash.
His proof includes the hadith 'Whoever reaches a hadd in other than a hadd is transgressing' and the qiyas (analogy) on the slave's hadd.
3
State Abu Yusuf's Position and Proof
Abu Yusuf sets the maximum at 75 (or 79) lashes. He benchmarks the free person's hadd for qadhf (80 lashes) and reduces by one or five lashes based on narrations.
He considers freedom as the original state, so the free person's hadd is the relevant minimum.
4
Analyze the Opposing General Hadith
A hadith in Bukhari and Muslim states: 'Do not beat more than ten lashes except in the limits of Allah.' The Hanafi school argues this is not binding for ta'zir because Companions like Ali and Umar gave more than ten, and their actions would have been rejected if contrary to the hadith.
Thus the hadith is interpreted as a recommendation for non-hudud cases, not a prohibition.
5
Apply the Rule: Ta'zir is Less than the Minimum Hadd
Whichever benchmark is adopted, the key principle is that ta'zir lashes must be strictly fewer than the corresponding hadd. This ensures the fixed punishments of Allah are not equated with discretionary ones.
The minimum ta'zir is three lashes or whatever deters the offender, left to the imam's discretion.

باب حد القذف
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم ما يَعْلَمُ أَنَّهُ يَنْزَجِرُ لِأَنَّهُ يَخْتَلِفُ بِاِخْتِلَافِ النَّاسِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفُ لأَنَّهُ عَلَى قَدْرِعُظْمِ الْجُرْمِ وَصِغَرِهِ وَ عَنْهُ أَنَّهُ يُقَرِّبُ كُلَّ نَوْعِ مِنْ بَابِهِ فَيُقَرِّبُ الشَّمْسَ وَالْقُبْلَةَ مِنْ حَدِ الزِنَاءِ وَالْقَدْفِ بِغَيْرِ الزَّنَاءِ مِنْ حَةِ الْقَدْفِ
ترجمہ تعزیر کی اکثر مقدار انتالیس کوڑے ہیں اور اقل مقدار تین کوڑے ہیں لیکن امام ابو یوسف رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اکثر مقدار پچھتر درے ہیں۔ اس باب میں اصل رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ فرمان ہے کہ جس نے غیر حد میں جد کی مقدار پہنچادی وہ راہ اعتدال سے تجاوز کرنے والا ہے۔ اس کی روایت بیہقی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کی ہے اور محمد نے بھی اسے مرسلا روایت کیا ہے اور جب تعزیر کو حد تک پہنچانا جائز نہ ہوا تو امام ابوحنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے حد کی کم سے کم مقدار کو دیکھا جو قذف کی صورت میں غلام کی حد ہے اس لئے تعزیر سے وہی مقدار مراد لی چونکہ اس میں چالیس درے ہوتے ہیں اور تعزیر کی سزا حد سے کم ہوتی ہے اس لئے ایک درہ اس سے کم کر دیا اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے آزاد شخص کی کم از کم حد یعنی اسی درے کو دیکھا کیونکہ انسان میں اصل آزادی ہے۔ پھر ایک روایت یہ بھی ہے کہ ان میں سے ایک درہ کم کر کے اناسی درے رکھے ۔ امام زفر رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا ہی قول ہے اور قیاس بھی یہی ہے۔ مگر دوسری روایت جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔ ان میں سے پانچ درے کم کر دیئے ہیں۔ کیونکہ حضرت علی کرم اللہ وجہ سے یہی منقول ہے۔ اس لئے انہیں کی تقلید کی ہے (بغوی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے ابن ابی لیلہ سے شرح السنتہ میں یہی ذکر کیا ہے) ۔ پھر کتاب میں تعزیر یکم از کم مقدار تین درے بیان کئے ہیں۔ کیونکہ اس سے کم ایک دو دروں سے تنبیہ کا مقصد حاصل نہیں ہوتا ہے ہمارے مشائخ ماوراءالنہر نے بیان کیا ہے که تغیر کی کم از کم مقدار امام کی رائے پر موقوف ہے۔ یعنی اس کے خیال میں جتنی مقدار سے تنبیہ حاصل ہو جائے جاری کرے کیونکہ تنبیہ مختلف لوگوں کے لحاظ سے مختلف ہوتی ہے ( یعنی بعضوں کو صرف ایک دو دروں سے جو تنبیہ ہو جاتی ہے۔ وہ دوسرے کو دس دروں سے ہو سکتی ہے اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے جرم کے چھوٹے اور بڑے ہونے کے اندازہ پر مقدار مقرر کی ہے اور ان سے یہ روایت بھی ہے کہ ہر قسم کے جرم کو اپنی جنس سے متعلق کیا جائے ۔ اس لئے اگر اجنبیہ عورت کو ہاتھوں سے چھوایا بوسہ لیا تو اسے زنا سے قریب کیا جائے اور اگر تہمت لگائی ہو یعنی زانی کے علاوہ دوسرے الفاظ فسق وغیرہ سے تو قذف کیا تو اسے حد قذف سے قریب کرے (ف معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ ایک حدیث میں ہے کہ حدود الہی کے سوا میں دس درے سے زیادہ نہ مارے جائیں۔ رواہ البخاری ومسلم ۔ لیکن امام ابو حنیفہ و مالک ، شافعی و غیر هم رحمتہ اللہ علیہم نے کہا ہے اس درے سے بھی زیادہ مارنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ صحابہ نے اس سے بھی زیادہ سزادی ہے اور خود حضرت علی و عمر سے بھی زیادہ سزا ثابت ہے، پس اگر ان کا یہ عمل حدیث کے مخالف ہوتا ہے تو صحابہ اس کا انکار فرماتے ہیں)۔
تشریح وَالتَّعْزِيرُ خَمْسًا وَ سَبْعِينَ سَوْطًا وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ قَوْلَهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلام الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔ تعزیر کے ساتھ جس کا حکم
قَالَ وَإِنْ رَأَى الْإِمَامُ أَنْ يَضُمَّ إِلَى الضَّرْبِ فِي التَّعْزِيرِ الْحَبْسَ فَعَلَ لأَنَّهُ صَلُحَ تَعْزِيْرٌ أَوْقَدْ وَرَدَ الشَّرْعُ بِهِ فِي الْجُمْلَةِ حَتَّى جَازَانُ يَكْتَفِيَ بِهِ فَجَازَ أَنْ يَضُمَّ إِلَيْهِ وَلِهَدَالَمْ يَشْرُعُ فِي التَّعْزِيْرِ بِالتُهُمَةِ قَبْلَ ثُبُوتِهِ كَمَا شُرِعَ فِي الْحَدِلانَّهُ مِنَ التَّعْزِيرِ
ترجمہ اور اگر امام یہ مناسب سمجھے کہ مجرم کو مار کے ساتھ جیل کی بھی سزادے تو اسے اس کا بھی حق ہے۔ کیونکہ قید خانہ میں ڈال دینا تعزیر کے مناسب ہے اور کسی حد تک شریعت میں یہ ثابت بھی ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ جب صرف قید کی سزا دینا بھی جائز ہے تو اسے دوسرے کے ساتھ ملانا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اسی لئے تعزیر کی صورت میں تہمت ثابت ہونے سے پہلے میں قید میں ڈالنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ حد کی صورت میں جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ تعزیر میں سے ہے (یعنی اگر کسی شخص پر کسی حد کی گواہی دی گئی ۔ مثلاً زنا یا شراب خوری کے۔ تو اس کے ثابت ہونے سے پہلے اسے قید میں رکھا۔ جائے۔ پھر جب ثابت ہو جائے تو اسے سزادی جائے)۔ تشریح قَالَ وَإِنْ رَأَى الْإِمَامُ أَنْ يَضُمَّ إِلَى الضَّرْبِ فِي التَّعْزِيرِ الْحَبْسَ فَعَلَ الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Chapter of hadd for false accusation. The maximum of ta'zir is thirty-nine lashes and the minimum is three lashes. But Abu Yusuf said the maximum is seventy-five lashes. The original [proof] in this chapter is the saying of the Prophet: 'Whoever reaches a hadd in other than a hadd, he is transgressing the moderate path.' This was narrated by Bayhaqi and Muhammad narrated it as mursal. Since ta'zir cannot reach the extent of a hadd, Abu Hanifa looked at the lowest amount of a hadd which is the hadd of a slave in qadhf, so he took that amount for ta'zir, which is forty lashes, and because ta'zir is less than hadd, he reduced one lash. Abu Yusuf considered the lowest hadd of a free person, i.e., eighty lashes, because freedom is the original state. Then there is a narration that he reduced one lash to seventy-nine. This is the view of Zufar, which is also the qiyas. But another narration in the book is that five lashes are reduced, because it is narrated from Ali. Thus they followed him. Then in the book, the minimum of ta'zir is mentioned as three lashes, because less than that, one or two lashes, do not achieve the purpose of deterrence. Our scholars of Transoxiana stated that the minimum of ta'zir is dependent on the Imam's discretion. That is, according to his opinion, whatever amount achieves deterrence, he may carry it out, because deterrence varies with different people. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he determined the amount based on the magnitude of the crime. And from him it is also narrated that each type of crime should be related to its category. So if someone touches or kisses a non-mahram woman, it is brought near the hadd of zina; and if someone slanders with other than zina, i.e., with words of fisq, then it is brought near the hadd of qadhf. It should be known that in a hadith it states: 'Do not beat more than ten lashes except in the limits of Allah.' Narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. But Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i and others said that it is permissible to beat more than ten lashes, because the Companions gave more than that, and it is also established from Ali and Umar. If their action opposed the hadith, the Companions would have denied it. Commentary: 'And ta'zir is seventy-five lashes' and the original in it is his saying, peace be upon him, etc. The meaning is clear from the translation. Along with ta'zir, what ruling... He said: If the Imam sees that he should add imprisonment to lashing in ta'zir, he may do so, because imprisonment is suitable as ta'zir and it has been legislated in the Shari'ah in general, to the extent that it is permissible to suffice with it, so it is permissible to add it. And thus it is not legislated in ta'zir for a suspicion before its proof, as it is legislated in hadd, because it is from the part of ta'zir. Translation: And if the Imam deems it appropriate to also give imprisonment along with lashing, he has the right, because imprisoning is suitable for ta'zir and it is proven in Shari'ah to some extent. So when it is permissible to give only imprisonment, then combining it [with lashing] is also permissible. Therefore, in ta'zir, imprisoning before the accusation is proven is not permissible, as it is permissible in hadd, because it is from the part of ta'zir (i.e., if someone is testified for a hadd, e.g., zina or drinking, then before its proof, he may be imprisoned. Then when it is proven, punishment is given). Commentary: He said: And if the Imam sees to add imprisonment to lashing in ta'zir, he may do so. The meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the hadd of false accusation (qadhf) but focuses on ta'zir (discretionary punishment). It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the maximum number of lashes in ta'zir. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the maximum is thirty-nine lashes, reasoning that ta'zir must be less than the minimum hadd, which for a slave in qadhf is forty lashes, so one lash is reduced. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the minimum hadd for a free person is eighty lashes, so ta'zir may go up to seventy-nine lashes. Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar have differing reductions. The text also discusses the minimum ta'zir lash (three) and the reliance on the imam's discretion. A hadith from Bukhari and Muslim limits beating to ten lashes except in hudud, but the Hanafi school permits exceeding ten based on the practice of the Companions. The second part of the passage discusses the permissibility of combining imprisonment with lashing in ta'zir. The imam may use imprisonment alone or add it to lashing, as it serves the purpose of deterrence. However, imprisonment before the crime is proven (as in hadd cases) is not allowed in ta'zir, whereas in hadd it is permissible to detain the accused before proof.

Key Terms
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for crimes that do not have a fixed hadd or for which the hadd is not fully established.
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Shari'ah for specific crimes (e.g., zina, qadhf, theft).
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) against a chaste person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadd does Imam Abu Hanifa use as the benchmark for the maximum ta'zir lashes?
A) The hadd for zina (100 lashes)
B) The hadd for qadhf for a free person (80 lashes)
C) The hadd for qadhf for a slave (40 lashes)
D) The hadd for theft (amputation)

Key Takeaway
Ta'zir lashes must be less than the minimum hadd; Abu Hanifa sets the maximum at 39 based on the slave's qadhf hadd of 40.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Order of Severity of Beating in Ta'zir and Hudud
Ranking of punishment severity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of severity of beating among ta'zir and the hudud according to the Hanafi school, and explain the reasoning based on reduced count and proof strength.

Core Idea
Ta'zir lashes are hardest, then zina, then drinking, then qadhf; severity compensates for reduced count.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a distinctly Hanafi ranking of punishments by the quality of beating. While ta'zir has fewer lashes, each lash is struck harder to maintain deterrence. Among the hudud, the severity follows the strength of the proof: Quran (zina), then companion consensus (drinking), then a less certain crime (qadhf). Understanding this ranking is key to applying discretionary punishments correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ranking order
From the text, list the four punishments in descending order of beating severity: ta'zir, then hadd al-zina, then hadd al-shurb, then hadd al-qadhf.
Ta'zir is not a hadd but is more severe in quality.
2
Understand the compensation principle
Note that ta'zir has a reduced number of lashes compared to hudud, so the quality (force) is increased to achieve deterrence. This principle is unique to Hanafi fiqh.
The qadi has discretion in number but not in quality.
3
Analyze proof strength for each hadd
For each hadd, note the strength of its proof: zina (Quran), shurb (ijma of Companions), qadhf (probable cause). Stronger proof leads to more severe beating in quality.
Qadhf already includes rejection of testimony, so no need for severe beating.

سزا میں سختی کی ترتیب
قَالَ وَأَشَدُّ الضَّرْبِ التَّعْزِيرُ لأَنَّهُ جَرَى التَّخْفِيفُ فِيهِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْعَدَدِ فَلَا يُخَفَّفُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْوَصْفِ كَيْلًا يُؤدِّيَ إِلَى فَوَاتِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَلِهَدَالَمْ يُخَفَّفْ مِنْ حَيْثُ التَّفْرِيقِ عَلَى الْأَعْضَاءِ
ترجمہ کہا سخت ترین مار تعزیر ہے (تعزیر کرتے وقت سختی سے کوڑے لگائے جائیں۔ کیونکہ اس میں ایک بار کوڑوں کی مقدار کے اعتبار سے نرمی کر دی گئی ہے تو دوبارہ وصف کے اعتبار سے نرمی نہیں کی جائے گی۔ تاکہ اصل مقصود ( ایز اور سانی اور تنبیہ ) فوت نہ ہو جائے۔ اس لئے متفرق اعضاء پر مارنے کی رعایت بھی نہ ہوگی۔
تشریح قَالَ وَأَشَدُّ الضَّرْبِ التعزير لأنَّهُ جَرَى التَّخْفِيفَ فِيهِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْعَدَدِ فَلَا يُخَفَّفُ الخ تعزیر مین چونکہ عدد کے اعتبار سے تخفیف آگئی ہے لہذا تعزیر کے وصف (یعنی شدید یا حفیف ضرب) میں تخفیف نہ کریں گے کہ اس سے مقصد فوت ہو جاتا ہے عدد کے اعتبار سے . تعزیر میں قاضی کی رائے کو دخل ہے لیکن تعزیر کے وصف میں قاضی کو دخل نہیں ہے۔
حد زنا میں کس قدرسختی ہو
قَالَ ثُمَّ حَدُّ الزِّنَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ ثَابِتٌ بِالْكِتَابِ وَحَدَّ الشَّرْبِ ثَبَتَ بِقَوْلِ الصَّحَابَةِ وَلِأَنَّهُ أَعْظَمُ جِنَايَةً حَتَّى شُرِعَ فِيهِ الرَّجمُ ثُمَّ حَدُّ الشُّرْبِ لَانَّ سَبَبَهُ مُتَيَقِنْ بِهِ ثُمَّ حَدُّ الْقَذَفِ لِاَنَّ سَبَبَهُ مُحْتَمَلْ لِاحْتِمَالِ كَوْنِهِ صَادِقًا وَلَانَّهُ جَرَى فِيهِ التَّعْلِيظُ مِنْ حَيْثُ رَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ فَلَا يُغَلَظُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْوَصْفِ
ترجمہ کہا، تعزیر کے بعد زنا کی حد میں سختی کا لحاظ ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا ثبوت قرآن مجید سے ہوتا ہے اور شراب خوری کی حد صحابہ کرام کے قول (اجماع) سے ہوئی ہے اور اس لئے بھی کہ حد زنا کا جرم بہت بڑا ہے یہاں تک کہ اس میں سنگسار کرنے کا بھی حکم دیا گیا ہے۔ پھر زنا کی جد کے بعد شراب پینے کی حد سخت ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس حد کا سبب یعنی شراب پینا یقینی سبب ہے۔ اس کے بعد تہمت کی حد ہے کیونکہ اس کے سبب ( تہمت لگانے) میں احتمال ہوتا ہے۔ کہ شاید یہ تہمت لگانے والا سچا ہو اور دوسری بات یہ بھی ہے کہ اس حد کے لگ جانے کے بعد جسے لگائی گئی ہے اس کی گواہی آئندہ بھی مردود ہو جانے کے اعتبار سے اس میں پہلے ہی سختی کر دی گئی ہے۔ اسی لئے اب وصف یعنی مار میں سختی نہیں کی جائے گی۔
تشریح قَالَ ثُمَّ حَدُّ الزِّنَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ ثَابِتٌ بِالْكِتَابِ وَحَدَّ الشَّرْبِ ثَبَتَ بِقَوْلِ الصَّحَابَةِ ... الخ وصف کے اعتبار سے سزاؤں کے بارے میں بتانا مقصود ہے کہ جس سزا کی دلیل پختہ یعنی دلیل جتنی زیادہ مضبوط ہے اس کے وصف میں کتب کریں گے اور پھر جس میں دلیل اتنی زیادہ مضبوط نہیں جیسے حدز نا کہ قرآن سے ثابت ہے اور اس میں سنگسار بھی کیا جاتا ہے پھر اس کے بعد حد شرب ہے کہ وہ صحابہ کرام رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین کے اجماع سے ثابت ہے اور یہ یقینی جرم ہے، پھر حد قذف ہے کہ تہمت لگانے والے کے بارے میں احتمال ہے کہ سچا ہو یا جھوٹا ہو لہذا اس اعتبار سے
Arrangement of severity in punishment. He said: The most severe beating is ta'zir, because leniency has been applied to it in terms of number, so it should not be made lenient in terms of quality, lest the intended purpose be lost. And thus it is not made lenient in terms of distribution over the limbs. Translation: He said: The most severe beating is ta'zir (i.e., during ta'zir, lashes should be given severely). Because once leniency has been applied in the count, leniency should not be applied in the quality, so that the original purpose (deterrence and discipline) is not lost. Therefore, the consideration of distributing over the limbs will not be observed. Commentary: He said: The most severe beating is ta'zir, because leniency has occurred in it in terms of number, so we will not make lenient its quality (i.e., severity or lightness of beating), because the purpose would be lost due to the number. In ta'zir, the qadi's opinion has play in the number, but in the quality of ta'zir, the qadi has no discretion. How much severity in the hadd of zina? He said: Then the hadd of zina [is severe] because it is established by the Book, and the hadd of drinking is established by the saying of the Companions (ijma), and because it is a greater crime, so much so that stoning is prescribed in it. Then the hadd of drinking [is next] because its cause is certain. Then the hadd of qadhf [is next] because its cause is probable, due to the possibility that the accuser may be truthful, and also because strictness has already been applied in it in terms of rejecting testimony, so it is not made strict in terms of quality. Translation: He said: After ta'zir, the hadd of zina is observed in severity because its proof is from the Quran, and the hadd of drinking is from the consensus of the Companions, and also because the crime of zina is very great, to the extent that stoning is prescribed in it. Then after the hadd of zina, the hadd of drinking is more severe, because its cause (drinking) is certain. Then comes the hadd of qadhf, because its cause is probable, as the accuser may be truthful, and also because once this hadd is applied, the person accused has his testimony rejected for the future, so strictness has already been applied in that aspect; therefore, no further strictness in the quality of beating is applied. Commentary: He said: Then the hadd of zina because it is established by the Book... The purpose is to explain regarding the quality of punishments: whichever punishment has a stronger proof, we will be strict in its quality, and then whichever has a less strong proof, like the hadd of zina is proven by the Quran and includes stoning, then after it the hadd of drinking which is proven by the consensus of the Companions and is a certain crime, then the hadd of qadhf because regarding the accuser there is probability that he may be truthful or false, so from this aspect...
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage discusses the relative severity of different punishments. It first states that ta'zir lashes are the most severe in terms of quality (force) because the number of lashes is already less than hudud. To compensate and ensure deterrence, the lashes are struck hard, even distributed over the limbs without the care given in hudud. Then it ranks the hudud: the hadd of zina is most severe among hudud because it is proven by the Quran and involves stoning; second is the hadd of drinking (shurb) because it is proven by ijma of the Companions and the cause (drinking) is certain; third is the hadd of qadhf because it is proven by a less certain cause (the accusation may be true) and the hadd itself already carries stigma (rejection of testimony). The passage emphasizes that the severity in quality is inversely related to the strength of the proof and the number: when the number is reduced (as in ta'zir), the quality is increased to maintain deterrence.

Key Terms
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment; the most severe in quality of beating.
حد الزنا (hadd al-zina): Fixed punishment for unlawful sexual intercourse; the most severe hadd in quality.
حد الشرب (hadd al-shurb): Fixed punishment for drinking alcohol; proven by companion consensus.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): Fixed punishment for false accusation of zina; least severe among the hudud in quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which punishment has the most severe beating in terms of quality?
A) Hadd of zina
B) Hadd of qadhf
C) Hadd of drinking
D) Ta'zir

Key Takeaway
Ta'zir lashes are struck hardest; among hudud, the severity of beating follows the strength of the proof, with zina being most severe and qadhf least.

Order of Severity in Hadd and Ta'zir Punishments
Explains the hierarchy of severity in corporal punishments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of severity in corporal punishments according to the Hanafi school and explain the ta'lil for each ranking.

Core Idea
Ta'zir beating is most severe because its number is lenient; hadd ranks follow textual certainty and crime severity.

This passage from Al-Hidayah sets out the Hanafi ranking of corporal punishments by severity of the beating. The author begins with ta'zir as the most severe, then orders the hadd punishments for zina, drinking, and qadhf. Each rank is justified by a blend of textual source and legal reasoning, balancing the need for deterrence with the limits set by revelation.

Guided Path
1
List the punishments in order
Identify the four punishments mentioned: ta'zir, hadd of zina, hadd of shurb, hadd of qadhf. Arrange them from most severe to least severe as per the passage.
Ta'zir is the most severe beating, then zina, then shurb, then qadhf.
2
Analyze the reason for ta'zir's severity
Understand why ta'zir is most severe: the number of lashes is lenient (limited), so to achieve the goal of reform and deterrence, the quality of each lash must be increased. Also, it is not distributed over the limbs as in hadd.
Uses the principle of compensation: leniency in number is balanced by severity in description.
3
Examine the basis for each hadd rank
For zina: text from the Qur'an and the presence of stoning make it a greater crime. For shurb: established by qawl al-sahaba (Companions' consensus) and its cause is certain. For qadhf: its cause is probable (accuser may be truthful) and it already has added severity in testimony rejection.
Zina is higher because of stronger textual evidence and graver nature.
4
Apply the logic to a hypothetical
Consider why qadhf is least severe: the possibility that the accuser is truthful reduces certainty, and the extra punishment of testimony rejection compensates for leniency in beating.
This shows the Hanafi method of balancing multiple legal consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَأَشَدُّ الضَّرْبِ التَّعْزِيرُ لأَنَّهُ جَرَى التَّخْفِيفُ فِيهِ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْعَدَدِ فَلَا يُخَفَّفُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْوَصْفِ كَيْلًا يُؤدِّيَ إِلَى فَوَاتِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَلِهَدَالَمْ يُخَفَّفْ مِنْ حَيْثُ التَّفْرِيقِ عَلَى الْأَعْضَاءِ
قَالَ ثُمَّ حَدُّ الزِّنَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ ثَابِتٌ بِالْكِتَابِ وَحَدَّ الشَّرْبِ ثَبَتَ بِقَوْلِ الصَّحَابَةِ وَلِأَنَّهُ أَعْظَمُ جِنَايَةً حَتَّى شُرِعَ فِيهِ الرَّجمُ ثُمَّ حَدُّ الشُّرْبِ لَانَّ سَبَبَهُ مُتَيَقِنْ بِهِ ثُمَّ حَدُّ الْقَذَفِ لِاَنَّ سَبَبَهُ مُحْتَمَلْ لِاحْتِمَالِ كَوْنِهِ صَادِقًا وَلَانَّهُ جَرَى فِيهِ التَّعْلِيظُ مِنْ حَيْثُ رَةِ الشَّهَادَةِ فَلَا يُغَلَظُ مِنْ حَيْثُ الْوَصْفِ
He said: The most severe beating is ta'zir, because leniency was introduced in it regarding the number, so it is not made lenient in description, lest the intended purpose be lost. And for this reason, it is not made lenient in terms of distribution over the limbs. He said: Then the hadd of zina (is severest) because it is established by the Book, and the hadd of drinking (shurb) was established by the saying of the Companions, and because it is a greater crime, even stoning was legislated in it. Then the hadd of shurb (is next) because its cause is certain. Then the hadd of qadhf, because its cause is probable, due to the possibility that he is truthful, and because severity was already applied in it regarding the rejection of testimony, so it is not made severe in description.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage details the hierarchy of severity in corporal punishments. The author first states that ta'zir (discretionary punishment) involves the most severe beating because its number of lashes is lenient (maximum 39 for free person, 19 for slave) so to achieve reform and deterrence, the quality of each lash must be severe; also the beating is not distributed over different limbs as is done in hadd punishments. Following ta'zir, the hadd for zina is next in severity as its evidence comes from the Qur'an and it is a major crime (even involving stoning for married offenders). Then the hadd for drinking alcohol is next because its cause (consumption of wine) is certain. Finally, the hadd for qadhf (false accusation) is least severe because its cause may be truthful, and because qadhf already carries the additional penalty of the accuser's testimony being permanently rejected.

Key Terms
التَّعْزِيرُ (al-ta'zīr): Discretionary corporal punishment for crimes not subject to hadd or kaffarah, with number of lashes varying by judge's discretion.
الْقَذَفِ (al-qadhf): False accusation of adultery or fornication; a hadd crime punishable with 80 lashes.
التَّعْلِيظُ (al-ta‘līẓ): Severity or strictness; here refers to the additional penalty of rejecting the accuser's testimony in qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is ta'zir beating described as the most severe in quality?
A) Because it has a fixed number of lashes.
B) Because the number is lenient, so severity in description is needed to achieve the goal.
C) Because it is for crimes against God.
D) Because it involves distribution over limbs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hierarchy ranks ta'zir beating as most severe in quality, followed by hadd of zina, then shurb, then qadhf, based on the balance between textual authority and criminal certainty.

Ruling on Death from Hadd or Ta'zir by the Imam
States the Hanafi ruling that blood is hira when death occurs from judicial punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that no blood money is due when a person dies from judicial punishment and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
When the imam executes Allah's right by command, the death is attributed to Allah, not the imam.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: if a person dies from hadd or ta'zir administered by the imam, is blood money (diyah) due? The Hanafi school holds that the blood is hira (wasted)—no compensation is due—while Imam al-Shafi'i argues that diyah is obligatory from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). Understanding the reasoning behind each position deepens your grasp of liability (damān) in Islamic criminal law and the legal effect of command.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What exactly does the Hanafi school hold regarding blood money when a person dies from judicial punishment?
The position is that the blood is hira—no diyah or qisas.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Which school objects and on what grounds? Imam al-Shafi'i holds that diyah is due from the public treasury.
The opposing school is the Shafi'i madhhab.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is the Shafi'i dalil? They argue that the death is an error (khatā') in ta'zir, and since the benefit of punishment accrues to all Muslims, compensation should come from public wealth.
The Shafi'i view considers the imam's action as a permitted act gone wrong.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut this? They argue that the imam executes Allah's right by command, so the death is attributed directly to Allah, not to the imam, thus no damān.
The Hanafi response emphasises the legal effect of command (amr) in removing liability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in rulings? Hanafi: no financial liability; Shafi'i: diyah from bayt al-mal.
This affects whether the victim's family receives compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ جَدَّهُ الْإِمَامُ اَوْ عَزَّرَهُ فَمَاتَ فَدَمُهُ هَدْرلَانَّهُ فَعَلَ مَا فَعَلَ بِأَمْرِ الشَّرْعِ وَفِعْلُ الْمَامُورِ لَا يَتَقَيَّدُ بِشَرْطِ السَّلَامَةِ كَالْفَصَّادِ وَالْبَزَّاغِ بِخِلَافِ الزَّوْجِ إِذَا عَزَرَ زَوْجَتَهُ لِأَنَّهُ مُطلَقَ فِيهِ وَالْإِطْلَاقَاتُ يَتَقَيَّدُ بِشَرْطِ السَّلَامَةِ كَالْمُرُورِ فِى الطَّرِيقِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ تَجِبُ الدِّيَةُ فِي بَيْتِ الْمَالِ لأَنَّ الْإِتْلَاقَ خَطَافِيهِ إِذِ التَّعْزِيْرُ لِلتَّادِيْبِ غَيْرَ انَّهُ تَجِبُ الدِّيَهُ فِي بَيْتِ الْمَالِ لِاَنَّ نَفَعَ عَمَلِهِ يَرْجِعُ إِلى عَامَةِ الْمُسْلِمِيْنَ فَيَكُونُ الْعَزْمُ فِي مَالِهِمْ قُلْنَا لَمَّا استوقى حَقَّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بِأَمْرِهِ صَارَكَانَ اللهُ أَمَاتَهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ وَاسِطَةٍ فَلَايَجِبُ الضَّمَانُ
And whoever the imam imposes hadd upon or ta'zir upon and he dies, then his blood is wasted, because he did what he did by command of the Shari'ah, and the action of the commanded one is not conditioned upon safety, like the phlebotomist and the cupper. Contrary to the husband when he disciplines his wife, because he has freedom in it, and permissions are conditioned upon safety, like passing on the road. Al-Shafi'i said: The blood money is obligatory in the treasury, because the destruction is an error in it, since ta'zir is for discipline; but the blood money is obligatory in the treasury because the benefit of his action returns to the general body of Muslims, so the compensation is from their wealth. We said: When he executed the right of Allah Almighty by His command, it became as if Allah caused his death without an intermediary, so compensation is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents a inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position: If a person dies from hadd (fixed punishment) or ta'zir (discretionary punishment) administered by the imam (ruler or judge), the blood is hira (wasted) — no diyah (blood money) or qisas (retaliation) is due. The reasoning: the imam acts by the command of the Shari'ah, and when someone is commanded to perform an act, they are not responsible for unintended harm occurring during that act, just as a phlebotomist or cupper is not liable if the patient dies. This is contrasted with a husband disciplining his wife: the husband is merely permitted (not commanded), so his permission is conditioned on safety; therefore, if harm occurs, he is liable. Imam al-Shafi'i argued that diyah is due from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) because the harm is an error (khatā') and ta'zir's purpose is discipline, and the benefit accrues to all Muslims. The Hanafi response: The imam executes Allah's right by His command, so the death is attributed to Allah directly, not to the imam; hence no damān (civil liability).

Key Terms
هَدَرٌ (hadar): Legally wasted, without claim for blood money or retaliation.
بَيْتِ الْمَالِ (bayt al-māl): The public treasury of the Islamic state, used for the welfare of Muslims.
خَطَأٌ (khaṭa’): Error or mistake; here Shafi'i argues that the death is an unintended error in ta'zir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school hold that no blood money is due when a person dies from hadd by the imam?
A) Because the imam is above the law.
B) Because the imam acted by command of Shari'ah, and the commanded one is not liable for unintended harm.
C) Because the victim was a criminal and deserves it.
D) Because the blood money would come from the treasury anyway.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the imam's execution of a valid hadd or ta'zir is an act of Allah's command, so any resulting death carries no financial liability.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
