8 min
Ruling When Imām's Execution of Hadd or Taʿzīr Causes Death
States Hanafi ruling with qiyas and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that no liability arises when the imam's execution of hadd or ta'zir causes death, explain the qiyas proof, and contrast it with the Shafi'i position that blood money is due from the public treasury.

Core Idea
The imam acts by Shari'ah command; his action is like Allah's own, so no liability for death.

When a judge or imam carries out a prescribed punishment (hadd) or a discretionary punishment (ta'zir), and the recipient dies, who is liable? The Hanafi school gives a clear answer: the blood is wasted (hadar) – no diyah, no qisas. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that ruling, the analogy that supports it, and the respectful disagreement of Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that blood money is paid from the public treasury.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the blood of the person who dies during hadd/ta'zir execution by the imam is hadar (wasted). No compensation is due.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the death is a mistake (khata') and blood money is due from the public treasury (bayt al-mal).
The Shafi'i view is based on the purpose of ta'zir (discipline) and public benefit.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i argument: ta'zir is for discipline, not killing; thus death is unintentional. Since the benefit of punishment goes to the community, liability should fall on the community treasury.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the imam executes the right of Allah by divine command. It is as if Allah caused the death without intermediary. Therefore, no liability.
This is supported by the analogy of the phlebotomist (faṣṣād) and cupper (bazzāgh) who act by permission and are not liable if death occurs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi – no compensation; Shafi'i – diyah from bayt al-mal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ حَدَّهُ الْإِمَامُ أَوْ عَزَّرَهُ فَمَاتَ فَدَمُهُ هَدَرٌ لِأَنَّهُ فَعَلَ مَا فَعَلَ بِأَمْرِ الشَّرْعِ وَفِعْلُ الْمَأْمُورِ لَا يَتَقَيَّدُ بِشَرْطِ السَّلَامَةِ كَالْفَصَّادِ وَالْبَزَّاغِ بِخِلَافِ الزَّوْجِ إِذَا عَزَّرَ زَوْجَتَهُ لِأَنَّهُ مُطْلَقٌ فِيهِ وَالْإِطْلَاقَاتُ تَتَقَيَّدُ بِشَرْطِ السَّلَامَةِ كَالْمُرُورِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ تَجِبُ الدِّيَةُ فِي بَيْتِ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّ الْإِتْلَافَ خَطَأٌ فِيهِ إِذِ التَّعْزِيرُ لِلتَّأْدِيبِ غَيْرَ أَنَّهُ تَجِبُ الدِّيَةُ فِي بَيْتِ الْمَالِ لِأَنَّ نَفْعَ عَمَلِهِ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى عَامَّةِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ فَيَكُونُ الضَّمَانُ فِي مَالِهِمْ قُلْنَا لَمَّا اسْتَوْفَى حَقَّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى بِأَمْرِهِ صَارَ كَأَنَّ اللَّهَ أَمَاتَهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ وَاسِطَةٍ فَلَا يَجِبُ الضَّمَانُ.
And whoever the imam carries out hadd or ta'zir upon and he dies, his blood is wasted because he did what he did by the command of the Shari'ah, and the action of the one commanded is not conditioned by the condition of safety, like the phlebotomist and the cupper. Contrary to the husband when he disciplines his wife, because he is given absolute discretion in it, and absolute permissions are conditioned by the condition of safety, like passing on the road. And al-Shafi'i said: The blood money is obligatory from the public treasury because the destruction is a mistake in it, since ta'zir is for discipline; but the blood money is obligatory from the public treasury because the benefit of his action returns to the general Muslims, so the liability is on their wealth. We said: When he executed the right of Allah Most High by His command, it becomes as if Allah caused his death without any intermediary, so liability is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses the liability of the imām (or judge) when a punishment he carries out results in the death of the condemned person. The ruling is clear: the blood of the deceased is hadar (wasted), meaning no qisas or diyah is due from the imām. The reasoning is that the imām acts by the command of the Sharīʿah—he is obligated to execute the prescribed penalty. Therefore, his action is analogous to that of a phlebotomist (faṣṣād) or a cupper (bazzāgh), who perform medical procedures by the patient's consent; if the patient dies, they are not liable because their action was permitted and not intended to cause death. Similarly, the imām is not liable because the mandate of the Sharīʿah is not conditioned on the safety of the recipient. The exception is the case of a husband disciplining his wife. This is because the husband is not obliged to administer discipline—he is merely permitted to do so. Permissive commands are conditional on safety, like the permission to walk on a public road: if you cause harm while exercising that permission, you are liable. Therefore, if a husband kills his wife while disciplining her, he is liable. Imam al-Shāfiʿī opposed this view. He argued that the death is an unintended mistake (khaṭaʾ) because the punishment is meant to discipline, not to kill. Since the benefit of the punishment returns to the Muslim community, the diyah should be paid from the public treasury (bayt al-māl). The Ḥanafī response is that the imām, when executing the ḥadd, is merely an instrument of divine command. It is as if Allah Himself took the life of the criminal without an intermediary. Hence, no liability falls on the imām or the public treasury.

Key Terms
هدر (hadar): Blood that is not subject to compensation (diyah or qisas).
تعزير (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment less than hadd for offenses lacking fixed punishment or when conditions for hadd are not met.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if the imam's execution of hadd or ta'zir causes the death of the recipient?
A) The imam must pay blood money from his own wealth.
B) The blood money is paid from the public treasury.
C) The blood is wasted (hadar) and no compensation is due.
D) The imam is subject to qisas.

Key Takeaway
The imam is not liable for death resulting from executing Shari'ah punishments because his action is attributed to Allah's command.

The Linguistic and Legal Definition of Sariqah (Theft)
Defines sariqah linguistically and explains additional Shar'ī conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sariqah linguistically and distinguish between its linguistic and Shar'ī applications, explaining why additional conditions are needed for the ḥadd penalty.

Core Idea
Sariqah linguistically means secret taking, but Sharīʿah adds conditions for the ḥadd penalty.

This passage opens the chapter on theft (kitāb al-sariqah) by grounding the term in its linguistic root. The author shows that while the language is broad, the Sharīʿah narrows it for punishment. Understanding this foundation is key to grasping the later conditions like hirz and niṣāb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
The text defines sariqah as taking something from another in a concealed and secret manner. Note the root word and its Qur'ānic usage for eavesdropping (istirāq al-samʿ).
The linguistic meaning is broad.
2
Understand the Shar'ī addition
The Shari'ah adds attributes (conditions) beyond the linguistic meaning for the ḥadd penalty. These will be explained later in the text.
The linguistic definition alone does not trigger ḥadd.
3
Analyze the degree of linguistic observance
The linguistic meaning may apply fully (both initially and finally) or partially (initially only). Example: secretly breaching a wall but then openly taking the money – the initial secrecy makes it linguistically sariqah.
The open taking may affect whether ḥadd applies.
4
Distinguish major vs. minor theft
Major theft (highway robbery) involves stealing from the imam's eye (his surveillance); minor theft involves stealing from the owner's eye. This relates to the condition of concealment for ḥadd.
The 'eye' refers to vigilant supervision.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السَّرْقَةُ فِي اللُّغَةِ أَخْذُ الشَّيْءِ مِنَ الْغَيْرِ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الْخُفْيَةِ وَالْإِسْتِسْرَارِ وَمِنْهُ إِسْتِرَاقُ السَّمْعِ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى إِلَّا مَنِ اسْتَرَقَ السَّمْعَ وَقَدْ زِيدَتْ عَلَيْهِ أَوْصَافٌ فِي الشَّرِيعَةِ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِيكَ بَيَانُهُ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى وَالْمَعْنَى اللُّغَوِيُّ مُرَاعًى فِيهَا ابْتِدَاءً وَانْتِهَاءً أَوِ ابْتِدَاءً لَا غَيْرُ كَمَا إِذَا نُقِبَ الْجِدَارُ عَلَى الْإِسْتِسْرَارِ وَأُخِذَ الْمَالُ مِنَ الْمَالِكِ مُكَابَرَةً عَلَى الْجِهَارِ وَفِي الْكُبْرَى أَعْنِي قَطْعَ الطَّرِيقِ مُسَارَقَةُ عَيْنِ الْإِمَامِ لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ الْمُتَصَدِّي لِحِفْظِ الطَّرِيقِ بِأَعْوَانِهِ وَفِي الصُّغْرَى مُسَارَقَةُ عَيْنِ الْمَالِكِ وَمَنْ يَقُومُ مَقَامَهُ
Sariqah linguistically is taking something from another in a concealed and secret manner. From this is istiraq al-sam' (eavesdropping). Allah Most High said: 'Except one who snatches a hearing.' And additional attributes have been added to it in the Shari'ah, as will come to you its explanation if Allah wills. And the linguistic meaning is considered in it both initially and finally, or initially only, as when a wall is breached secretly and the wealth is taken from the owner forcibly and openly. And in major theft, I mean highway robbery, it is stealing the eye of the imam because he is the one who undertakes the protection of the road with his assistants. And in minor theft, it is stealing the eye of the owner or whoever stands in his place.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage introduces the subject of Kitāb al-Sariqah by first defining the term linguistically and then clarifying its Sharʿī scope. Linguistically, sariqah means taking something from another secretly and concealed. This includes the Qurʾānic usage of istirāq al-samʿ (eavesdropping) by devils. In the Sharīʿah, additional attributes are added for the ḥadd penalty to apply. The author notes that the linguistic meaning may be observed either at the beginning and end of the act, or only at the beginning. For example, if someone secretly breaches a wall and then openly takes money from the owner, the initial secret act makes it sariqah linguistically, but the open taking may affect whether it qualifies for ḥadd. The passage then distinguishes between major theft (kubrā), which is highway robbery (qaṭʿ al-ṭarīq), and minor theft (ṣughrā). In highway robbery, the thief steals the 'eye' of the imām—meaning he avoids the imām's surveillance, since the imām is responsible for protecting roads. In normal theft, the thief steals the 'eye' of the owner or his representative (e.g., a trustee). This distinction helps determine when ḥadd becomes applicable, as the condition of concealment from the owner's vigilance is relevant.

Key Terms
سرقہ (sariqah): Linguistically: secret taking; in Shari'ah: taking property of value from a secure place without shubha above the nisab.
استراق السمع (istiraq al-sam'): Eavesdropping: stealing hearing secretly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the linguistic meaning of sariqah (theft) according to the text?
A) Taking property forcibly and openly.
B) Taking something from another in a concealed and secret manner.
C) Robbery on the highway.
D) Taking property from an owner without his knowledge.

Key Takeaway
The linguistic definition of sariqah is broad, but the Shar'ī definition narrows it by adding conditions for the ḥadd penalty to apply.

Minimum Nisab for Hadd al-Sariqah: Ten Dirhams or Equivalent
States Hanafi condition of ten dirhams for cutting the hand, with proof and disputes with Shafi'i and Malik.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for applying the hadd of cutting the hand, including the nisab of ten dirhams, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Core Idea
The hand is only cut if the stolen property equals ten dirhams – a substantial amount ensures deterrence.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi position on the minimum value (nisab) required for the hadd punishment of cutting the hand for theft. The author lays out the conditions and proofs, then contrasts the views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik. Understanding this dispute helps clarify why different schools reach different rulings on the same act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its conditions
Read the first part of the passage: the thief must be sane and adult, steal ten dirhams (or equivalent) from a secure place (hirz) without any shubha (ambiguity). Cutting becomes wajib.
The nisab is a condition (shart), not a pillar (rukn).
2
Locate the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The passage cites the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:38) and provides a rational argument: a small amount would not deter, and the theft of a small amount is not hidden, so the essential element of theft is missing.
The rational argument is a form of istihsan or istidlal.
3
Analyze the opposing schools' proof
The passage mentions Shafi'i (quarter dinar) and Maliki (three dirhams). Their proof is a hadith that the Prophet only cut for a shield worth three dirhams, and the least transmitted amount is three dirhams.
The Hanafi school does not accept this as limiting because they hold that the hadith is not explicit about the minimum.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi, theft below ten dirhams does not result in cutting; under Shafi'i, cutting applies at a quarter dinar (approx. 1.0 g gold); under Maliki, at three dirhams. This affects many cases.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each school has its own methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ إِذَا سَرَقَ الْعَاقِلُ الْبَالِغُ عَشْرَةَ دَرَاهِمَ أَوْ مَا يَبْلُغُ قِيمَتُهُ عَشْرَةَ دَرَاهِمَ مَضْرُوبَةً مِنْ حِرْزٍ لَا شُبُهَةَ فِيهِ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ الْقَطْعُ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ فَاقْطَعُوا أَيْدِيَهُمَا الْآيَةُ وَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ اعْتِبَارِ الْعَقْلِ وَالْبُلُوغِ لِأَنَّ الْجِنَايَةَ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ دُونَهُمَا وَالْقَطْعُ جَزَاءُ الْجِنَايَةِ وَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّقْدِيرِ بِالْمَالِ الْخَطِيرِ لِأَنَّ الرَّغَبَاتِ تَفْتُرُ فِي الْحَقِيرِ وَكَذَا أَخْذُهُ لَا يَخْفَى فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ رُكْنُهُ وَلَا حِكْمَةَ الزَّجْرِ لِأَنَّهَا فِيمَا يَغْلِبُ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ بِعَشْرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ مَذْهَبُنَا وَعِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ التَّقْدِيرُ بِرُبْعِ دِينَارٍ وَعِنْدَ مَالِكٍ بِثَلَاثَةِ دَرَاهِمَ لَهُمَا أَنَّ الْقَطْعَ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَا كَانَ إِلَّا فِي ثَمَنِ الْمِجَنِّ وَأَقَلُّ مَا نُقِلَ فِي تَقْدِيرِهِ ثَلَاثَةُ دَرَاهِمَ وَالْأَخْذُ بِالْأَقَلِّ وَهُوَ الْمُتَيَقَّنُ بِهِ
He said: And when the sane, adult person steals ten dirhams or what equals their value, coined [dirhams], from a secure place in which there is no doubt, cutting becomes obligatory upon him. The proof for it is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And the male thief and the female thief, cut off their hands.' And consideration of sanity and adulthood is necessary because the crime is not realized without them, and cutting is the penalty for the crime. And estimation with substantial wealth is necessary because desires weaken in trifling [wealth], and similarly its taking is not hidden, so its essential element is not realized, and there is no wisdom of deterrence because that is in what is common. And the estimation with ten dirhams is our madhhab. According to al-Shafi'i, the estimation is with a quarter dinar, and according to Malik, with three dirhams. Their proof is that cutting in the time of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was only in the price of a shield, and the least transmitted in its estimation is three dirhams, and one takes the least which is the certain.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage presents the Ḥanafī ruling on the minimum amount (niṣāb) for applying the ḥadd punishment of cutting the hand. According to Abū Ḥanīfa, the hand is cut only when the thief steals ten dirhams (or the value equivalent in goods) from a secure place (ḥirz) with no element of doubt (shubha). The conditions of sanity and puberty are also essential, as no criminal liability exists without them. The proof for the general obligation of cutting is the Qurʾānic verse: 'And the male thief and the female thief, cut off their hands' (al-Māʾidah 5:38). As for the specific amount, the Ḥanafī school relies on rational reasoning: cutting for a small amount would not serve as a deterrent because the culprit would not be sufficiently discouraged. Moreover, taking a small amount is not hidden (it goes unnoticed), so the element of secrecy is lacking. Hence, a substantial value is required for the ḥadd to apply. The text then mentions the views of Imām al-Shāfiʿī (quarter dinar) and Imām Mālik (three dirhams). Their proof derives from the Ḥadīth that the Prophet ﷺ only cut the hand for a shield worth three dirhams, and the least reported amount is three dirhams. The Ḥanafī school does not accept this as limiting the niṣāb; they maintain that the ten dirhams standard is established by the practice of the Companions and the need for a meaningful deterrent.

Key Terms
درهم (dirham): A silver coin used as standard for nisab; ten dirhams is the minimum value for hadd in Hanafi.
حرز (hirz): A secure place where property is kept and theft is prevented by normal means.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum nisab for cutting the hand in hadd al-sariqah?
A) Three dirhams
B) A quarter dinar
C) Ten dirhams
D) One dinar

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a nisab of ten dirhams for hadd al-sariqah, applying cutting only when the stolen property meets or exceeds this substantial value, to ensure effective deterrence.

Conditions for Hand Amputation and the Nisab Dispute
Ruling for qat' with conditions and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for the hadd of theft (qat') and explain the inter-madhhab dispute over the minimum value (nisab) of stolen property.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school requires ten dirhams of coined silver for amputation, a precaution to avert doubt.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author presents the ruling for hand amputation in theft, outlining strict conditions including sanity, adulthood, a minimum value of ten dirhams of coined silver, and secure storage (hirz). The core of the passage is a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik over the nisab. Understanding this dispute reveals the Hanafi principle of caution (ihtiyat) in hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its conditions
State the necessary conditions for qat': the thief must be sane and adult, the stolen property must reach ten dirhams of coined silver (or equivalent value), and it must be taken from a secure place (hirz) free of doubt (shubha).
2
Locate the primary evidence
The Quranic verse 5:38 ('Cut off their hands') establishes the penalty, while the hadith 'La qat'a illa fi dinar aw 'asharat darahim' specifies the minimum value.
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni thubut, but the Hanafi school relies on it.
3
Note the opposing schools' positions
Imam al-Shafi'i sets the nisab at a quarter of a dinar (approx. 3 dirhams) and Imam Malik at three dirhams. Both cite the hadith of the shield (mihann) valued at three dirhams.
4
Examine the opposing proof
The shield hadith is apparently specific but not explicit for nisab. Al-Shafi'i further argues that the dinar was worth 12 dirhams, so a quarter equals 3 dirhams.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school prioritizes the explicit hadith of dinar/ten dirhams. Taking the higher amount is precautionary to avoid doubt (shubha) and potential error in applying hadd. The shield hadith is not explicit for the nisab.
This reflects the principle 'al-hududu tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' (hudud are averted by doubts).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ إِذَا سَرَقَ الْعَاقِلُ الْبَالِغُ عَشْرَةَ دَرَاهِمَ أَوْ مَا يَبْلُغُ قِيمَتُهُ عَشْرَةَ دَرَاهِمَ مَضْرُوبَةٌ مِنْ حِرْزِ لَا شُبُهَةٌ فِيْهِ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ الْقَطْعُ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيهِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ فَاقْطَعُوا أَيْدِيَهُمَا الْآيَةُ وَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اِعْتِبَارِ الْعَقْلِ وَالْبُلُوغِ لِاَنَّ الْجِنَايَةَ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ دُونَهُمَا وَالْقَطْعُ جَزَاءُ الْعِنَايَةِ وَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّقْدِيرِ بِالْمَالِ الْخَطِيرِ لَانَّ الرَّغَبَاتِ تَفْتَرُّفِي الْحَقِيرِ وَ كَذَا أَخْدُهُ لَا يَخْفى فَلَا يَتَحَقَّقُ رُكْنُهُ وَلَا حِكْمَةَ الزَّجْرِلَانَّهَا فِيْمَا يَغْلِبُ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ بِعَشْرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ مَذْهَبْنَا وَ عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيِّ التَّقْدِيرُ بِرَبْعِ دِينَارٍ وَ عِنْدَ مَالِكٌ بِثَلَثَةِ دَرَاهِمَ لَهُمَا أَنَّ الْقَطْعَ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَا كَانَ إِلَّا فِى ثَمَنِ الْمَحَنِ وَأَقَلُّ مَانُقِلَ فِي تَقْدِيرِهِ ثَلَثَةُ دَرَاهِمَ وَالْاخْذُ بِالْاقَلَّ وَهُوَ الْمُتَيَقَّنُ بِهِ غَيْرَاَنَّ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَقُولُ كَانَتْ قِيمَةُ الدِّينَارٍ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ اِثْنَى عَشَرَ دِرْهَمَا وَالصَّلَقَةُ رُبُعُهَا وَلَنَا أَنَّ الْأَخْذَبِا لْأَكْثَرِ فِي هَذِهِ الْبَابِ أَوْلَى اِحْتِيَالًا لِدَرْءِ الْحَدِوَهَذَا لِأَنَّ فِي الْأَقَلَّ شُبُهَةَ عَدْمِ الْجِنَايَةِ وَهِيَ دَارِئَةٌ لِلْحَدِ وَ قَدْ تَأَيَّدَ ذَالِكَ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا قَطعَ إِلَّا فِي دِينَارٍ أَوْ عَشَرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ وَاسْمُ الدَّرَاهِمِ يُطْلَقُ عَلَى الْمَضْرُوبَةِ عُرُفًا فَهَذَايُبَيِّنُ لَكَ اِشْتِرَاطَ الْمَضْرُوبِ كَمَا قَالَ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَهُوَ ظَاهِرُ الرِّوَايَةِ وَهُوَ الْاصَحُ رِعَايَةً لِكَمَالِ الْجِنَايَةِ حَتَّى لَوْسَرَقَ عَشْرَةَ تِبْرًا قِيمَتُهَا أَنْقَصُ مِنْ عَشْرَةٍ مَضْرُوبَةٍ لَا يَجِبُ الْقَطْعُ وَالْمُعْتَبَرُوزْنُ سَبْعَةِ مَثَاقِيْلَ لِأَنَّهُ الْمُتَعَارَفُ فِي عَامَّةِ الْبَلَادِ وَقَوْلُهُ اَوْ مَايَبْلُغُ قِيمَتُهُ عَشْرَةَ دَرَاهِمَ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ غَيْرَ الدَّرَاهِمِ يُعْتَبَرُ قِيْمَتُهُ بِهَا وَإِنْ كَانَ ذَهَبًا وَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ حِرْزِ لَا شُبُهَةٌ فِيهِ لِاَنَّ الشُّبُهَةَ دَرِائَةٌ وَسَنُبَيَّنُهُ مِنْ بَعْدُ انْشَاءَ الله تَعَالَى
He said: When a sane, adult thief steals ten dirhams, or something whose value reaches ten coined dirhams, from a secure place (hirz) that has no doubt (shubha) about it, then cutting (his hand) becomes obligatory. The basis for this is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:38). Consideration of sanity and adulthood is necessary because a crime is not established without them, and amputation is the penalty for the crime. It is necessary to fix the threshold at valuable property because desires lose interest in insignificant things; likewise, taking it would not be hidden, so its pillar (rukn) is not established, nor would the wisdom of deterrence be achieved, because that is effective in cases that are prevalent. The threshold in our school is ten dirhams. According to al-Shafi'i, the threshold is a quarter of a dinar. According to Malik, it is three dirhams. Their evidence is that amputation during the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was only for the price of a shield (mihann), and the minimum reported in its estimation is three dirhams; taking the minimum is better because it is the certain amount. However, al-Shafi'i says that the value of a dinar during the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was twelve dirhams, so a quarter of it is three dirhams. Our evidence is that taking the greater (akthar) in this chapter is better as a precaution to avert the hadd penalty. This is because in the lesser amount there is a doubt of lack of crime, and doubt prevents the hadd. This is supported by his saying, peace be upon him: 'There is no cutting except in a dinar or ten dirhams.' The name 'dirhams' is customarily applied to coined ones. This shows you the condition of being coined, as stated in the book, and it is the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) and the most correct, out of consideration for the completeness of the crime. So much so that if he stole ten pure silver pieces (tibr) whose value is less than ten coined dirhams, cutting is not obligatory. The considered weight is seven mithqals because that is the customary weight in most lands. His statement 'or something whose value reaches ten dirhams' indicates that other than dirhams are assessed by their value, even if gold. A secure place without doubt is necessary because doubt averts the hadd, and we will explain this later, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage lays out the Hanafi ruling for when the hadd penalty of hand amputation is obligatory for theft. The thief must be sane and adult (ʿāqil bāligh). The stolen item must be of a minimum value: ten dirhams of coined silver, or the equivalent value in other goods. It must be taken from a secure place (hirz) free of any doubt (shubha) that could prevent the penalty. The primary evidence is the Qur'anic verse (5:38). The text then explains why sanity and adulthood are required: the crime is not fully realized without them, and the penalty is a punishment for a crime. Valuation is necessary because insignificant items do not motivate theft and are not taken secretly, so the element of secrecy (rukn of theft) is absent, and the deterrent purpose is not served. The Hanafi school sets the nisab at ten dirhams. This is contrasted with the positions of Imam al-Shafi'i (quarter dinar) and Imam Malik (three dirhams). Both opponents cite the hadith of the shield (mihann) valued at three dirhams. However, al-Shafi'i argues that a dinar was twelve dirhams so a quarter is three dirhams as well. The Hanafi response is that we take the higher amount (ten dirhams) as a precaution to avert the hadd penalty, because a lower amount introduces doubt (shubha) whether the crime is complete. This is supported by the hadith: 'La qat'a illa fi dinar aw 'asharat darahim.' The text also emphasizes that the dirhams must be coined (madrūba), i.e., minted as currency. This is the ruling of Zahir al-Riwayah and the most correct (asahh). If one steals uncoined silver (tibr) worth less than ten coined dirhams, no cutting. The standard weight is seven mithqals (approximately 3.15 grams per dirham? Actually 10 dirhams = 7 mithqals, so each dirham is 0.7 mithqal). The condition of hirz (secure place) is essential because any doubt (shubha) in the security or ownership prevents the hadd.

Key Terms
قطر (القطع) (qat' (al-qat')): Cutting off the hand as a hadd penalty for theft.
درہم (dirham): Silver coin, the standard of value for nisab in theft.
حرز (hirz): A secure place where property is kept.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt that prevents the application of hadd penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum value of stolen property required in the Hanafi school for the hadd of hand amputation?
A) Three dirhams.
B) A quarter dinar.
C) Ten dirhams of coined silver.
D) Seven mithqals of gold.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditions the hadd of theft on strict safeguards, especially a high nisab, to minimize error and uphold the principle of doubt averting punishment.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
10 min
Nisab for Theft: Hanafi Threshold of Ten Dirhams
Establishes Hanafi threshold of 10 dirhams for hadd, refuting other schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi nisab for hadd amputation, explain the Hanafi proof from hadith and ihtiyat, and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i and Maliki arguments.

Core Idea
The hand is cut only for ten dirhams of minted silver — caution in hadd demands the higher threshold.

Theft (sariqa) is a hudud crime, but not every instance triggers amputation. A key condition is the value (nisab) of the stolen property. This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling that the nisab is ten dirhams (or equivalent) of minted silver, contrasting it with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions. Understanding the proof structure and the principle of averting punishment due to doubt (shubha) is essential.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the three positions
The core dispute is the minimum value of stolen property that makes amputation wajib. Hanafi: 10 dirhams. Shafi'i: quarter dinar. Maliki: 3 dirhams. Note the Hanafi rationale: taking the higher amount as precaution.
The higher threshold reduces the number of amputations.
2
Examine the Hanafi primary dalil
The hadith 'لا قطع إلا في دينار أو عشرة دراهم' (No cutting except for a dinar or ten dirhams) is the cornerstone. Analyse its wajh al-dalalah: the exception 'إلا' establishes the minimum; the disjunction 'أو' gives two alternatives, and the Hanafis adopt the higher (ten dirhams) due to ihtiyat.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) so the ruling is wajib, not fard.
3
Analyse the opposing proofs and their weaknesses
The Shafi'i/Maliki rely on the hadith of the shield (worth 3 dirhams) and the hadith of quarter dinar. The Hanafi response: the shield hadith has idhtirab (variations: 3, 5 dirhams); the quarter dinar hadith is interpreted as 3 dirhams at the time, but the explicit 'ten dirhams' hadith is clearer and supported by the practice of the Caliphs.
Mursal narrations (e.g., Ibn Mas'ud) are accepted as hujja in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the principle of dar' al-hadd
Hadud are averted by doubts (shubahat). At lower values, doubt exists about the crime being 'complete' — a person may not intend a major theft. The higher threshold removes doubt, ensuring that only clear cases of serious theft are punished.
This principle also applies to other conditions like hirz (secure place).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
Under Hanafi law, fewer thefts result in amputation compared to Shafi'i/Maliki law. This is not leniency but a careful application of the Prophet's hadith and the avoidance of unjust punishment.
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is 10 dirhams of minted silver, weight 7 mithqals.

سونا ہو اور محفوظ جگہ سے چرانے کی بتائی ہوئی قید بلاشبہ ضروری ہے۔ کیونکہ اگر اس کے محفوظ ہونے میں ذرہ برابر بھی شبہ ہو گا تو اس سے حد نہیں لگائی جاسکے گی۔ انشاء اللہ آئندہ وضاحت کے ساتھ اس بحث کو بیان کریں گے۔ (اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ دینار سے اعتبار کیوں نہیں ہو گا حالانکہ جو حدیث بیان کی گئی ہے۔ اس میں ایک دینار کا اندازہ کہا گیا ہے۔ تو جواب یہ ہوگا کہ دینار کی قیمت کبھی دس درہم اور بھی بڑھ کر چالیس درہموں تک ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے یہ سمجھ لیا کہ دس درہموں کی قیمت مراد ہے۔ اس مسئلہ کی توضیح اسی طرح ہوگی کہ فرمان باری تعالی السارق والسارقة .... الخ میں مال کے کسی انداز اور مقدار کا بیان نہیں ہے ۔ کہ وہ کتنا چھوٹا ہو یا بڑا۔ کم ہو یا زیادہ۔ کیونکہ گیہوں کا ایک دانہ لے لینا بھی چوری ہوتی ہے اور حدیث ابو ہریرہ میں ہے کہ اللہ تعالی چور پر لعنت کرے کہ انڈا چراتا ہے اس لئے اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا ہے اور رسی چراتا ہے۔ جس کی وجہ سے اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا بخاری و مسلم نے اسی طرح روایت کی ہے۔ اسی حدیث کی وجہ سے بعض فقہاء نے کہا ہے کہ تھوڑا مال ہو یا زیادہ سب کے چرانے میں ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ انڈا اور رسی کا ذکر جنس کے طور پر ہے اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا ہے کہ ایک ہی انڈا یا تھوڑی سی رسی سے ہی ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائے۔ اور صحابہ کا اس بات پر اجماع پایا گیا ہے کہ انہوں نے تھوڑی سی چیز چرانے پر ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا ہے۔ اس لئے کوئی مقدار ضرور متعین ہوگی چنانچہ امام مالک و شافعی و احمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہم کے نزدیک اس کی مقدار تین درہم ہے۔ چنانچہ ابن عمر کی حدیث میں ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک شخص کا ہاتھ اس لئے کاٹ دیا تھا کہ اس نے تین درہم کی قیمت کی ڈھال چرائی تھی۔
اس کے مانند حضرت عائشہ کی حدیث میں ہے۔ دونوں روایتیں بخاری و مسلم نے بیان کی ہیں اور ایک حدیث میں ہے کہ چور کا ہاتھ چوتھائی دینار میں کاٹا جائے۔ اس کی روایت بخاری و مسلم اور احمد نے کی ہے۔ اس وقت میں تین درہم چوتھائی دینار کے برابر ہوتے تھے ۔ ترمذی رحمتہ اللہ نے کہا ہے کہ بعض علماء کا اس پر عمل ہے۔ جن میں حضرت ابو بکر صدیق رضی اللہ عنہ وعثمان اور علی رضی اللہ عنہ ہیں اور حضرت ابن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ سے روایت ہے کہ ایک دینار یا دس درہم کے بغیر ہاتھ کاٹنے کا حکم نہیں ہے۔ یہ حدیث مرسل ہے اور امام سفیان ثوری اور اہل کوفہ کا یہی قول ہے۔ میں کہتا ہوں کہ ہمارے نزدیک مرسل روایت بھی حجت ہوتی ہے۔
امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے آثار میں کہا ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم و حضرت عمر و عثمان و علی اور ابن مسعود سے دس درہموں کی تعین کی روایت موجود ہے۔ پس جب کہ ان کے حدود کے بارے میں اختلاف ہوا تو ہم نے اس مقدار کو معمول بنالیا جو معتمد ہے۔ یعنی دس درہم کو۔ پھر ابن مسعود رحمتہ اللہ سے یہ بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کے مبارک زمانہ میں دس درہم سے کم میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا تھا۔ اتنی اس حدیث کو امام طحاوی وعبدالرزاق وغیرھمانے بھی روایت کیا ہے۔
اور ایمن ابن ام ایمن سے روایت ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ڈھال کی قیمت ہونے کے بغیر ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ جب کہ اس زمانہ میں ڈھال کی قیمت ایک دینار تھی۔ اس کی روایت نسائی و طبرانی و طحاوی اور حاکم نے کی ہے اور یہ ایمن جو اس حدیث کے راوی ہیں وہ یا تو حضرت زبیر کے مولیٰ ہیں یا عبد الواحد کے والد ہیں۔ اور یہی اشبہ و قرین قیاس ہے۔ جیسا کہ التقریب میں ہے۔ اور ان کے ثقہ ہونے کے بارے میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اس بات میں اختلاف ہے کہ یہ حدیث مسند ہے یا مرسل ہے۔ پھر بھی جمہور علماء کے نزدیک مرسل حدیث حجت ہوتی ہے اور دوسری روایتوں سے بھی اس دعویٰ کی تقویت ہوگئی تو بالاتفاق حجت ہو گئی اور حضرت ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما کی حدیث میں مذکور ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں ایک شخص کا ہاتھ ایک ایسی ڈھال کی چوری کرنے کی وجہ سے کاٹا گیا جس کی قیمت ایک دینار یا دس درہم تھی۔ اس کی روایت ابو داؤد، النسائی اور الحاکم نے کی ہے ۔ اس کی اسناد میں محمد ابن الحق راوی ثقہ ہیں۔ اصح قول یہی ہے اور ان کے علاوہ یہاں دوسری روایتیں اور آثار بھی ہیں۔ پھر صحیحین کی حدیث ابن عمر و عائشہ میں اضطراب ہے۔ چنانچہ نسائی نے یہ حدیث ابن عمر میں ڈھال کی قیمت پانچ درہم بھی روایت کی ہے۔
It is preferable, except that al-Shafi'i says: The value of a dinar at the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was twelve dirhams, and the zakat (due) is one quarter of it (the dinar). And for us (Hanafis): Taking the higher amount in this chapter is more preferable as a precaution to avert the hadd (punishment). This is because in the lower amount there is a doubt of the absence of the crime, and doubt averts the hadd. And this is supported by his (peace be upon him) statement: 'No cutting except for a dinar or ten dirhams.' And the name 'dirham' is customarily applied to the minted (coined) ones. So this clarifies for you the condition of minted (coinage) as stated in the Book (matn). And it is the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) and it is the most correct, observing the completeness of the crime. So much so that if someone stole ten pieces of silver bullion whose value was less than ten minted dirhams, amputation is not obligatory. And the weight considered is seven mithqals, because it is the customary weight in most lands. And his (the author's) statement: 'or whatever reaches its value ten dirhams' indicates that non-dirham items are evaluated by them (dirhams), even if it is gold. And there must be a secure place (hirz) without any doubt, because doubt averts (the hadd). We will explain it later, God willing.

The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If a sane adult steals from someone ten dirhams or something whose value equals ten dirhams in coin, from a secure place, in such a way that there is no doubt, then it becomes obligatory to cut off the thief's hand. The basis of this ruling is the noble verse: 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands.' ... the verse: meaning the man who stole and the woman who stole, so cut off both their hands to the end of the verse, i.e., this is their punishment. And consideration of sanity and adulthood is necessary because without these attributes no crime is complete and valid. Therefore, the hand of a minor and an insane person will not be cut. And setting a limit of substantial or valuable property is necessary because there is less inclination to steal insignificant property. Also, when taking mere insignificant property, the taker does not attempt to conceal it. Therefore, the concealment, which is a pillar of theft, is not found in mere insignificant property. Similarly, the benefit of deterrence will not be achieved because the wisdom of punishment as deterrence is found in cases that occur frequently. In setting the limit of protected property and substantial amount, our school is that it is ten dirhams. According to Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), a quarter dinar is sufficient. According to Imam Malik (may Allah have mercy on him), three dirhams are necessary. The evidence of Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i is that during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) the hand was cut for stealing a leather shield, and the value of that shield as narrated is three dirhams. Accepting the minimum amount (three dirhams) is preferable because absolute certainty is achieved in that amount. But Imam al-Shafi'i also says that during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) one dinar was twelve dirhams, thus quarter dinar equals three dirhams. And our evidence is that taking the highest amount in this chapter is better as a means and pretext to avoid the hadd. Because in the lower amount there remains doubt that perhaps the crime is not complete, and doubt is such that it removes the hadd. Our doubt is supported by the hadith: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The hand is cut off for a dinar or ten dirhams.' Then customarily dirham means that which is coined (minted). This shows that coinage is a condition, as mentioned in the Book (matn). And this is the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) and it is the most correct, so that the complete crime reaches its final limit and extremity. To the extent that if someone stole a piece of silver whose value is less than ten pure dirhams, then cutting his hand is not obligatory. (Similarly, if ten debased coins are minted whose value is less than ten pure dirhams, then cutting the hand for stealing them is not obligatory.) Then for dirhams, the weight of seven mithqals is considered, because it is the custom in all lands. Here the author (may Allah have mercy on him) stated: 'steals something whose value reaches ten dirhams' – this indicates that if it is something other than dirhams, its value is to be evaluated by dirhams, even if it is gold. And the condition of stealing from a secure place is undoubtedly necessary, because if there is even a particle of doubt about its security, the hadd cannot be applied. God willing, we will explain this discussion clearly later. (If it is said: why is the dinar not considered, whereas the hadith mentioned states the measure of one dinar? The answer is that the value of a dinar sometimes becomes ten dirhams and even exceeds up to forty dirhams. Therefore, we understood that ten dirhams' value is intended. The clarification of this issue is similarly that the command of Allah Most High 'As for the thief, male and female...' does not specify any measure or quantity of property, whether small or large, little or much. Because taking a single grain of wheat is also theft. And in the hadith of Abu Huraira, it is said: 'Allah curses the thief who steals an egg so his hand is cut off, and steals a rope so his hand is cut off.' Bukhari and Muslim narrated similarly. Due to this hadith, some jurists said that whether the property is little or much, the hand should be cut off for its theft. The answer is that the mention of egg and rope is generic; it does not necessitate cutting off the hand for a single egg or a small rope. And there is consensus (ijma) of the Companions that they did not cut off the hand for stealing a small thing. Therefore, a specific amount must be determined. Accordingly, according to Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on them), the amount is three dirhams. Thus, in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar, it is stated that the Messenger (peace be upon him) cut off a man's hand because he stole a shield worth three dirhams.
Similarly, in the hadith of 'Aisha, both narrations are reported by Bukhari and Muslim. And in one hadith: 'The thief's hand is cut off for a quarter dinar.' This is narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, and Ahmad. At that time, three dirhams equaled a quarter dinar. Tirmidhi (may Allah have mercy on him) said that some scholars acted upon this, including Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, 'Uthman, and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with them). And from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) it is narrated: 'There is no order to cut off the hand except for a dinar or ten dirhams.' This hadith is mursal, and Imam Sufyan al-Thawri and the people of Kufa hold this view. I say: According to us, a mursal narration is also a proof (hujja).
Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said in al-Athar: There is a narration from the Messenger (peace be upon him), 'Umar, 'Uthman, 'Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud regarding the specification of ten dirhams. So when there was disagreement about the limits, we adopted the amount that is reliable, i.e., ten dirhams. Then it is also established from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that during the blessed time of the Messenger (peace be upon him), the hand was not cut for less than ten dirhams. This hadith is also narrated by Imam Tahawi, 'Abd al-Razzaq, and others.
And from Ayman ibn Umm Ayman, it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The hand will not be cut off without the value of a shield, while at that time the value of a shield was one dinar.' This is narrated by Nasa'i, Tabarani, Tahawi, and Hakim. This Ayman, the narrator of this hadith, is either the freed slave of al-Zubayr or the father of 'Abd al-Wahid. And this is more similar and in accordance with analogy (qiyas), as mentioned in al-Taqrib. There is no disagreement about his reliability. However, there is disagreement whether this hadith is musnad or mursal. Still, according to the majority of scholars, a mursal hadith is a proof (hujja), and other narrations also strengthen this claim, so it becomes a proof by consensus. And in the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both), it is mentioned that during the time of the Messenger (peace be upon him), a man's hand was cut off for stealing a shield worth one dinar or ten dirhams. This is narrated by Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, and Hakim. In its chain, Muhammad ibn al-Haqq is a trustworthy narrator. This is the most correct saying, and besides this there are other narrations and reports. Then in the two Sahihs, the hadith of Ibn 'Umar and 'Aisha has some inconsistency. Thus, Nasa'i narrated the hadith of Ibn 'Umar with the value of the shield as five dirhams.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the minimum value (nisab) for which the hadd of amputation of the hand is established for theft. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: the stolen property must be ten dirhams (or its equivalent value) and must be taken from a secure place (hirz) without any doubt. The legal basis is the Quranic verse (5:38) and the hadith 'No cutting except for a dinar or ten dirhams.' The author then presents the positions of Imam al-Shafi'i (quarter dinar) and Imam Malik (three dirhams), along with their proofs: the hadith of the shield (worth three dirhams) and the practice of the Companions. The Hanafi response is that taking the higher amount (ten dirhams) is preferred as a precaution to avoid applying the hadd due to doubt (shubha). The doubt arises because a lower value may not constitute a complete crime. The author supports this with the hadith specifying one dinar or ten dirhams, and emphasizes that 'dirham' in custom means coined (minted) silver. Therefore, uncirculated silver bullion (tibr) or debased coins that do not reach the value of ten pure dirhams do not incur amputation. The weight standard is seven mithqals (approximately 29.96 grams). Later, the author refutes the argument that any small theft requires amputation (based on hadith about egg and rope) by clarifying that those narrations are generic and that the Companions' consensus establishes a minimum threshold. The author also reconciles conflicting hadith by giving preference to the stronger evidence: the mursal narration of Ibn Mas'ud and the explicit traditions from the Prophet and the Caliphs specifying ten dirhams. The relied-upon (mu'tamad) position in the Hanafi school is ten dirhams, which is also the position of the majority of early Kufan scholars and is supported by zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum value of stolen property required for the application of the hadd punishment of hand amputation.
حرز (hirz): A secure place where property is kept; theft from an insecure place does not incur hadd.
درهم (dirham): A silver coin; in this context specifically minted (coined) silver dirhams, not bullion or raw silver.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or uncertainty that averts the application of hadd punishment.
اضطراب (idhtirab): Inconsistency or variation in a hadith narration that weakens its reliability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi justification for setting the nisab at ten dirhams rather than three dirhams?
A) Three dirhams is too low to be considered valuable property.
B) The hadith 'لا قطع إلا في دينار أو عشرة دراهم' is explicit, and taking the higher amount is preferred to avert punishment due to doubt.
C) The shield hadith is fabricated.
D) The Caliphs set ten dirhams as a political decision.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi nisab of ten dirhams for amputation is rooted in the explicit hadith and the precautionary principle of avoiding hadd in cases of doubt.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
12 min
The Nisab for Amputation in Theft: Hanafi View and Refutation of Opposing Schools
Establishes Hanafi nisab at 10 dirhams/1 dinar with proofs and refutation of opposing views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the nisab for amputation (10 dirhams/1 dinar), identify the key proofs, and evaluate the Hanafi refutation of the opposing view (3 dirhams/quarter dinar).

Core Idea
The hand is not cut for less than 10 dirhams — established by consistent hadith and ijma, despite conflicting reports.

This passage tackles a foundational dispute in hudud law: what minimum value of stolen property triggers amputation? While the Quran does not specify an amount, the Hanafi school argues from multiple authentic reports and the practice of the Companions that the nisab is 10 dirhams or 1 dinar. The opposing schools rely on hadith in Bukhari and Muslim that mention 3 dirhams. We will examine the evidence and understand why the Hanafi school prefers the higher threshold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its key proof
State the nisab (10 dirhams/1 dinar) and the main supporting hadith: Ibn Mas'ud's mursal report, Ayman ibn Umm Ayman's hadith about the shield, and Ibn Abbas's report. Note that these are consistent and corroborated by the practice of the caliphs.
The Hanafi position is that the nisab is a fixed amount, not a flexible one.
2
Examine the opposing school's evidence
The opposing schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) use the hadith of Ibn Umar (the Prophet cut for a shield worth 3 dirhams) and Aisha (the hand is cut for a quarter dinar, which was 3 dirhams at that time). These are in Bukhari and Muslim.
These hadith appear strong because they are in the most authentic collections.
3
Analyze the Hanafi critique of opposing proof
Show that the opposing hadith are mudtarib (contradictory): different narrations mention 3 dirhams, 5 dirhams, half dinar, etc. This makes them unreliable for establishing a binding ruling. In contrast, the Hanafi reports are consistent.
Hanafi usul holds that mudtarib hadith cannot be used as evidence.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf and conclusion
The practical difference: for Hanafis, theft of goods between 3 and 10 dirhams does not incur amputation; for others it does. The Hanafi view is mufta bihi due to consistency and ijma.
The maxim: 'It is better to err by not applying the hadd than to apply it wrongly' supports caution.

اندازہ کہا گیا ہے۔ تو جواب یہ ہوگا کہ دینار کی قیمت کبھی دس در ہم اور بھی بڑھ کر چالیس درہموں تک ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے یہ سمجھ لیا کہ دس درہموں کی قیمت مراد ہے۔ اس مسئلہ کی توضیح اسی طرح ہوگی کہ فرمان باری تعالی السارق والسارقة .... الخ میں مال کے کسی انداز اور مقدار کا بیان نہیں ہے ۔ کہ وہ کتنا چھوٹا ہو یا بڑا۔ کم ہو یا زیادہ۔ کیونکہ گیہوں کا ایک دانہ لے لینا بھی چوری ہوتی ہے اور حدیث ابو ہریرہ میں ہے کہ اللہ تعالے چور پر لعنت کرے کہ انڈا چراتا ہے اس لئے اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا ہے اور رسی چراتا ہے۔ جس کی وجہ سے اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا بخاری و مسلم نے اسی طرح روایت کی ہے۔ اسی حدیث کی وجہ سے بعض فقہاء نے کہا ہے کہ تھوڑا مال ہو یا زیادہ سب کے چرانے میں ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ انڈا اور ری کا ذکر جنس کے طور پر ہے اس سے یہ لازم نہیں آتا ہے کہ ایک ہی انڈا یا تھوڑی سی رسی سے ہی ہاتھ کاٹ دیا جائے۔ اور صحابہ کا اس بات پر اجماع پایا گیا ہے کہ انہوں نے تھوڑی سی چیز چرانے پر ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا ہے۔ اس لئے کوئی مقدار ضرور متعین ہوگی چنانچہ امام مالک و شافعی و احمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہم کے نزدیک اس کی مقدار تین درہم ہے۔ چنانچہ ابن عمر کی حدیث میں ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ایک شخص کا ہاتھ اس لئے کاٹ دیا تھا کہ اس نے تین درہم کی قیمت کی ڈھال چرائی تھی۔ اس کے مانند حضرت عائشہ کی حدیث میں ہے۔ دونوں روایتیں بخاری و مسلم نے بیان کی ہیں اور ایک حدیث میں ہے کہ چور کا ہاتھ چوتھائی دینار میں کاٹا جائے۔ اس کی روایت بخاری و مسلم اور احمد نے کی ہے۔ اس وقت میں تین درہم چوتھائی دینار کے برابر ہوتے تھے ۔ ترندی رحمتہ اللہ نے کہا ہے کہ بعض علماء کا اس پر عمل ہے۔ جن میں حضرت ابو بکر صدیق پہیہ وعثمان اور علی دینہ ہیں اور حضرت ابن مسعود پیچھے سے روایت ہے کہ ایک دینار یا دس درہم کے بغیر ہاتھ کاٹنے کا حکم نہیں ہے۔ یہ حدیث مرسل ہے اور امام سفیان ثوری اور اہل کوفہ کا یہی قول ہے۔ میں کہتا ہوں کہ ہمارے نزدیک مرسل روایت بھی حجت ہوتی ہے۔ امام محمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے آثار میں کہا ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم و حضرت عمر و عثمان و علی اور ابن مسعود سے دس درہموں کی تعین کی روایت موجود ہے۔ پس جب کہ ان کی حدود کے بارے میں اختلاف ہوا تو ہم نے اس مقدار کو معمول بنالیا جو معتمد ہے۔ یعنی دس درہم کو۔ پھر ابن مسعود رحمتہ اللہ سے یہ بھی ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کے مبارک زمانہ میں دس درہم سے کم میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا تھا۔ اتنی اس حدیث کو امام طحاوی وعبدالرزاق وغیرھمانے بھی روایت کیا ہے۔ اور ایمن ابن ام ایمن سے روایت ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ڈھال کی قیمت ہونے کے بغیر ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ جب کہ اس زمانہ میں ڈھال کی قیمت ایک دینار تھی۔ اس کی روایت نسائی و طبرانی و طحاوی اور حاکم نے کی ہے اور یہ ایمن جو اس حدیث کے راوی ہیں وہ یا تو حضرت زبیر کے مولیٰ ہیں یا عبد الواحد کے والد ہیں۔ اور یہی اشبہ و قرین قیاس ہے۔ جیسا کہ التقریب میں ہے۔ اور ان کے ثقہ ہونے کے بارے میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اس بات میں اختلاف ہے کہ یہ حدیث مسند ہے یا مرسل ہے۔ پھر بھی جمہور علماء کے نزدیک مرسل حدیث حجت ہوتی ہے اور دوسری روایتوں سے بھی اس دعوئی کی تقویت ہوگئی تو بالاتفاق حجت ہو گئی اور حضرت ابن عباس پیچھے کی حدیث میں مذکور ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں ایک مرد کا ہاتھ چھڑے کی ایک ایسی ڈھال کی چوری کرنے کی وجہ سے کاٹا گیا جس کی قیمت ایک دینار یا دس درہم تھی۔ اس کی روایت ابو داؤد، النسائی اور الحاکم نے کی ہے ۔ اس کی اسناد میں محمد ابن الحق روای ثقہ ہیں۔ اصح قول یہی ہے اور ان کے علاوہ یہاں دوسری روایتیں اور آثار بھی ہیں۔ پھر صحیحین کی حدیث ابن عمرو عائشہ میں اضطراب ہے۔ چنانچہ نسائی نے یہ حدیث ابن عمر میں ڈھال کی قیمت پانچ در ہم روایت کی ہے اور حدیث عائشہ نہیں ایک اسناد سے چوتھائی دینار اور دوسری اسناد سے تین درہم یا نصف دینار یا اس سے زیادہ کی روایت کی ہے۔ اس لئے طحاوی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ حدیث مضطرب ہے اور اسی اضطراب کی وجہ سے اس روایت کو چھوڑ کر ایک دینار اور دس درہم کی روایت اختیار کی گئی اور دوم اس وجہ سے کہ قلیل میں پوری مقدار میں شبہ ہے اور سوم اس وجہ سے کہ یہ بات ثابت ہو چکی ہے اگر بادشاہ معاف کرنے میں غلطی کر دے تو وہ اس بات سے بہتر ہے کہ حد لگانے میں غلطی کرے۔ یعنی زیادہ سے زیادہ یہی بات ہوگی کہ تھوڑی مقدار میں حد واجب تو ہوئی تھی مگر امام نے چھوڑ دیا یہ اس بات سے کہیں بہتر ہے کہ حد واجب نہیں ہوئی تھی پھر بھی امام نے اس کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا۔
No literal translation provided as the text is primarily Urdu commentary with embedded Arabic quotations; see commentary for meaning.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the minimum value (nisab) of stolen goods that necessitates amputation of the hand. The author first states the Hanafi position that the nisab is 10 dirhams or its equivalent in value. He then addresses a potential objection: why use dirhams instead of dinars? The answer is that the value of a dinar fluctuates between 10 and 40 dirhams, so the stable standard is 10 dirhams. The text then notes that the Quranic verse (al-Sariq wa al-Sariqah) does not specify quantity. It cites the hadith of Abu Huraira about a thief stealing an egg or a rope, but clarifies that these are examples of genus, not quantity. The Companions' consensus (ijma) indicates that a small amount does not trigger amputation. The passage then presents the views of Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad who set the nisab at 3 dirhams, citing hadith from Ibn Umar and Aisha. However, the author shows that those hadith are contradictory (mudtarib): the same hadith is narrated with different values (3 dirhams, 5 dirhams, half dinar, etc.). Therefore, the stronger evidence supports the Hanafi view. The author then presents supporting reports: from Ibn Mas'ud (a mursal hadith that the Prophet did not cut for less than a dinar or 10 dirhams), from Ayman ibn Umm Ayman (the Prophet said the hand is not cut unless the shield is worth a dinar, which at that time equaled 10 dirhams), and from Ibn Abbas (a man's hand was cut for a shield worth a dinar or 10 dirhams). These reports are authenticated by various scholars. The author concludes that the relied-upon (mu'tamad) view is 10 dirhams, as it is supported by multiple authentic transmissions and the practice of the early caliphs. The passage also mentions the legal maxim: it is better to err in not applying the hadd than to apply it wrongly.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisāb): The minimum value (10 dirhams or 1 dinar) of stolen goods that triggers amputation.
حد (ḥadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Shariah, here amputation of the hand for theft.
اضطراب (iḍṭirāb): Contradiction in narration (different values) that renders a hadith unreliable for establishing a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi critique of the opposing school's evidence (hadith of Ibn Umar and Aisha) for the nisab?
A) The hadith are weak due to a broken chain
B) The hadith are mudtarib (contradictory) with different values reported
C) The hadith are about petty theft, not amputation
D) The hadith are only found in Shafi'i collections

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi nisab of 10 dirhams is upheld by consistent sahih transmissions and ijma, rejecting mudtarib reports.

Equality of Slave and Free in Amputation for Theft
Ruling with two proofs for equality of slave and free in amputation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on amputation for a slave thief and explain the two proofs (Quranic generality and impossibility of halving).

Core Idea
Slave and free receive the same amputation for theft: the Quranic text does not distinguish, and you cannot cut half a hand.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a clear Hanafi ruling: the hadd of amputation applies equally to slave and free thieves. The author provides two distinct proofs – one textual (the generality of the Quranic verse) and one rational (the impossibility of halving a physical punishment). You will learn not only the ruling but also the legal reasoning that supports it, which reinforces the school's commitment to protecting property.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The author explicitly states: 'The slave and the free are equal in amputation.' Identify the act (theft) and the punishment (amputation of the hand).
The ruling is unconditional regarding the slave's status.
2
Identify the first proof (Quranic text)
The Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:38) says 'The thief, male and female, cut off their hands.' There is no mention of slave or free. Recognize that the text is general ('amm) in its application.
In Hanafi usul, a general text applies to all instances until a specific exclusion (takhsis) is proven.
3
Analyse the legal inference (wajh al-dalalah)
The lack of differentiation means the hadd applies to both slave and free. The verse's generality is the operative cause of the ruling.
This is a direct proof from the Quran (dalil naqli).
4
Identify the second proof (impossibility of halving)
The author adds a rational argument: halving the punishment (tanṣīf) is impossible because it would require cutting half a hand. Therefore, the full punishment must be applied.
This prevents a potential analogy with other hudud where slaves receive half punishment (e.g., flogging for zina).
5
Connect to the purpose (ḥikmah)
The full punishment is applied 'as a protection of people's property.' Understand that the ruling serves a broader societal interest (ḥifẓ al-māl).
This illustrates the Hanafi use of maqāṣid (objectives of Sharīʿah) in juristic reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَالْعَبْدُ وَالْحُرُّفِي الْقَطْعِ سَوَاءٌ لِأَنَّ النَّصَّ لَمْ يَفْصِلُ وَلِأَنَّ التَّنْصِيفَ مُتَعَذِّرٌ فَيَتَكَامَلُ صِيَانَةً لِأَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ ترجمہ کہا غلام اور آزاد دونوں ہاتھ کاٹے جانے کے معاملہ میں برابر ہیں۔ کیونکہ نص قرآنی (السارق والسارقة الآيہ) میں کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے اور اس لئے بھی کہ یہاں آدھی سزا دینا محال ہے۔ یعنی غلام کا آدھا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جا سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے غلام کو بھی پوری ہی سزا دی جائے گی تاکہ لوگوں کے مال محفوظ رہ سکیں۔
He said: The slave and the free are equal in amputation because the text did not differentiate, and because halving is impossible, so [the punishment] is completed as a protection of people's property.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the author. The matn states that a slave and a free person are equal in the punishment of amputation for theft. Two reasons are given: first, the Quranic verse (al-Sariq wa al-Sariqah) does not distinguish between slave and free; second, it is impossible to apply half a hadd (e.g., half a hand), so the full punishment must be applied. The Urdu commentary adds that this is to protect people's property, meaning that if slaves were exempted or given lesser punishment, it would encourage theft among them.

Key Terms
الحد (al-ḥadd): Fixed punishment for theft; here amputation.
التنصيف (al-tanṣīf): Halving the punishment; impossible in this case as it would require cutting half a hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are a slave and a free person treated equally in amputation for theft according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the Quran does not distinguish between them
B) Because it is impossible to halve the punishment
C) Both A and B
D) Because slaves are not considered legally responsible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies the full hadd of amputation to both slave and free thief because the Quranic text is unqualified and halving the punishment is physically impossible.

One Confession or Two? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Amputation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of confessions for amputation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on the number of confessions required for amputation and explain the proof and the counter-argument from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
One confession suffices for amputation; the majority of Hanafi imams reject requiring repetition except in zina.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of confessions needed for the hadd punishment of amputation. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that a single confession is sufficient, while Imam Abu Yusuf argues that two confessions are required. The text explores the reasoning behind each position and ultimately establishes the relied-upon view. Understanding this dispute helps clarify how Hanafi jurists balance different types of evidence (testimony vs. confession) and the role of qiyas in hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions and their proponents
The passage states that amputation is wajib upon one confession according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf requires two confessions, and in one narration, in two different sittings. Note the intra-Hanafi nature of the ikhtilaf.
All three are Hanafi imams; the dispute is within the school.
2
Understand Abu Yusuf’s proof: analogy to testimony and zina
Abu Yusuf argues that confession is a type of proof (hujja) and should be analogized to testimony, which requires multiplicity (two witnesses). He also cites zina, where four confessions are needed.
Abu Yusuf uses qiyas: confession : testimony :: theft : zina.
3
Analyze the response of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: distinction between confession and testimony
They respond that a single confession reveals the theft, just as in qisas and qadhf one confession suffices. Testimony requires repetition because it reduces suspicion of lying; confession involves no such suspicion. The ruling for zina is an exception based on revelation and cannot be extended by qiyas.
Key distinction: repetition in testimony diminishes kadhb (falsehood), but confession has no such tuhma (suspicion).
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Yusuf’s view, a thief who confesses once in court would not be amputated; under the majority, amputation is applied immediately after the single confession.
The practical consequence is whether the hadd is carried out or delayed.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position and its basis
The author (al-Marghinani) presents the majority view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad as the stronger position. This is the relied-upon view for fatwa. The reasoning is that one confession makes the theft manifest, and repetition brings no benefit; the door of retraction remains open for hadd.
The majority view aligns with other schools (Malik, Shafi’i) and is considered the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجِبُ الْقَطْعُ بِإِقْرَارِهِ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً وَهَذَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا يُقْطَعُ إِلَّا بِالْإِقْرَارِ مَرَّتَيْنِ وَيُرْوَى عَنْهُ أَنَّهُمَا فِي مَجْلِسَيْنِ مُخْتَلِفَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ إِحْدَى الْحُجَّتَيْنِ فَتَعْتَبَرُ بِالْأُخْرَى وَهِيَ الْبَيِّنَةُ كَذَلِكَ اعْتَبَرْنَا فِي الزِّنَاءِ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ السَّرْقَةَ قَدْ ظَهَرَتْ بِالْإِقْرَارِ مَرَّةً فَيُكْتَفَى بِهِ كَمَا فِي الْقِصَاصِ وَحَدِّ الْقَذْفِ وَلَا اعْتِبَارَ بِالشَّهَادَةِ لِأَنَّ الزِّيَادَةَ تُفِيدُ فِيهَا تَقْلِيلَ تُهْمَةِ الْكَذِبِ وَلَا تُفِيدُ فِي الْإِقْرَارِ شَيْئًا لِأَنَّهُ لَا تُهْمَةَ وَبَابُ الرُّجُوعِ فِي حَقِّ الْحَدِّ لَا يَنْسَدُّ بِالتَّكْرَارِ وَالرُّجُوعُ فِي حَقِّ الْمَالِ لَا يَصِحُ أَصْلًا لِأَنَّ صَاحِبَ الْمَالِ يُكَذِّبُهُ وَاشْتِرَاطُ الزِّيَادَةِ فِي الزِّنَاءِ بِخِلَافِ الْقِيَاسِ فَيُقْتَصَرُ عَلَى مَوْرِدِ الشَّرْعِ ترجمہ اور چور کے ایک ہی بار چوری کا اقرار لینے سے اس کا ہاتھ کاٹنا واجب ہوتا ہے۔ یہ قول امام ابو حنیفہ ومحمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا ہے (اور یہی اکثر علماء کا بھی قول ہے اور امام مالک و شافعی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کا بھی یہی قول ہے ) اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ دو مرتبہ سے کم اقرار پر ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا اور ان سے ہی ایک روایت یہ بھی ہے کہ یہ دونوں اقرار دو مختلف جلسوں میں ہوں۔ کیونکہ گواہی اور اقرار ( دو حجتوں) میں سے اقرار ایک قسم کی حجت ہے۔ اسلئے گواہی پر اسے بھی قیاس کرنا ہوگا۔ زنا میں بھی ہم نے ایسا ہی اعتبار کیا ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ ومحمد رحمتہ اللہ علیہا کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کے ایک بار کے اقرار سے چوری ظاہر ہو گئی۔ اس لئے اسی پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ قصاص اور حد قذف میں ہوتا ہے اور گواہی پر اس کا قیاس درست نہ ہوگا کیونکہ گواہی میں ایک گواہ سے زیادہ ہونے میں یہ فائدہ ہے کہ جھوٹے ہونے کی تہمت کا احتمال بہت کم ہو جاتا ہے اور اقرار میں ایک بار سے زیادہ ہونے سے کچھ بھی فائدہ نہیں ہوتا ہے کیونکہ اس میں کسی کی تہمت کا موقع نہیں ہے اور اگر کئی اقرار کے بعد بھی کوئی انکار کرنا ہی چاہے تو اسے کوئی روک بھی نہیں سکتا ہے لیکن مال کے بارے میں اقرار سے پھر جانا بالکل صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے انکار کے ساتھ ہی مال کا اصل
And amputation is obligatory by his confession once, and this is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: He is not amputated except by confession twice, and it is narrated from him that they are in two different sittings. Because it is one of the two proofs, so it is analogized to the other, which is testimony; likewise we considered in zina. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the theft is manifest by confession once, so it is sufficient, as in retribution and hadd of slander. And testimony is not considered because increase in it reduces suspicion of lying, and it does not add anything in confession because there is no suspicion. And the door of retraction in hadd is not closed by repetition, and retraction in property is not valid at all because the owner denies him. And the condition of increase in zina is against qiyas, so it is limited to the place of revelation.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of confessions required to necessitate amputation for theft. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, a single confession is sufficient. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, two confessions are required, and in one narration, they should be in two different sittings. Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that confession is one type of proof (hujja), and the other type (testimony) requires two witnesses; thus, confession should also be repeated. This is analogous to zina, where four confessions are needed. However, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad respond that a single confession reveals the theft, just as in qisas and hadd of qadhf where one confession suffices. They argue that testimony requires repetition to reduce the chance of falsehood, but confession does not involve such suspicion. The door of retraction remains open for hadd even after repeated confessions, so repetition brings no benefit. In property matters, retraction after confession is not accepted because the owner would deny it. The requirement of repetition in zina is an exception (based on specific revelation) and cannot be extended by analogy. The Urdu commentary adds that this is also the position of the majority of scholars, including Malik and Shafi'i.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrār): Confession of the accused to the crime of theft.
الحد (al-ḥadd): Fixed punishment; here amputation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding the number of confessions needed for amputation in theft?
A) Four confessions
B) Two confessions in two sittings
C) One confession
D) Three confessions

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a single confession of theft suffices for amputation; the requirement of repetition applies only to zina based on specific revelation.

The Hanafi Proof for the Nisab of Theft
Defends nisab by rejecting a conflicting hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi nisab for theft, explain why the hadith of Aisha is rejected, and apply the three proofs used in the Hanafi argument.

Core Idea
The hadith of Aisha is mudtarib; the Hanafi nisab of 10 dirhams/1 dinar is based on sounder narrations, shubha, and judicial caution.

This lesson examines how the Hanafi school establishes the minimum value of stolen goods (nisab) required for cutting the hand. The passage focuses on critiquing a hadith from Aisha that suggests a lower threshold, and offers three independent proofs supporting the Hanafi position of 10 dirhams or 1 dinar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Position
State the nisab for theft according to the Hanafi school: 10 dirhams or 1 dinar (or equivalent value). This is the threshold that triggers the hadd punishment.
Dirhams are silver coins; a dinar is a gold coin. Hanafis treat both as equivalent for nisab.
2
Analyze the Rejection of the Hadith of Aisha
The passage reports that Imam Tahawi declared the hadith mudtarib (contradictory) because it comes with variant wordings (quarter dinar, three dirhams, half dinar). This idtirab makes it unreliable for establishing a legal ruling, so the school prefers the sounder narration of 1 dinar/10 dirhams.
Mudtarib is a technical hadith defect; Hanafis give it significant weight in weakening a tradition.
3
Understand the Shubha Argument
Even if the hadith were sound, Hanafis argue that a small amount (below 10 dirhams) involves shubha (doubt), and hudud are suspended by doubts. Thus, the nisab must be high enough to eliminate doubt.
Shubha includes doubts about the value, ownership, or the thief's intention.
4
Evaluate the Policy Preference (Legal Maxim)
The passage concludes with a policy argument: it is better for the ruler to err by pardoning when cutting was actually due, than to cut when it was not due. This reflects the Hanafi principle of avoiding hudud wherever possible.
This is not a scriptural proof but a rational principle (istihsan) supporting the higher nisab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
در ہم روایت کی ہے اور حدیث عائشہ نہیں ایک اسناد سے چوتھائی دینار اور دوسری اسناد سے تین درہم یا نصف دینار یا اس سے زیادہ کی روایت کی ہے۔ اس لئے طحاوی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ حدیث مضطرب ہے اور اسی اضطراب کی وجہ سے اس روایت کو چھوڑ کر ایک دینار اور دس درہم کی روایت اختیار کی گئی اور دوم اس وجہ سے کہ قلیل میں پوری مقدار میں شبہ ہے اور سوم اس وجہ سے کہ یہ بات ثابت ہو چکی ہے اگر بادشاہ معاف کرنے میں غلطی کر دے تو وہ اس بات سے بہتر ہے کہ حد لگانے میں غلطی کرے۔ یعنی زیادہ سے زیادہ یہی بات ہوگی کہ تھوڑی مقدار میں حد واجب تو ہوئی تھی مگر امام نے چھوڑ دیا یہ اس بات سے کہیں بہتر ہے کہ حد واجب نہیں ہوئی تھی پھر بھی امام نے اس کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا۔
He narrated by dirham? And the hadith of Aisha is not; from one chain she narrated a quarter dinar, and from another chain she narrated three dirhams or half a dinar or more than that. Therefore, Imam Tahawi said that this hadith is mudtarib, and due to this idtirab, this narration was abandoned and the narration of one dinar and ten dirhams was adopted. Second, because in a small amount there is complete shubha (doubt). Third, because it is established that if the ruler errs in pardoning, that is better than him erring in establishing the hadd. That is, at most it will be that the hadd was obligatory in a small amount but the imam left it; this is far better than that the hadd was not obligatory yet the imam cut off his hand.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a proof-based commentary on why the Hanafi school sets the nisab for theft at 10 dirhams or 1 dinar, rejecting the hadith of Aisha which implies a lower threshold. The commentator reports that Imam Tahawi declared the hadith mudtarib (contradictory in its chains), so the school preferred the more reliable narration of 1 dinar/10 dirhams. Two further reasons are given: first, in small amounts there is shubha (doubt) that prevents the hadd; second, it is better for the ruler to err on the side of leniency by not applying the cut than to apply it when it is not obligatory.

Key Terms
مضطرب (mudtarib): A hadith narrated with contradictory versions making it unreliable for establishing legal rulings.
شبہ (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hadd penalties.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of stolen goods required for cutting the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is not found in Sahih Bukhari
B) Because it is mudtarib (contradictory)
C) Because it contradicts the Quran
D) Because the nisab is 10 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi nisab of 10 dirhams or 1 dinar is supported by rejecting the mudtarib hadith of Aisha, the principle of shubha, and the judicial policy of erring on the side of leniency.

Equality of Slave and Free in the Hadd of Cutting
States that slave and free are equal in hand-cutting penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on equality of slave and free in the hadd of cutting and explain the Quranic evidence and the impossibility of halving the penalty.

Core Idea
The Quranic text on theft applies equally; halving an amputation is impossible, so full hadd applies to slaves.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling in hudud: the equality of slave and free in the penalty for theft. The Hanafi school insists on the generality of the Quranic text and the physical impossibility of halving an amputation, leading to the conclusion that a slave's hand is cut just like a free person's. Understanding this ruling highlights the school's commitment to textual literalism (amm) and its rejection of qiyas when it contradicts a definitive text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the first line: 'The slave and the free are equal in the cutting.' State the ruling clearly: both receive the same hadd penalty for theft.
2
Identify the Primary Proof
The text says 'because the [Quranic] text did not differentiate.' The primary proof is the Quranic verse (5:38) which commands cutting the hand of the thief without specifying slave or free. Recognize that the generality of the nass is preserved.
The Quranic text is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalala according to Hanafis.
3
Identify the Secondary Proof
The text says 'because halving it is impossible.' This refers to the physical impossibility of cutting half a hand. Understand that this refutes any attempt to reduce the slave's penalty by analogy (qiyas) to other hudud where slaves receive half.
This argument is unique to the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the Wisdom
The text adds 'as a protection of people's wealth.' This shows the underlying rationale: equal punishment deters theft by slaves, safeguarding property. Recognize that the ruling serves a maqsad (objective) of shari'ah.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the slave's penalty is half of the free's, based on general qiyas that slaves' punishments are halved. This is an important ikhtilaf, but the Hanafi position is the mufta bihi in the school.
The Shafi'i view uses qiyas, while the Hanafi view prioritizes the literal text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلام اور آزادہ قطع ید میں مساوی ہیں
قَالَ وَالْعَبْدُ وَالْحُرُّفِي الْقَطْعِ سَوَاءٌ لِاَنَّ النَّصَّ لَمْ يَفْصِلُ وَلاَنَّ التَّنْصِيفَ مُتَعَدَّرْ فَيَتَكَامَلُ صِيَانَةٌ لِأَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ
The slave and the free are equal in the cutting. Because the [Quranic] text did not differentiate, and because halving it is impossible, so it is completed [as a full penalty] as a protection of people's wealth.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This is a ruling statement establishing that slave and free are equal in the hadd of cutting for theft. The proof is that the Quranic verse 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands' (5:38) does not distinguish between slave and free. Additionally, halving the penalty is physically impossible—one cannot cut half a hand—so it must be applied fully even to slaves. The wisdom is to protect people's property, as slaves would otherwise be incentivized to steal. This position is unanimous among the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تنصیف (tansif): Halving the penalty; here it refers to the impossibility of half a hand amputation.
نص قرآنی (nass qur'ani): The explicit Quranic text; here it is the verse on theft without differentiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Quranic verse mentions 'male and female' but not slave and free
B) Because the Quranic text does not differentiate and halving the penalty is impossible
C) Because the Prophet cut a slave's hand
D) Because there is ijma on this

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that slave and free are equal in the hadd of cutting for theft because the Quranic text is general and halving the penalty is physically impossible.
