Number of Confessions Required for Cutting
Intra-Hanafi dispute on one vs two confessions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of confessions for the hadd of theft, explain Abu Yusuf's dissent, and apply the school's preferred ruling.

Core Idea
One confession suffices to prove theft for hudud, unlike witness testimony where two are needed to eliminate suspicion.

This passage tackles a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: how many confessions are required to impose the hadd of cutting for theft? While Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani deem one confession sufficient, Abu Yusuf insists on two, drawing analogies to testimony and zina. Understanding this debate reveals the Hanafi method of qiyas and the rationale behind the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: one confession is enough.
This is the majority view within the school.
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
Note Abu Yusuf's position requiring two confessions, preferably in separate sessions.
This is a minority view but recorded in the madhhab.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Abu Yusuf's analogy: confession is one of two proofs (the other being testimony), so it should mirror testimony (two witnesses); also analogy to zina requiring four confessions.
Both analogies are qiyas jaliy.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the rebuttal: testimony needs multiplicity to reduce suspicion of lying, but confession carries no such suspicion; the zina analogy is exceptional (khilaf al-qiyas) and confined to its own text.
Also, retraction of hudud confession remains possible even after repetition, unlike property rights.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: on one confession, cutting is imposed per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad but not per Abu Yusuf. The mufta bihi is one confession.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجِبُ الْقَطْعُ بِاقْرَارِهِ مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً وَهذَا عِنْدَابِي حَنِيفَةً وَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَقَالَ ابْوَيُؤْسُفٌ لَا يُقْطَعُ إِلَّا بِالْإِقْرَارِ مَرَّتَيْنِ وَيُرْوَى عَنْهُ أَنَّهُمَا فِي مَجْلِسَيْنِ مُخْتَلِفَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ إِحْدَى الْحُجَّتَيْنِ فَتَعْتَبَرُ بِالأخرى وَهِيَ الْبَيِّنَةُ كَذَالِكَ اعْتَبَرْنَا فِي الزِنَاءِ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ السَّرْقَةَ قَدْ ظَهَرَتْ بِالْإِقْرَارِمَرَّةً فَيُكْتَفَى بِهِ كَمَا فِي الْقِصَاصِ وَحَدِ الْقَدْفِ وَلَا اعْتِبَارَ بِالشَّهَادَةِ لَانَّ الزِّيَادَةَ تُفِيدُ فِيهَا تَقْلِيْلُ تُهْمَةِ الْكِذَبِ وَلَا تُفِيدُ فِي الْإِقْرَارِ شَيْئًا لِأَنَّهُ لَاتُهْمَةَ وَبَابُ الرُّجُوعِ فِي حَقِ الْحَدِلَا يَنْسَدُّ بِالتَّكْرَارِ وَالرُّجُوعُ فِى حَقِ الْمَالِ لَا يَصِحُ أَصْلالِاَنَّ صَاحِبَ الْمَالِ يُكَذِّبُهُ وَاشْتِرَاطُ الزَّيَادَةِ فِي الزِّنَاءِ بِخِلَافِ الْقِيَاسِ فَيُقْتَصَرُ عَلَى مَوْرِدِ الشَّرْعِ
And the cutting becomes obligatory by his confession once. And this is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: He is not cut except by confession twice, and it is narrated from him that the two [confessions] should be in two different sessions. Because it is one of the two proofs, so it is measured by the other, which is the witness testimony; similarly we have considered in zina. And for them [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad]: the theft became apparent by the confession once, so it is sufficient, as in retaliation (qisas) and the hadd of slander (qadhf). And no consideration is given to witness testimony because the increase in it reduces the suspicion of falsehood, but it does not benefit anything in confession because there is no suspicion. And the door of retraction in the right of the hadd is not closed by repetition, and retraction in the right of property is not valid at all because the owner of the property would deny him.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of confessions required to impose the hadd of cutting for theft. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that one confession is sufficient, analogizing to qisas and qadhf where one confession suffices. Abu Yusuf requires two confessions, analogizing to witness testimony (bayyinah) where two witnesses are needed, and also drawing from zina where four confessions are required. The Hanafi response clarifies that the purpose of multiple witnesses is to eliminate suspicion of lying, but confession carries no such suspicion; one confession fully reveals the theft. Additionally, the defendant can retract a hudud confession even after repetition, but cannot retract a property-related admission. The Zina analogy is rejected as contrary to qiyas and confined to its own text. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: one confession is sufficient.

Key Terms
اقرار (iqrar): Confession of the thief to the act of theft; a proof for establishing the hadd.
حجت (hujjah): Proof or evidence; here confession and testimony are the two types of hujjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One confession
B) Two confessions in different sessions
C) Four confessions
D) Three confessions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) requires only one confession for the hadd of theft, unlike witness testimony which requires two.

beginner
6 min
Number of Witnesses Required for Cutting
Ruling on witness requirement for cutting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of witnesses required for the hadd of cutting in Hanafi fiqh and explain the additional precautionary measures the imam must take before executing the punishment.

Core Idea
Two male witnesses are required for hadd cutting; the imam must investigate thoroughly to avoid wrongful punishment.

This passage establishes the evidentiary standard for the hudud punishment of cutting for theft. The Hanafi school requires two male witnesses, analogizing to other legal claims (huquq). Additionally, the imam is instructed to question the witnesses on the details of the theft and to verify their credibility by imprisoning the accused, reflecting the principle of ihtiyat (caution) in hudud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the hadd punishment of cutting for theft. According to the text, it becomes wajib (obligatory) upon the testimony of two witnesses.
The ruling is wajib because it is a fixed punishment from Allah.
2
Locate the basis (dalil)
The basis is qiyas: as in all other rights (such as financial claims), two witnesses are required. The text says 'as in all other rights.'
This is explicit qiyas jaliy, comparing theft to other legal claims.
3
Note the additional precaution
The imam must question the witnesses about the quality, nature, time, and place of the theft. He should also imprison the accused to investigate the witnesses' credibility.
This reflects the principle of ihtiyat to ensure the hadd is not applied in cases of doubt.
4
Understand the rationale
Hudud are severe punishments, so they must be established with certainty. Extra caution prevents wrongful punishment, as supported by the hadith 'Avoid hudud in cases of doubt.'
The text references previous discussions in hudud.
5
Recognize the consensus
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded; all three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on two witnesses for cutting.
This unanimity strengthens the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَجِبُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ لِتَحَقُّقِ الظُّهُورِ كَمَا فِي سَائِرِ الْحُقُوقِ وَيَنْبَغِى اَنْ يَّسْأَ لَهُمَا الْإِمَامُ عَنْ كَيْفِيَّةِ السَّرْقَةِ وَمَاهِيَّتِهَا وَزَمَانِهَا وَمَكَانِهَا لِزِيَادَةِ الْإِحْتِيَاطِ كَمَامَرَّ فِي الْحُدُودِ وَيَحْبِسُهُ إِلَى أَنْ يَسْأَلَ عَنِ الشُّهُودِ لِلسُّهُمَةِ
He said: It becomes obligatory by the testimony of two witnesses, for the realization of manifestation, as in all other rights. And it is befitting that the imam ask them about the quality of the theft, its nature, its time, and its place for extra caution, as has passed in hudud. And he imprisons him until he investigates the witnesses for the accusation.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This ruling states that the hadd of cutting is established by two witnesses, analogous to other legal claims. The imam is advised to question the witnesses about the details of the theft (how it occurred, what was stolen, time, place) to exercise caution, as is done in other hudud cases. Additionally, the accused thief should be imprisoned pending verification of the witnesses' credibility, due to the serious nature of the accusation. This is a unanimous ruling within the Hanafi school; no disagreement is mentioned.

Key Terms
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony of two male witnesses (or one male and two females in financial matters) to prove the theft.
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Caution; the imam should carefully investigate to avoid wrongful punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many witnesses are required for the hadd of cutting for theft according to Hanafis?
A) One witness and the thief's confession
B) Two male witnesses
C) One male and two female witnesses
D) Four witnesses

Key Takeaway
Two male witnesses are obligatory for the hadd of cutting, and the imam must exercise ihtiyat by questioning them and investigating the accused.

Group Theft and the Nisab Requirement
Ruling on group theft with individual nisab condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on group theft and explain why each participant must individually receive the nisab for the hadd to apply.

Core Idea
In group theft, the hadd is only applied if each thief individually receives the nisab.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling on theft committed by multiple individuals. The central principle is that liability for the hadd punishment is individual, not collective. Even if a group steals together, each person's share must meet the nisab threshold for the cutting penalty to apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is group theft (ishtirak fi sariqah). The ruling is that cutting is wajib conditionally — only if each participant's share reaches the nisab.
The default position: no cutting unless the condition is met.
2
Identify the Condition
The condition is that each individual must receive at least 10 dirhams (or equivalent). If a participant gets less, cutting is not applied to that person.
The nisab is assessed per person, not collectively.
3
Understand the Rationale
The reason (illah) is that the obligation of cutting arises from each person's own criminal act (jinayah), not from the collective. Therefore, the nisab is considered in the right of each individual.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli): the cause is personal theft of nisab.
4
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
Shafi'is consider the total value stolen; if it reaches nisab, all participants are cut regardless of individual shares. Hanafis require individual shares to reach nisab.
The practical consequence: in a group theft of 25 dirhams by three persons, Hanafis cut only those who receive 10 or more; Shafi'is cut all three.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا اشْتَرَكَ جَمَاعَةٌ فِي سَرِقَةٍ فَأَصَابَ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ عَشْرَةً دَرَاهِمَ قُطِعَ وَإِنْ أَصَابَهُ أَقَلُّ لَا يُقْطَعُ لِأَنَّ الْمُوْجِبَ سَرْقَةُ النِّصَابِ وَ يَجِبُ عَلى كُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ بِعِنَايَتِهِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ كَمَالُ النِّصَابِ فِي حَقِهِ
He said: When a group participates in theft and each of them obtains ten dirhams, they are cut. And if he obtains less, he is not cut, because the cause for obligation is theft of the nisab, and it becomes obligatory on each of them by his own crime, so the completion of the nisab is considered in his right.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This is a ruling on shared theft. If a group steals together, the hand of each is only cut if that individual's share of the stolen goods amounts to the nisab of 10 dirhams. The reason is that the obligation of cutting arises from each person's own criminal act, not from the collective act. Therefore, the nisab is assessed per person, not collectively. If a child, insane person, or the owner's relative (mahram) participates, the cutting is not applied even if shares reach nisab, because other legal impediments apply.

Key Terms
اشتراك (ishtirak): Co-participation in the theft by multiple individuals.
جناية (jinayat): The criminal act of each participant; the basis for individual liability.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum threshold for the hadd of theft: 10 dirhams or 1/4 dinar or equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a group theft where five people steal 40 dirhams in total (10 each), what is the ruling?
A) All five are cut
B) None are cut because it was a group
C) Only the leader is cut
D) Each is cut if they receive at least 10 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the hadd for theft is applied to each participant in a group theft only if that individual's share reaches the nisab.

Prophetic and Sahaba Narrations on Confession
Cites hadith of Abu Umayya and anecdote of Abu Darda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of confessions required for the hadd of theft and explain the legal reasoning behind not requiring multiple confessions.

Core Idea
The Prophet repeated confession as caution, not obligation; one clear confession suffices for the hadd.

In this lesson, we examine two narratives that shed light on the Hanafi approach to confession in hudud. The hadith of Abu Umayya shows the Prophet seeking multiple confirmations, while the anecdote of Abu Darda highlights the importance of voluntary and informed confession. Together, they illustrate the principle that hudud are averted by doubts (shubuhat).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narratives
Locate the hadith of Abu Umayya about the thief and the story of Abu Darda and the slave girl. Note the key actions: the Prophet repeated the confession; Abu Darda told the slave girl to deny.
These are two distinct proofs from different categories: Prophetic practice and Sahaba practice.
2
Analyze the Prophet's repetition
The Prophet repeated the confession two or three times before cutting the hand. Determine whether this repetition was a legal requirement or a precautionary measure. The Hanafi position: it was for verification (tathabbut), not a condition for imposing the hadd.
The imperative for caution does not create a legal obligation; it is recommended (mandub).
3
Analyze Abu Darda's guidance
Abu Darda, as governor, told the slave girl to deny the theft because she did not understand the consequences. This shows that confession must be voluntary and informed; coercion or ignorance invalidates it.
The hadd is averted by doubts, including doubt about the accused's awareness.
4
Connect to the Hanafi principle
Both narrations support the maxim 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' (hudud are averted by doubts). One confession is legally sufficient if given voluntarily and clearly; repetition is not a condition but a recommended caution.
The Hanafi school thus does not require multiple confessions; a single, clear confession is enough to establish the hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
معلوم ہونا چاہئے کہ ابو امیہ کی حدیث میں ایک چور کے قصہ میں ہے کہ رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کا اقرار دو یا تین بار دہرایا اور اس نے بار بار اقرار کیا تب اس کے ہاتھ کاٹنے کا حکم دیا۔ چنانچہ ہاتھ کاٹا گیا۔ پھر اس کو بلا کر فرمایا کہ تم اللہ تبارک و تعالیٰ سے استغفار اور تو بہ کرو۔ تو اس نے کہا کہ میں اللہ تعالے سے مغفرت چاہتا اور اس سے تو بہ کرتی ہوں ۔ پھر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے خود بھی اس کے واسطے دعا فرمائی۔ کہ الہی اس کی توبہ قبول فرما۔ اس کی روایت احمد و ابوداؤ دو ابن ماجہ والدارمی والی کم اور امیز ارنے کی ہے۔
......
ایک مرتبہ حضرت ابوالدرداء یلہ کے پاس ایک حبشی باندی لائی گئی جس نے چوری کی تھی اور اس وقت وہ دمشق کے حاکم تھے تو فرمایا کہ اے سلامہ! کیا تم نے چوری کی ہے۔ تم یہ کہہ دو کہ نہیں تب وہ بولی کہ نہیں (چوری نہیں کی ہے) یہ دیکھ کر لوگوں نے کہا کہ اے ابوالدرداء ، کیا آپ اس کو یہ سکھلاتے ہیں۔ فرمایا کہ تم لوگ میرے پاس ایسی ایک عورت کو لائے ہو جس کو یہ بھی معلوم نہیں ہے کہ اس کے ساتھ کیا ہوا۔ تا کہ وہ اقرار
It should be known that in the hadith of Abu Umayya concerning a thief, the Prophet repeated his confession two or three times, and he confessed repeatedly, then he ordered his hand to be cut. So it was cut. Then he called him and said: Seek forgiveness from Allah the Blessed and Exalted and repent. So he said: I seek forgiveness from Allah and I repent to Him. Then the Prophet himself prayed for him: O Allah, accept his repentance. This is narrated by Ahmad, Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, al-Darimi, and others. ...... One time, Abu al-Darda' was brought a black slave girl who had stolen, and he was the governor of Damascus. He said: O Salamah! Did you steal? Say 'no'. Then she said: No (I did not steal). Seeing this, the people said: O Abu al-Darda', are you teaching her this? He said: You have brought to me a woman who does not even know what is happening to her, so that she would confess.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage provides narrative support for the rulings on confession. The hadith of Abu Umayya shows the Prophet seeking multiple confessions (two or three times) before ordering the cut, indicating that repetition is not needed for validity but for verification. The anecdote of Abu Darda shows a sahabi advising a slave girl not to confess, demonstrating that confession should be voluntary and not coerced, especially when the accused is unaware of consequences. These narrations illustrate the principle that hudud are to be averted by doubts (shubuhat). The Hanafi position that one confession suffices is not contradicted by the hadith, as the Prophet's repetition was pedagogical.

Key Terms
اقرار دہرانا (iqrar dohrana): Repeating the confession; the Prophet asked for multiple confirmations for caution.
استغفار و توبہ (istighfar wa tawbah): Seeking forgiveness and repenting after the hadd is applied.
الحدود تدرأ بالشبهات (al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat): Hudud punishments are averted by doubts; any doubt in the proof or circumstances prevents the hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To confess immediately
B) To say 'no, I did not steal'
C) To remain silent
D) To ask for a trial

Key Takeaway
A single, voluntary confession is sufficient for the hadd of theft; repetition is recommended but not required, and any doubt must avert the punishment.

Hand-Cutting Requires Two Witnesses; Imam's Caution
Ruling on two witnesses and imam's investigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidential requirement for hand-cutting in theft and explain the imam's recommended investigation.

Core Idea
Hand-cutting for theft requires two witnesses; the imam investigates for caution.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn establishes the number of witnesses required for the hadd punishment of hand-cutting. The author also directs the imam to question the witnesses thoroughly and to detain the accused pending verification. This reflects the Hanafi commitment to strict proof in hudud cases, ensuring no punishment is inflicted without certainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Locate the central legal statement: hand-cutting is obligatory (wajib) by the testimony of two witnesses.
This is the core hukm of the passage.
2
Find the talil (legal reason)
The text says 'for the verification of the manifestation, just as in other rights.' Testimony is the means to establish the crime with certainty.
The analogy (qiyas) to other claims reinforces the principle.
3
Extract the procedural instructions
The imam is advised to ask about the manner, nature, time, and place of the theft, and to imprison the accused until witnesses are investigated.
These are not conditions but recommended precautions.
4
Classify the imam's actions
The phrase 'yambaghi' (it is appropriate) indicates recommendation (nadb), not obligation (wujub). Failure to do so does not invalidate the punishment.
Distinguish between wajib (hukm) and recommended conduct.
5
Connect to broader Hanafi principles
Hudud punishments require the highest level of caution (ihtiyat) to avoid error. The imam's thorough investigation embodies this principle.
Compare with other hudud like zina which require four witnesses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَجِبُ بِشَهَادَةِ شَاهِدَيْنِ لِتَحَقُّقِ الظُّهُورِ كَمَا فِي سَائِرِ الْحُقُوقِ وَيَنْبَغِى اَنْ يَّسْأَ لَهُمَا الْإِمَامُ عَنْ كَيْفِيَّةِ السَّرْقَةِ وَمَاهِيَّتِهَا وَزَمَانِهَا وَمَكَانِهَا لِزِيَادَةِ الْإِحْتِيَاطِ كَمَامَرَّ فِي الْحُدُودِ وَيَحْبِسُهُ إِلَى أَنْ يَسْأَلَ عَنِ الشُّهُودِ لِلسُّهُمَةِ
He said: Hand-cutting is obligatory by the testimony of two witnesses for the verification of the manifestation, just as in other rights. And it is appropriate that the imam ask them about the manner of the theft, its nature, its time, and its place for increased caution, as has passed in the chapter of hudud. And he should imprison him until he inquires about the witnesses due to the accusation.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage states a ruling regarding the proof of hand-cutting for theft. The author, al-Quduri, asserts that hand-cutting is established by the testimony of two male witnesses, just as in other legal claims. The legal reasoning (talil) is that testimony ensures the manifestation of the crime. The imam is encouraged to ask detailed questions about the theft to exercise caution, similar to other hudud cases. Additionally, the accused may be imprisoned pending verification of the witnesses' credibility.

Key Terms
شَاهِدَيْنِ (shāhidayn): Two male witnesses of upright character (ʿadl) required for proof of theft in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Group Theft and Hand-Cutting
Ruling on hand-cutting when multiple thieves cooperate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for applying hand-cutting in group theft and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
A thief's hand is cut only if his individual share of the stolen property reaches the nisab.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: multiple thieves working together. It clarifies that each thief's share must independently meet the nisab threshold. The ruling is not based on the total stolen but on each individual's portion. This principle safeguards against applying the hadd penalty unjustly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is group theft. The ruling: hand-cutting is obligatory if each thief receives at least 10 dirhams; otherwise, it is not cut.
2
Identify the condition
The condition is that each thief's share must reach the nisab (10 dirhams or equivalent). This is the key requirement for the hadd to apply.
3
Understand the reasoning
The obligation of hand-cutting is attached to each thief individually based on his own act (bi'inayatihi). Therefore, the nisab is considered separately for each person.
4
Apply to a scenario
Take a case: three thieves steal 27 dirhams and divide equally (9 each). Since each gets less than 10, no hand is cut. If they steal 30 dirhams (10 each), all three are cut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِذَا اشْتَرَكَ جَمَاعَةٌ فِي سَرِقَةٍ فَأَصَابَ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ عَشْرَةً دَرَاهِمَ قُطِعَ وَإِنْ أَصَابَهُ أَقَلُّ لَا يُقْطَعُ لِأَنَّ الْمُوْجِبَ سَرْقَةُ النِّصَابِ وَ يَجِبُ عَلى كُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ بِعِنَايَتِهِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ كَمَالُ النِّصَابِ فِي حَقِهِ
He said: When a group participates in a theft and each one of them gets ten dirhams, then hand-cutting is obligatory; but if he gets less, it is not cut, because the obligating factor is the theft of the nisab, and it is obligatory on each one of them according to his own act, so the completion of the nisab is considered with respect to him.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario of joint theft. The ruling is clear: hand-cutting applies only if each individual thief's share reaches the nisab of 10 dirhams. The reasoning is that the obligation of hand-cutting is attached to each thief individually based on his own crime. Therefore, the share of each must be at least the nisab. If any thief receives less than 10 dirhams, his hand is not cut, even if the total stolen exceeds the nisab.

Key Terms
نِصَاب (niṣāb): The minimum value of stolen property (10 dirhams or equivalent) required for hand-cutting in theft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All three have their hands cut
B) Only A has his hand cut
C) Only B and C have their hands cut
D) No one has a hand cut

Key Takeaway
In group theft, the hadd applies to each thief only if his individual share of the stolen property reaches the nisab.

Items for Which Hand is Not Cut: The Hanafi Position on Trifling (Tāfih) Thefts
Chapter on what items incur hand-cutting and what do not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi criteria for exempting items from the hadd of theft and evaluate the opposing view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Hand-cutting is not applied to trifling items that are naturally abundant and poorly guarded.

This passage defines which stolen items incur the hadd punishment of hand-cutting. The Hanafi school differentiates between valuable items that are properly secured and trifling items that are abundant and unguarded. We explore the primary evidence from the hadith of Aisha and the rational reasoning for exemption, then contrast the view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on tāfih items
List the items explicitly mentioned as exempt (wood, grass, reeds, fish, birds, game, etc.) and note the conditions: the item must be trifling (tāfih) and permissible in Dar al-Islam.
Tāfih means naturally abundant and of little value such that owners are not stingy.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The hadith of Aisha (ra) that the hand was not cut during the Prophet's time for trifling things. This is the main textual proof.
The hadith is ahad and zanni al-thubut, but it is relied upon.
3
Analyze the rational arguments
Understand the additional reasons: people rarely seek these items against the owner's will, guarding is deficient (wood thrown at doors, birds fly), and common ownership creates doubt.
Doubt repels the hadd.
4
Contrast with the opposing view
Abu Yusuf (and al-Shafi'i) hold that hand is cut for everything except clay, earth, and dung. Their basis is the general rule of cutting for theft of value.
The text also mentions a hadith 'No cutting in birds' that supports the Hanafi view.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi majority rebuts by citing the specific hadith and the deficient guarding reasoning. The mufta bihi is the majority position.
The thamarah al-khilaf: In Hanafi law, stealing wood or a bird does not incur hadd; in Shafi'i law, it would (except for dirt).

وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِيمَا يُوجَدُ تَافِها مُبَاحًا فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ كَالْخَشَبِ وَالْحَشِيْشِ وَالْقَصْبِ وَالسَّمَكِ وَالطَّيْرِ وَالصَّيْدِ وَالزَّرُنِيخِ وَالْمَغْرَةِ وَالنَّورَةِ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيْهِ حَدِيثُ عَائِشَةٌ قَالَتْ كَانَتِ الْيَدُ لَا تُقْطَعُ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي الشَّيْءِ التَّافَهِ أَى الْحَقِيرِ وَمَا يُوجَدُ جِنْسُهُ مُبَاحًا فِي الْأَصْلِ بِصُورَتِهِ غَيْرُ مَرْغُوبٍ فِيْهِ حَقِيرٌ تَقِلُّ الرَّغْبَاتُ فِيهِ وَالطَّبَاعُ لَا تَضِنُ بِهِ فَقَلَّمَا يُوجَدُ اخْذُهُ عَلى كُرْهِ مِنَ الْمَالِكِ فَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى شُرْعِ الزَّاجِرِ وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَجِبِ الْقَطْعُ فِي سَرْقَةِ مَادُونَ البَصَابِ وَلَانَّ الْحِرْزَ فِيهَا نَاقِصٌ اَلَايُرَى أَنَّ الْخَشَبَ تُلْقَى عَلَى الْأَبْوَابِ وَإِنَّمَا يُدْخَلُ فِى الدَّارِ لِلْعِمَارَةِ لَا لِلإِحْرَازِ وَالطَّيْرُ يَطِيرُ وَالصَّيْدُ يَفِرُّ وَ كَذَا الشَّرْكَةُ الْعَامَّةُ الَّتِي كَانَتْ فِيهِ وَهُوَ عَلَى تِلْكَ الصِّفَة تُورِثُ الشُّبُهَةَ وَالْحَدُّيَنْدَرِى بِهَا وَيَدْخُلُ فِي السَّمَكِ الْمَالِحُ وَالطَّرِيُّ وَفِي الطَّيْرِ الدَّجَاجُ وَالْبَطْ وَالْحَمَامُ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَلا طَلَاقِ قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا قَطعَ فِي الطَّيْرِ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ الْقَطْعُ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا الطينَ وَالتُّرَابَ وَالسَّرْقِينَ وَهُوَقَولُ الشَّافِعِيِّ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا ذَكَرْنَا
And hand is not cut for what is found trifling and permissible in the land of Islam, such as wood, grass, reeds, fish, birds, game, orpiment, red ochre, and lime. The basis for this is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: 'The hand was not cut during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for a trifling thing, i.e., a paltry thing.' And what is found, its genus is inherently permissible in its form, not desired, paltry, with little desire for it, and natures are not stingy with it, so rarely is its taking found against the owner's will. Hence there is no need for enacting a deterrent. For this reason, hand-cutting is not obligatory for stealing less than the nisab. And also because guarding of such items is deficient. Do you not see that wood is thrown at doors, and only brought into the house for construction, not for safekeeping? And birds fly, game escapes. Similarly, the common ownership that existed in it, while it is in that state, creates doubt, and the hadd is repelled by it. And included in fish are salted and fresh; and in birds include chickens, ducks, and pigeons due to what we mentioned. And due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'No cutting in birds.' And from Abu Yusuf: hand-cutting is obligatory for everything except clay, earth, and dung. And that is the view of al-Shafi'i. And the proof against him is what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a new chapter defining which stolen items incur hand-cutting. The Hanafi position is that hand is not cut for items that are naturally abundant and of little value (tāfih), such as wood, grass, reeds, fish, birds, game, orpiment, red ochre, and lime. The primary evidence is the hadith of Aisha that during the Prophet's time, the hand was not cut for trifling things. The commentator then provides rational arguments: such items are not highly desired; people are not stingy with them; thus the thief rarely takes them against the owner's will, so harsh punishment is unnecessary. Also, such items are not properly guarded (ḥirz nāqiṣ). Items like birds and game naturally escape, indicating lack of secure custody. The passage then addresses an intra-madhhab dispute: Abu Yusuf opines that hand is cut for everything except clay, earth, and dung, aligning with the Shafi'i school. The commentator refutes this by reiterating the Hanafi evidence of the hadith and the deficient guarding. The passage also clarifies that salted fish and domesticated birds (chickens, ducks, pigeons) are included in the exempted categories because the same reasoning applies.

Key Terms
تَافِه (tāfih): A trifling, insignificant item that is naturally abundant and of little value, such that owners are not stingy with it.
حِرْز (ḥirz): A secure place of storage; for theft to incur hand-cutting, the stolen item must have been in a proper ḥirz. Deficient ḥirz repels the hadd.
حِرْز نَاقِص (ḥirz nāqiṣ): Deficient guarding; when the item is not properly secured, e.g., wood thrown at doors or birds that can fly, the guarding is incomplete, creating doubt that repels the hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following would NOT result in hand-cutting if stolen from an open area?
A) A wooden log
B) A silver coin worth 10 dirhams
C) A live chicken from a coop
D) A fish from a market stall

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts theft of trifling (tāfih) items from hadd punishment due to their abundance, lack of guarding, and the Prophetic practice.

Theft of Trivial and Permissible Items: No Amputation
Ruling on items not subject to hadd amputation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on theft of trivial permissible items and explain why hadd is not applied, including the evidence and the intra-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Stealing trivial, common items is haram, but no hadd amputation due to shubha from deficient guarding and negligible value.

Theft is a grave sin, but the prescribed hadd punishment of amputation has strict conditions. This lesson examines items that are so trivial and freely available that even if stolen, the hadd is not imposed. We will explore the Hanafi rule, the proofs from hadith and rationale, and the differing opinion within the Hanafi school itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items and the general rule
List the examples (wood, grass, fish, birds, etc.) and note that the hand is not cut for them. Understand that these items are both trivial and permissible in origin in Dar al-Islam.
The Hanafi concept of 'tafih' is key: items of little value that custom treats as insignificant.
2
Examine the primary dalil
Read the hadith of Aisha (RA) which states that during the Prophet's time, the hand was not cut for trivial things. Also consider the explicit hadith 'No amputation for birds'.
These ahadith are taken as specific qualifications to the general Quranic verse on cutting the hand.
3
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The author explains that because these items are trivial, people do not guard them carefully, and they often involve common ownership. This creates a shubha (doubt) that repels the hadd.
The principle 'al-hadd yadra'u bi al-shubuhat' (the hadd is repelled by doubts) is operative here.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf differs: he holds that amputation is required for all stolen items except clay, dirt, and dung. Understand his reasoning—a broader application of the general verse.
Imam Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa, creating a 2-1 majority within the school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the response
The majority position is relied upon for fatwa. The response to Abu Yusuf is that the specific hadith evidence overrides the general, and the shubha argument is strong.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah explicitly rejects Abu Yusuf's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِيمَا يُوجَدُ تَافِهًا مُبَاحًا فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ كَالْخَشَبِ وَالْحَشِيْشِ وَالْقَصْبِ وَالسَّمَكِ وَالطَّيْرِ وَالصَّيْدِ وَالزَّرُنِيخِ وَالْمَغْرَةِ وَالنَّورَةِ وَالْأَصْلُ فِيْهِ حَدِيثُ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ كَانَتِ الْيَدُ لَا تُقْطَعُ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي الشَّيْءِ التَّافِهِ أَيِ الْحَقِيرِ وَمَا يُوجَدُ جِنْسُهُ مُبَاحًا فِي الْأَصْلِ بِصُورَتِهِ غَيْرُ مَرْغُوبٍ فِيهِ حَقِيرٌ تَقِلُّ الرَّغْبَاتُ فِيهِ وَالطَّبَاعُ لَا تَضِنُ بِهِ فَقَلَّمَا يُوجَدُ أَخْذُهُ عَلَى كُرْهٍ مِنَ الْمَالِكِ فَلَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى شُرْعِ الزَّاجِرِ وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يَجِبِ الْقَطْعُ فِي سَرَقَةِ مَا دُونَ النِّصَابِ وَلَأَنَّ الْحِرْزَ فِيهَا نَاقِصٌ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْخَشَبَ تُلْقَى عَلَى الْأَبْوَابِ وَإِنَّمَا يُدْخَلُ فِي الدَّارِ لِلْعِمَارَةِ لَا لِلْإِحْرَازِ وَالطَّيْرُ يَطِيرُ وَالصَّيْدُ يَفِرُّ وَكَذَا الشَّرْكَةُ الْعَامَّةُ الَّتِي كَانَتْ فِيهِ وَهُوَ عَلَى تِلْكَ الصِّفَةِ تُورِثُ الشُّبَهَةَ وَالْحَدُّ يَنْدَرِئُ بِهَا وَيَدْخُلُ فِي السَّمَكِ الْمَالِحُ وَالطَّرِيُّ وَفِي الطَّيْرِ الدَّجَاجُ وَالْبَطُّ وَالْحَمَامُ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا وَلِحَدِيثِ قَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا قَطْعَ فِي الطَّيْرِ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ الْقَطْعُ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا الطِّينَ وَالتُّرَابَ وَالسَّرْقِينَ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ وَالْحُجَّةُ عَلَيْهِ مَا ذَكَرْنَا
And the hand is not cut for what is found as trivial and permissible in the abode of Islam, like wood, grass, reeds, fish, birds, game, arsenic, red ochre, and lime. The basis for this is the hadith of Aisha (RA) who said: The hand was not cut during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for trivial items, i.e., insignificant things. And what is found whose genus is originally permissible in its form, not greatly desired, insignificant, with few desires for it, and natures are not stingy with it, so rarely is its taking found with the owner's dislike, thus there is no need for a deterrent law. For this reason, amputation is not required for theft of less than the nisab, and because the guarding (hirz) of them is deficient. Do you not see that wood is thrown at doors, and is only taken into the house for construction, not for safekeeping? And birds fly, game flees, and likewise the common share that exists in it while it is in that state creates doubt (shubha), and the hadd is repelled by it. And salted and fresh fish enter [the ruling], and among birds, chickens, ducks, and pigeons, for what we have mentioned, and due to his (peace be upon him) statement: 'No amputation for birds.' And from Abu Yusuf that amputation is obligatory for everything except clay, dirt, and dung, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i, and the proof against him is what we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on what cuts the hand and what does not. The author states the general rule: no hand amputation for stealing items that are considered trivial (tafih) and permissible in origin in Dar al-Islam. Examples include firewood, grass, reeds, fish, birds, game animals, arsenic, red ochre, and lime. The primary proof is the hadith of Aisha (RA) indicating that during the Prophet's time, the hand was not cut for trivial things. The rationale is that these items are of little value, people do not guard them carefully, and they are often left in common areas, creating a doubt (shubha) that repels the hadd punishment. Additionally, the hadith 'لا قطع في الطير' (No amputation for birds) supports this. The passage then addresses the view of Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, who argue that amputation is required for all stolen items except a few like clay and dung. However, the author dismisses their view by referring back to the hadith evidence provided. The majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that no amputation applies to these items. The passage also clarifies that items like salted fish, fresh fish, chickens, ducks, and pigeons are included in the ruling.

Key Terms
تافه (tafih): Trivial, insignificant, of little value.
مباح (mubah): Permissible; items that are originally lawful to possess and use without restriction.
حرز (hirz): Secure storage; the place or manner in which property is kept safe.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the hand not cut for stealing firewood thrown at a doorstep?
A) Because firewood is not property (mal).
B) Because firewood is trivial and the guarding is deficient, creating a shubha.
C) Because the owner did not place it in a locked room.
D) Because the thief had permission to take it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the hadd amputation for theft is not applied to items that are trivial and permissible in origin because the combination of low value, deficient guarding, and common ownership creates a shubha that repels the punishment.

Theft of Quickly Spoiling Items: No Amputation
Ruling on items that spoil rapidly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on amputation for quickly spoiling items, explain the proof from hadith and custom, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Fresh fruit spoils fast; Hanafis cut no hand, Shafi'is cut once stored — custom decides.

The Hidayah now addresses a special category of stolen goods: items that spoil quickly. The ruling is controversial between Hanafis and Shafi'is, turning on a key hadith and the role of custom. In this lesson, we unpack the rationale that leads to opposite rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items and the exempting principle
List the items that spoil quickly according to the text: milk, meat, and fresh fruits. Note that the principle is that anything that spoils rapidly (yatasara'u ilayhi al-fasad) is exempt from amputation.
2
Examine the primary dalil: the hadith
The author cites two hadith: 'No amputation for fruit (thamar) and no amputation for kathar' and 'No amputation for food (ta'am).' Identify the key terms: thamar (fresh fruit), kathar (palm heart or young fruit), ta'am (food prepared for immediate eating). These establish a general exemption.
The Hanafi school interprets 'ta'am' restrictively to exclude staples like wheat and sugar.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i also cites the same hadith but interprets it conditionally: exemption applies only while fruit is on the tree; once it is taken to the threshing floor (jarin) or storage, amputation applies.
Shafi'i argues that the hadith's wording 'thamar' refers to unharvested fruit.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response using 'urf
The Hanafi response is that the hadith was spoken in accordance with the custom (urf) of the Arabs. In their custom, only dry fruit (yabis) was brought to the threshing floor; fresh fruit was not stored. Therefore, the exemption applies to fresh fruit regardless of storage, while dry fruit (which is stored) is subject to amputation by consensus.
This shows how 'urf (custom) can limit the scope of a general text.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if someone steals fresh fruit from a store, the Hanafi school says no amputation (because it is still fresh and spoils quickly), while the Shafi'i school says amputation (because it is now stored). The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِيمَا يَتَسَارَعُ إِلَيْهِ الْفَسَادُ كَاللَّبَنِ وَاللَّحْمِ وَالْفَوَاكِهِ الرَّطَبَةِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا قَطْعَ فِي ثَمَرٍ وَلَا كَثَرٍ وَالْكَثَرُ الْجُمَّارُ وَقِيلَ الْوَدِيُّ وَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا قَطْعَ فِي الطَّعَامِ وَالْمُرَادُ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ مَا يَتَسَارَعُ إِلَيْهِ الْفَسَادُ كَالْمُهَيَّا لِلْأَكْلِ مِنْهُ وَمَا فِي مَعْنَاهُ كَاللَّحْمِ وَالثَّمَرِ لِأَنَّهُ يُقْطَعُ فِي الْحِنْطَةِ وَالسُّكْرِ إِجْمَاعًا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يُقْطَعُ فِيهَا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا قَطْعَ فِي ثَمَرٍ وَلَا كَثَرٍ فَإِذَا أَوَاهُ الْجَرِينُ أَوِ الْحِرَاتُ قُطِعَ قُلْنَا أَخْرَجَهُ عَلَى وِفَاقِ الْعَادَةِ وَالَّذِي يُؤْوِيهِ الْجَرِينُ فِي عَادَتِهِمْ هُوَ الْيَابِسُ مِنَ الثَّمَرِ وَفِيهِ الْقَطْعُ
And the hand is not cut for what quickly spoils, like milk, meat, and fresh fruits, because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'No amputation for fruit (thamr) and no amputation for kathar.' And kathar is the jammar (palm heart), and it is said it is the wadi (young fruit). And he (peace be upon him) said: 'No amputation for food (ta'am).' And the intent, Allah knows best, is what quickly spoils, like that which is prepared for eating, and what is in its meaning, like meat and fruit. Because there is consensus that amputation is done for wheat and sugar. And al-Shafi'i said: Amputation is done for them [i.e., fruits] because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'No amputation for fruit and no amputation for kathar. So when they are taken to the threshing floor (jarin) or the storage places, amputation is done.' We said: He [the Prophet] related it in accordance with custom, and what the threshing floor houses in their custom is dry fruit, and for that, amputation is done.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage expands the ruling to items that quickly decay, such as milk, meat, and fresh fruits. The proof is the hadith 'لا قطع في ثمر ولا كثر' (no amputation for fruit and no amputation for kathar) and 'لا قطع في الطعام' (no amputation for food). The term 'kathar' is explained as the heart of the palm or young dates. The author clarifies that by 'food' (ta'am) is meant items that are prepared for immediate consumption and spoil quickly. This is different from staple foods like wheat and sugar, for which amputation is universally agreed. The passage then presents the Shafi'i position: Shafi'i also cites the same hadith but interprets it to mean that amputation is not applied to fruit while it is on the tree, but once it is gathered in the threshing floor (jarin) or storehouse, amputation applies. The Hanafi response is that the hadith is based on the common custom ('urf) where only dry fruit is stored in the threshing floor; fresh fruit is not stored, so amputation still applies to dry fruit but not to fresh. Thus, the Hanafi ruling stands: no amputation for quickly spoiling fresh items.

Key Terms
ثمر (thamar): Fruit; specifically fruit that is still on the tree or fresh.
كثَر (kathar): The heart of the palm (jammar) or young dates (wadi).
جرين (jarin): Threshing floor or storage area where harvested crops are collected.
طعام (ta'am): Food; in this context, items prepared for immediate eating that spoil quickly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following items would NOT be exempt from amputation if stolen?
A) A carton of fresh milk
B) A bag of dried dates
C) A bunch of fresh grapes
D) A piece of raw meat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi exemption from hadd for quickly spoiling items is based on prophetic hadith and the custom that such items were not stored; dry items are not exempt.

No Hand Amputation for Theft of Mubah Items
Ruling on theft of mubah items and the hadd exemption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on theft of mubah items and explain why shubha removes the hadd punishment.

Core Idea
Mubah items create shubha, removing the hadd; birds are exempt by explicit hadith.

Hand amputation is a severe punishment for theft, but Islamic law restricts it to cases with clear ownership rights. When an item is mubah—originally permissible for anyone to take—the community's shared right creates doubt (shubha) that blocks the hadd. In this passage, the Hidayah explains which items fall under this exception and addresses a minority view within the Hanafi school. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to apply the broader principle that hadd is suspended by doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule on hadd for theft
Recall that in Islamic law, hand amputation applies to theft of property (mal) with specific conditions (nisab, custody, no shubha). This passage establishes an exception for mubah items.
Hadd is not applied when there is any shubha (doubt) in the ownership.
2
Recognize the cause of shubha for mubah items
Mubah items like wood, grass, fish, and birds in their natural state are owned by the community collectively. This common ownership creates a shubha that prevents the hadd.
The shubha arises from the fact that anyone can lawfully acquire these items.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence for birds
The hadith of Uthman (ra) explicitly says 'la qat'a fi al-tayr'—no cutting for theft of birds. This is the primary proof for exempting birds. The commentator extends it analogically to all mubah items.
Hadith is narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah and Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Compare the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Yusuf held that cutting is required for everything except wet/dry clay and dung. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) follow the hadith. The commentator prefers the majority, declaring it 'asahh' (most correct).
Abu Yusuf's view is recorded in the Nawadir; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority.
5
Apply the distinction to different objects
Fish (fresh, dried) and birds (chicken, pigeon) are exempt. Gold, silver, pearls, and crafted items like wooden doors, planks, and vessels are not mubah and thus require cutting under normal conditions.
Once mubah items are transformed into usable products, they become personal property and the exemption no longer applies.

باب ما يقطع فيه و مالا يقطع
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم .. سارے باشندوں کے شریک ہونے سے چیزوں کے مباح ہونے کا شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور اسی شبہ کی وجہ سے اس سے حدختم ہو جاتی ہے۔ (اوپر ایک قید اپنی اصلی صورت اس لئے لگائی گئی ہے کہ اگر مثلا لکڑیوں کے کواڑ ۔ درواز ہے وغیرہ بنائے گئے تو ان کی چوری کا بھی اعتبار کیا جائے گا) ۔ پھر مچھلیوں میں خشک اور نمکین مچھلی اور تازہ پچھلی سب شامل ہیں۔ یعنی ان میں سے کسی کی چوری میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا اور پرندوں میں مرغی ، پنج کبوتر داخل ہیں۔ کیونکہ پرندوں کی صفتیں ان میں بھی پائی جاتی ہیں اور اس وجہ سے بھی کہ مذکورہ حدیث لا قطع فی الطیر یعنی پرندوں کی چوری میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا ہے اس کی روایت ابن ابی شیبہ اور عبدالرزاق نے حضرت عثمان سے کی ہے اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے روایت ہے کہ ہر چیز میں ہاتھ کا شنا واجب ہوگا۔ سوائے گیلی اور خشک مٹی اور گوبر کے۔ شامی رحمہ اللہ کا بھی یہی قول ہے۔ مگر ان کے خلاف وہ حدیث حجت ہے جو ہم نے پہلے ذکر کر دی ہے۔ ف۔ اگر سونا، چاندی ، موتی لعل اور زمرد وغیرہ کسی نے چرائے تو ظاہر المذہب میں ہاتھ کا ٹا جائے گا۔ اگر لکڑی کے دروازے، پہلے، اور بنے ہوئے برتن چرائے تو بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ تمام پرندوں میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا یہی اصح ہے۔ تشريح وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِيمَا يُوجَدُ تَافِهَا مُبَاحًا فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ كَالْخَشَبِ وَالْحَشِيشِ الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Chapter on what necessitates cutting and what does not. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Six... all residents sharing causes doubt of things being mubah, and due to this doubt the hadd (punishment) is removed. (The condition 'in their original form' is added because if, for example, wooden doors, etc., are made, then the theft of them will be considered). Then among fish, dried and salted fish and fresh fish are all included. That is, the hand will not be cut for theft of any of them. Among birds, chicken, pigeons are included. Because the characteristics of birds are also found in them, and also because of the mentioned hadith 'la qat'a fi al-tayr' (no cutting for theft of birds). This was narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah and Abd al-Razzaq from Uthman. And from Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) it is narrated that cutting the hand is obligatory for everything except wet and dry clay and dung. Shami (may Allah have mercy on him) also holds this view. But against them, the hadith we mentioned earlier is evidence. Then, if someone steals gold, silver, pearls, rubies, emeralds, etc., in the zahir al-madhhab, the hand will be cut. If one steals wooden doors, planks, and woven vessels, the same ruling applies. For all birds, the hand will not be cut; this is the most correct. Commentary: 'وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِيمَا يُوجَدُ تَافِهَا مُبَاحًا فِي دَارِ الْإِسْلَامِ كَالْخَشَبِ وَالْحَشِيشِ الخ' The meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hidayah, commented upon in Urdu. It states that theft of items that are found mubah (i.e., originally permissible for anyone to take without ownership) in Dar al-Islam does not incur hand amputation. The reason is shubha (doubt) due to the common ownership of such items. Examples include wood, grass, fish, and birds. The commentary explains that even if these are transformed into products (e.g., wood into doors), the theft may be considered, but for the raw materials, no cutting. For birds, the hadith of Uthman is cited. A minority opinion from Imam Abu Yusuf holds that cutting applies to everything except wet/dry mud and dung, but the relied-upon position follows the hadith. Precious metals and crafted items like doors do require cutting if stolen, as they are not mubah.

Key Terms
مباح (mubah): Items that are originally permissible for anyone to take without ownership, like wood, grass, fish, birds in their natural state.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt that removes the hadd punishment, here due to the shared permissibility of mubah items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the hand not cut for theft of wood found in Dar al-Islam?
A) Because wood is not valuable
B) Because wood is mubah and owned by the community, creating shubha
C) Because the Prophet forbade cutting for any natural resource
D) Because wood is cheap

Key Takeaway
Mubah items in Dar al-Islam carry a shubha that blocks the hadd punishment for theft, with birds specifically exempted by a hadith.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

No Hand Amputation for Quickly Perishable Items
Dispute with Shafi'i on theft of perishables

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on theft of perishable items, explain the proofs from hadith, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The hand is not cut for items that spoil quickly because the hadith exemption is based on custom and preservation of wealth.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the application of the hadd punishment for theft. The central question: Does stealing perishable items like milk, meat, or fresh fruit trigger hand amputation? The Hanafi school says no, based on well-known hadiths and the customary practice of the Arabs. We will walk through the proofs, the opposing view, and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: theft of items that spoil quickly (milk, meat, fresh fruit, etc.) does not incur the hadd of hand amputation. Note the exception for wheat and sugar by consensus.
2
Locate the Hanafi proofs
Find the hadiths cited: 'La qat'a fi thamar wa la kathar' and 'La qat'a fi al-ta'am'. Understand how these are interpreted to cover perishable items.
3
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State the Shafi'i view: the hadith exemption applies only while items are on the tree or not stored; once brought to the jareen, cutting applies. Note their supporting evidence.
They also cite the hadith of Ibn Umar about the jareen.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine how Hanafis rebut the Shafi'i proof: the Prophet's statement was based on Arab custom, which stored only dried fruit in the jareen. The conflicting hadith is weak and includes double compensation (not accepted).
5
Determine the practical difference
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis do not cut for fresh fruit even if stored; Shafi'is cut if stored in a secure place. Both agree on cutting for dried fruits.

دودھ، گوشت، پھل اور ترکاری کی چوری میں ہاتھ کا ٹا جائے گا یا نہیں
لَ وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِيمَا يَتَسَارَعُ إِلَيْهِ الْفَسَادُ كَاللَّبَنِ وَاللَّحْمِ وَالْفَوَاكِهِ الرَّطَبَةِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا قَطعَ فِي ثَمَرِ وَلَا كَثَرِ وَ الْكَثَرُ الْجُمَّارُ وَقِيلَ الْوَدِى وَقَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا قَطعَ فِي الطَّعَامِ وَالْمُرَادُ وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ مَايَتَسَارَعُ إِلَيْهِ الْفَسَادُ كَالْمُهَيَّا لِلاكْلِ مِنْهُ وَمَا فِي مَعْنَاهُ كَاللَّحْمِ وَالثَّمَرِ لِاَنَّهُ يُقْطَعُ فِي الْحِنْطَةِ وَالسُّكْرِ إِجْمَاعًا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يُقْطَعُ فِيهَا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَاقَطعَ فِي ثَمَرِوَلَا كَثَرِ فَإِذَا أَوَاهُ الْجَرِينُ أَوِ الْحِرَاتُ قُطِعَ قُلْنَا أَخْرَجَهُ عَلَى وِفَاقِ الْعَادَةِ وَالَّذِي يُوْوِيْهِ الْجَرِينُ فِى عَادَتِهِمْ هُوَ الْيَابِسُ مِنَ الثَّمَر وَفِيهِ الْقَطْعُ
ترجمه قدوری رحمتہ اللہ نے کہا۔ ایسی چیز جو جلد خراب ہو جاتی ہے اس کے چرانے سے بھی ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا ہے۔ جیسے دودھ، گوشت، تازہ پھل ( اور روٹی) کیونکہ رسول کا فرمان ہے کہ ثمر (پھل) اور کثر ( کاف اور ثاء کے فتحہ کے ساتھ ) میں ہاتھ کاٹنا نہیں ہے۔ (اس کی روایت ترمذی والنسائی وابن ماجہ اور ابن حبان نے اپنی بیچ میں کی ہے)۔ اور کثر کے معنی بتمار ( جیم کو پیش اور میم کو تشدید کے ساتھ ) کے ہیں اور بعضوں نے کہا ہے کہ اس کے معنی ودی ( واؤ کے فتح اور دال کے کسرہ اور یا کی تشدید کے ساتھ میل کے معنی میں ) رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے۔ کہ طعام کے سوا دوسری چیز میں قطع نہیں ہے۔ ابوداؤد نے مرسلاً اس کی روایت کی ہے اور عبدالرزاق ابن ابی شیبہ ومالک رحمہم اللہ نے بھی اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اس طعام سے مراد یہ ہے کہ ایسی چیز ہو جو فی الفور کھائی جاسکتی ہو یا جلد بگڑنے والی چیز کی طرح ہو جیسے گوشت و پھل۔ یہ مراد اس لئے لی گئی ہے کہ گیہوں اور شکر چرانے میں بالا تفاق ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا اور امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ ان مذکورہ چیزوں میں بھی ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ شمر و کثر میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا ہے۔ لیکن وہ جب کھلیان (میدان جس میں غلہ اکٹھا کر لیا جاتا ہو ) میں لا کر رکھ لئے جائیں تو اس سے چوری کرنے سے ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ یہ استثناء عادت کے طور پر ہے اور جو پھل کہ جرین ( کھلیان) میں رکھے جاتے ہیں وہ عرب کی عادت کے مطابق خشک ہی رکھے جاتے ہیں اور خشک پھلوں کی چوری میں ہمارے ہاں بھی ہاتھ کاٹا جاتا ہے۔
تشریح لا قطع فی ثمر ولا كثر شمر اور کثر کی چوری سے ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ شمر کے معنی جمار یا ودی کے ہیں امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ ان دونوں چیزوں کے چرانے سے ہاتھ نہیں کانٹا جائے گا ہاں اگر یہ تو ڑ کر کھلیان میں جمع کر لئے گئے ہوں تو ان کے چہرانے سے بھی ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ اور احناف کے نزدیک دودھ گوشت پھل ثمر یا کثر کسی کے چرانے سے ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ف۔ واضح ہو کہ امام محمد رحمہ اللہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ ثمر سے مراد وہ پھل ہیں جو خرمہ وغیرہ کے درختوں پر لگے ہوئے ہوں۔ ان کے چرانے سے ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا اور کثر سے مراد کھجور کے درخت کا ہے۔ اس کے چرانے سے ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے لا قطع في ثمر ولا کثر ۔ اور فرمایا کہ ہم اس قول کو قبول کرتے ہیں اور امام ابو حنیفہ رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کا بھی یہی قول ہے جیسا کہ لآثار میں ہے۔
یہ حدیث صحیح ابن حبان و حاکم و مسند احمد وسنن ابی داؤ دونسائی و ابن ماجہ اور ترمذی وغیرہ میں موجودہ ہے۔ شیخ ابن حجر رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اس کی اسناد صحیح ہے طحاوی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اس حدیث کو علماء نے قبول کیا ہے۔ اور ابن العربی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ اگر اس میں کسی کا کچھ کلام ہو تو اس کی طرف توجہ نہیں دی جائے گی۔ الحاصل یہ حدیث صحیح مشہور ہے۔ لیکن مسئلہ میں یہ اشکال پیش کیا گیا ہے کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر کی حدیث میں ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے درخت کے لگے ہوئے پھلوں کے متعلق پوچھا گیا تو فرمایا کہ جوضرورت مند اس میں سے کچھ کھالے لیکن اپنی جھولی میں رکھ کر نہ لے جائے تو اس پر کوئی سزا نہیں ہے اور جو اس میں سے کچھ ساتھ لے جائے تو وہ اس کے مثل کا ضامن ہو گا۔ پھر جب یہ پھل جرین ( کھلیان) میں پہنچ جائے اور اس میں سے کوئی اتنا چرالے جو ایک ڈھال کی قیمت کے برابر ہو تو اس کے ہاتھ کا کا مناضروری ہے۔ ابوداؤد اور نسائی نے اس کی روایت کی ہے اور یہی معنی کچھ زیادتی کے ساتھ احمد اور نسائی میں بھی مذکور ہیں۔ یعنی جو شخص جھولی بھر لے جائے تو اس کی دوگنی قیمت دے اور اسے کوڑے لگائے جائیں اور جو کھلیان میں سے اتنا لے جائے جس کی قیمت ایک ڈھال کی قیمت کے برابر ہو تو اس کا ہاتھ کا نا جائے۔ اور اس کے مطابق امام ابو یوسف و مالک و شافعی اور احمد رحمہم اللہ نے تازہ پھلوں کی چوری میں ہاتھ کا شنا جائز رکھا ہے۔ اور مصنف رحمۃ اللہ نے یہ جواب دیا ہے کہ کھلیان میں تو خشک چھوہارے ہی لے جاتے ہیں۔ اس صورت میں تو ہمارے نزدیک بھی ہاتھ کا نا جاتا ہے لیکن شیخ ابن الہام رحمہ اللہ نے کہا ہے کہ مغرب میں مذکور ہے کہ جرین وہ جگہ ہے کہ جہاں گدر ( ادھ پکے ) چھوہارے جمع کئے جاتے ہیں تا کہ وہ وہاں خشک ہو جائیں۔ اس طرح وہاں پہلے تو تازے چھوہارے ہی جاتے ہیں۔ اس کے علاوہ وہ جرین ایسی محفوظ جگہ بھی نہیں ہوتی ہے جہاں سے چرانے میں ہاتھ کا شناواجب ہو البتہ اس صورت میں کہ خاص طور سے اس میں کوئی محافظ بھی رکھا گیا ہو۔ اس لئے سب سے بہتر جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث لا قطع في ثمر ولاکثر کے معارض ہے اور حدود کے معاملہ میں اسی حدیث کو ترجیح ہوتی ہے جس سے حدود ختم ہوسکیں۔ اس کے علاوہ جرین کی حدیث میں دو گنے تاوان کا بھی ذکر ہے۔ حالانکہ علماء کی جماعت میں سے کوئی بھی اس کا قائل نہیں ہے۔ پھر یہ بھی واضح ہونا چاہئے کہ گیہوں اور شکر کی چوری میں ہاتھ کا ناجانا بالا جماع ثابت ہے۔ اس لئے یہ بات لازم آئی کہ طعام سے یا مر سے ایسی چیز مراد لی جائے جو جلد بگڑ جاتی ہو یا اس کے قریب ہو۔ جیسے فوراً کھالینے والی چیزیں یا جیسے گوشت اور تازہ پھل ۔ خواہ وہ کھلیان میں ہو یا کہیں اور ہوں اور گیہوں میں ہاتھ کاٹے جانے پر ایسی صورت میں اجماع ہے کہ قحط سالی نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ قحط سالی اگر ہوتو ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ خواہ وہ چیز بگڑ جانے والی ہو یا نہ ہو۔
Whether hand is cut for theft of milk, meat, fruits and vegetables? He said: And the hand is not cut for things that quickly spoil, like milk, meat, fresh fruits, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'No cutting in thamar (fruit) nor kathar' and kathar is jummar (palm heart), and it is said it is wadi (unripe date). And he (peace be upon him) said: 'No cutting in food.' And the intended meaning, Allah knows best, is that which quickly spoils, like that which is ready to eat, and what is similar to it like meat and fruit, because cutting is unanimously agreed upon for wheat and sugar. And al-Shafi'i said: The hand is cut for these, because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'No cutting in fruit nor kathar', but when they are taken to the jareen (threshing floor or storage) or the harat (garden enclosure), then cutting is applied. We said: He (the Prophet) expressed it according to custom, and what is placed in the jareen, in their custom, is dried fruit, and there is cutting for it.
Translation: Al-Quduri (may Allah have mercy on him) said: For something that spoils quickly, the hand is not cut for stealing it, like milk, meat, fresh fruit (and bread), because the Messenger said: 'There is no cutting for thamar (fruit) and kathar' (reported by Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Ibn Hibban). And kathar means jummar (palm heart) and some say wadi (unripe date). And the Messenger said: 'There is no cutting except in food.' This is reported by Abu Dawud as mursal, and also by Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shaybah and Malik. The intended meaning of 'food' here is something that can be eaten immediately or is like perishable items such as meat and fruit. This meaning is taken because cutting is unanimously agreed upon for wheat and sugar. Imam Shafi'i said: The hand is cut for these mentioned items, because the Prophet said: 'No cutting in thamar and kathar,' but when they are brought to the khalyan (field where grain is collected) and stored, then stealing from them incurs cutting. This exception is according to custom, and fruits stored in the jareen, in Arab custom, are stored dried, and for dried fruits, cutting is applied among us as well.
Commentary: 'La qat'a fi thamar wa la kathar' – The hand will not be cut for theft of thamar and kathar. Thamar means jummar or wadi. Imam Shafi'i said that the hand is not cut for theft of these two things, but if they are broken and collected in the khalyan, then cutting applies. According to the Hanafis, for theft of milk, meat, fruit, thamar or kathar, the hand is not cut. It should be clear that Imam Muhammad said: Thamar means fruits that are on date palms etc.; for stealing them, the hand is not cut. Kathar means the trunk of the date palm; for stealing it, the hand is not cut because of the hadith 'la qat'a fi thamar wa la kathar'. And he said: We accept this statement, and Imam Abu Hanifa also held this view, as is found in al-Athar.
This hadith is present in Sahih Ibn Hibban, al-Hakim, Musnad Ahmad, Sunan Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, Ibn Majah, Tirmidhi, etc. Ibn Hajar said its chain is sahih. Tahawi said the scholars have accepted it. Ibn al-Arabi said if anyone has any objection, it is not to be considered. In summary, this hadith is sahih and well-known. However, an objection is raised in the issue: In the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar, the Prophet was asked about fruits on trees and said: 'Whoever in need eats from it but does not take away in his garment, there is no penalty; whoever takes some away, he is liable to the like of it. When the fruit reaches the jareen (storage) and someone steals from it an amount equal to the price of a shield, then cutting is necessary.' This is narrated by Abu Dawud and Nasa'i. Similarly in Ahmad and Nasa'i with some addition: 'Whoever takes a garment full must pay double and be flogged; whoever steals from the jarein an amount worth a shield, his hand is cut.' According to this, Abu Yusuf, Malik, Shafi'i, and Ahmad considered cutting valid for fresh fruit theft. The author (al-Hidayah) replied that in the jareen, only dried dates are taken. In that case, we also cut. But Ibn al-Humam said that in al-Mughrib it is mentioned that jareen is a place where unripe dates are collected to dry. So initially fresh dates are taken there. Moreover, a jareen is not a secure place where stealing would necessitate cutting, unless a guard is specifically appointed. Therefore, the best answer is that the hadith of jareen conflicts with 'la qat'a fi thamar wa la kathar', and in matters of hadd, preference is given to the hadith that removes the hadd. Besides, the hadith of jareen also mentions double compensation, which no scholar holds. Further, it should be clear that cutting for wheat and sugar is established by consensus. So it is necessary that 'food' or 'fruit' in the hadith refers to things that spoil quickly or are close to that, like things eaten immediately or meat and fresh fruit, whether in the jareen or elsewhere. And for wheat, cutting is applied only when there is no famine; if there is famine, cutting is not applied, whether the item is perishable or not.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a detailed inter-madhhab dispute regarding theft of perishable items like milk, meat, and fresh fruits. The Hanafi position, based on the hadiths 'la qat'a fi thamar wa la kathar' and 'la qat'a fi al-ta'am', is that the hand is not cut for such items because they spoil quickly and are not considered wealth (mal) in a way that triggers hadd. The term 'thamar' is interpreted as fruits on trees or unripe dates, and 'kathar' as the palm heart or trunk. Imam Shafi'i argues that the hadith only exempts items while on the tree or not yet stored; once they are brought to the jareen (storage), cutting applies. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's statement was according to the custom of Arabs, who only stored dried fruits in the jareen; thus, the cutting applies only to dried fruits, not fresh ones. The commentary also addresses a conflicting hadith from Ibn Umar about the jareen, noting that it is weak and contains elements like double compensation that no scholar accepts. Further, the text clarifies that wheat and sugar are excluded from the perishable category by ijma', so cutting applies to them unless there is famine (in which case the hadd is suspended due to darurah). The author concludes that the hadith removing hadd is preferred over conflicting reports.

Key Terms
ثمر (thamar): Fruit, especially fresh fruit on trees or unripe dates; also interpreted as jummar (palm heart).
كثَر (kathar): Palm heart (jummar) or unripe dates (wadi); also said to mean the trunk of the date palm.
جرين (jareen): A threshing floor or storage place for dates, often where fruits are dried or kept.
طعام (ta'am): Food that is ready to eat or perishable; in the hadith, it excludes non-perishables like wheat and sugar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the hand not cut for theft of fresh fruit even if it is stored in a jareen?
A) Because the hadith 'la qat'a fi thamar' is absolute
B) Because fresh fruit is not considered property
C) Because the jareen in Arab custom only held dried fruit, so fresh fruit is not secured
D) Because the value is too low

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts perishable items from hand amputation based on hadith and custom, and this position is preferred over the Shafi'i view that storage triggers cutting.

No Hand Amputation for Fruits on Trees and Uncut Crops
Ruling on theft of unharvested fruits and crops

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that theft of unharvested fruits and crops does not incur hand amputation and explain the role of ‘adam al-ihraz (lack of secure storage) as a shubha.

Core Idea
Fruit on tree and uncut crops lack secure storage (ihraz), so cutting is suspended.

Theft of fully grown but unharvested fruits or crops might seem like a serious crime, but the Hanafi school applies a key condition for hudud: the stolen property must be in secure storage (ihraz). This lesson examines why the hand is not cut in such cases and how the principle of shubha (doubt) averts the prescribed punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items and the ruling
The text explicitly mentions fruits on trees and crops not yet harvested. The ruling is that no hand amputation (qaṭ‘ yad) applies.
2
Understand the reason: lack of ihraz
The rationale given is 'li‘adam al-iḥrāz' — because these items are not in secure storage. In Hanafi law, ihraz is a condition for the property to be considered properly possessed for hadd purposes.
Ihraz means placing in a protected location. Unharvested crops are considered still attached to the earth and thus not ihraz.
3
Recognize the shubha principle
The absence of ihraz creates a shubha (doubt) about the property being fully owned/possessed in the sense required for hadd. Hudud are suspended by any doubt.
This is a foundational Hanafi principle: ‘al-ḥadd yudra’u bish-shubuhāt’ — punishments are averted by doubts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
درختوں پر لگے ہوئے پھل اور لگی ہوئی کھیتی کی چوری میں قطع ید ہے یا نہیں
قَالَ وَلَاقَطعَ فِي الْفَاكِهَةِ عَلَى الشَّجَرِ وَالزَّرْعِ الَّذِى لَمْ يُحْصَدُ لِعَدْمِ الْإِحْرَازِ وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِي الْأَشْرِبَةِ الْمُطْرِبَةِ لان السَّارِقَ يَتَأَوَّلُ فِي تَنَاوُلِهَا الْإِرَاقَةَ وَلَانَّ بَعْضَهَا لَيْسَ بِمَالٍ وَفِي مَالِيَتِهِ بَعْضِهَا اخْتِلَاتٌ فَيَتَحَقَّقُ شُبَهَةً عَدْمٍ الْمَالِيَةِ
ترجمہ کہاوہ پھل جو درختوں پر لگے ہوں یا کھیتی جو کائی نہ گئی ہو اس کی چوری میں ہاتھ کا نانہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ پورے طور پر محفوظ نہیں ہے اور پینے کی ایسی چیز جس سے نشہ آتا ہو اس کی چوری میں بھی ہاتھ کاٹنا نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ چور یہ کہے گا کہ میں نے اسے بہا دینے اور برباد کرنے کی نیت
Whether hand is cut for theft of fruits on trees and uncut crops. He said: And there is no cutting for fruit on trees and crops that have not been harvested due to lack of secure storage (ihraz). And the hand is not cut for intoxicating drinks because the thief claims (excuses) that he intended to spill it, and because some of them are not property (mal), and regarding the property status of some there is difference, so doubt about lack of property status is established. Translation: He said: For fruits that are on trees or crops that have not been harvested, the hand is not cut for their theft because they are not fully secured. And for a drink that causes intoxication, the hand is not cut for its theft either, because the thief will say: 'I intended to spill it and waste it.'
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage gives two additional rulings from the Hidayah. First, theft of fruits still on trees or crops that have not been harvested does not incur hand amputation because they are not considered properly secured (ihraz). The lack of ihraz creates a shubha that removes the hadd. Second, theft of intoxicating drinks (like wine) also does not incur cutting. This is because the thief can claim he intended to spill it (not to own it), and more fundamentally, because such drinks are not considered property (mal) according to some, and there is disagreement about their property status. This disagreement creates a shubha that the item is not valid property, which prevents the application of hadd. The Hanafi school does not consider intoxicants as valuable property (mal) for the purposes of theft punishment, even if they have some value in the market.

Key Terms
إحراز (ihraz): Secure storage or protection of property; without it, the item is not considered properly possessed for hadd purposes.
شبهة (shubha): Doubt about the legality or property status that prevents application of hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hand not cut for theft of fruit on a tree, according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because fruit is not considered valuable property
B) Because the fruit is not in secure storage (ihraz)
C) Because the thief typically has a right to the fruit
D) Because the fruit is not yet ripe

Key Takeaway
Theft of unharvested fruits and crops does not incur hadd amputation because the stolen property lacks ihraz, creating a shubha that averts the punishment.

No Hand Amputation for Intoxicating Drinks
Ruling on theft of intoxicating drinks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why Hanafi law does not cut the hand for theft of intoxicating drinks and explain the two reasons: the thief's spilling claim and the shubha around property status.

Core Idea
Intoxicating drinks are not considered property (mal) nor protected by ihraz; thus no cutting.

Theft of wine or other intoxicants might seem no different from stealing other commodities, but Hanafi fiqh applies a unique reasoning. The thief's potential excuse of intending to spill it and the fundamental doubt about whether such drinks are legally valuable property (mal) together create a shubha that blocks the hadd. Let's unpack this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the item and the ruling
The item is intoxicating drinks (ashriba mutriba). The ruling is that hand amputation is not applied.
2
First rationale: the thief's claim of spilling
The text says the thief may claim he intended to spill the drink (iraqa), not to possess it. This claim introduces a shubha that the taking was not theft for ownership.
In Hanafi law, the intent of theft must be to take property (mal) permanently. If the thief claims he wanted to waste it, that negates the requisite intent.
3
Second rationale: doubt about property status (maliyya)
Some intoxicants are not considered property (mal) in Shari'ah, and for others there is disagreement (ikhtilaf). This uncertainty creates a shubha about 'adam al-maliyya (lack of property status).
Hanafis generally hold that intoxicants are not mal because they are not beneficial in a permitted way. However, some other schools consider them property if they have market value. The disagreement itself is a shubha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
درختوں پر لگے ہوئے پھل اور لگی ہوئی کھیتی کی چوری میں قطع ید ہے یا نہیں
قَالَ وَلَاقَطعَ فِي الْفَاكِهَةِ عَلَى الشَّجَرِ وَالزَّرْعِ الَّذِى لَمْ يُحْصَدُ لِعَدْمِ الْإِحْرَازِ وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِي الْأَشْرِبَةِ الْمُطْرِبَةِ لان السَّارِقَ يَتَأَوَّلُ فِي تَنَاوُلِهَا الْإِرَاقَةَ وَلَانَّ بَعْضَهَا لَيْسَ بِمَالٍ وَفِي مَالِيَتِهِ بَعْضِهَا اخْتِلَاتٌ فَيَتَحَقَّقُ شُبَهَةً عَدْمٍ الْمَالِيَةِ

Whether hand is cut for theft of fruits on trees and uncut crops. He said: And there is no cutting for fruit on trees and crops that have not been harvested due to lack of secure storage (ihraz). And the hand is not cut for intoxicating drinks because the thief claims (excuses) that he intended to spill it, and because some of them are not property (mal), and regarding the property status of some there is difference, so doubt about lack of property status is established. Translation: He said: For fruits that are on trees or crops that have not been harvested, the hand is not cut for their theft because they are not fully secured. And for a drink that causes intoxication, the hand is not cut for its theft either, because the thief will say: 'I intended to spill it and waste it.'

Commentary
This passage gives two additional rulings from the Hidayah. First, theft of fruits still on trees or crops that have not been harvested does not incur hand amputation because they are not considered properly secured (ihraz). The lack of ihraz creates a shubha that removes the hadd. Second, theft of intoxicating drinks (like wine) also does not incur cutting. This is because the thief can claim he intended to spill it (not to own it), and more fundamentally, because such drinks are not considered property (mal) according to some, and there is disagreement about their property status. This disagreement creates a shubha that the item is not valid property, which prevents the application of hadd. The Hanafi school does not consider intoxicants as valuable property (mal) for the purposes of theft punishment, even if they have some value in the market.

Key Terms
مالية (maliyyah): Property status; whether an item is considered valuable property (mal) in Islamic law.
أشربة مطربة (ashribah mutribah): Intoxicating drinks (that bring joy/trance).
إراقَة (iraqah): Spilling or wasting; the thief's claimed intention to spill the drink, negating theft for ownership.
