Hadd for Theft of a Tanbur and a Mushaf: Hanafi Position and Disputes
States Hanafi rulings with inter- and intra-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the theft of musical instruments and the Quran, explain the grounds of doubt (shubhah) and subsidiary (tabi‘), and compare the Shafi‘i and intra-Hanafi views.

Core Idea
No amputation for tanbur or mushaf: doubt and the subsidiary principle repel hadd.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two cases where the hadd of theft is not applied: the tanbur (a musical instrument) and the Quran (mushaf) even with ornaments. The reasoning hinges on two key Hanafi principles: the creation of doubt (shubhah) and the legal disregard of subsidiaries (tabi‘). The author presents the Shafi‘i disagreement and even an intra-Hanafi difference from Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objects and their rulings
For tanbur: no amputation. For mushaf: no amputation even with ornament. These are the explicit positions stated.
Both rulings are from zahir al-riwayah.
2
Understand the basis for tanbur: from ma‘azif
Musical instruments of idle amusement (ma‘azif) are prohibited in Sharī‘ah and thus lack legal property value (māliyyah). Without property, the hadd cannot apply.
This is a specific Hanafi classification; other schools may consider them property.
3
Understand the basis for mushaf: the thief’s excuse and the subsidiary principle
The thief can claim he took the mushaf for recitation or looking, creating a doubt (shubhah) that repels the hadd. Moreover, the property value of a mushaf lies in its content, which is not property; the physical materials and ornament are mere subsidiaries (tawābi‘) and not independently considered.
The analogy to a wine vessel reinforces the subsidiary principle.
4
Examine the Shafi‘i and intra-Hanafi objections
Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that the mushaf is valuable property (māl mutaqawwim) because its sale is permissible, so amputation applies when the value reaches nisāb. Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one agreeing with Shafi‘i, another that amputation applies if the ornament alone reaches nisāb because the ornament is independent.
The intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf is resolved by preferring the zahir al-riwayah.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and tarjīḥ
The Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) is muftā bihi. The doubt from a plausible lawful intent repels the hadd, and subsidiaries are not independently considered. The analogy to a wine vessel solidifies this – the vessel’s value is ignored because the primary substance (wine) is not property.
Hadd is repelled by even a slight doubt, as a matter of principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طنبور کی چوری میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا

قَالَ وَلَا فِي الطَّنْبُورِلَانَّهُ مِنَ الْمَعَازِفِ وَلَا فِي سَرْقَةِ الْمُصْحَفِ وَإِنْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ حُلِيَّةٌ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يُقْطَعُ لِأَنَّهُ مَالٌ مُتَقَوَّمٌ حَتَّى يَجُوزَبَيْعُهُ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ مِثْلُهُ وَعَنْهُ أَيْضًا أَنَّهُ يُقْطَعُ إِذَا بَلَغَتِ الْحُلِيَّةُ نِصَابًا لِأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ مِنَ الْمُصْحَفِ فَيُعْتَبَرُ بِالْفِرَادِهَا وَوَجْهُ الظَّاهِرِاَنَّ الْأَخِذَيَتَأَوَّلُ فِي اَخْذِهِ الْقِرَاءَةَ وَالنَّظُرُفِيْهِ وَلِأَنَّهُ لَا مَالِيَةَ لَهُ عَلَى اعْتِبَارِ الْمَكْتُوبِ وَإِحْرَازُهُ لِاَجِلِهِ لَا لِلْجِلْدِ وَالْأَوْرَاقِ وَالْحُلِيَّةُ وَإِنَّمَا هِيَ تَوَابِعُ وَلَا مُعْتَبَرَ بِالتَّبْعِ كَمَنْ سَرَقَ انِيَةً فِيهَا خَمْرٌ وَقِيمَةُ الْآنِيَةِ تَرْبُو عَلَى النِّصَابِ

ترجمہ اور یہ بھی کہا کہ طنبورہ چرانے کے بارے میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ لہو ولعب کے طور پر بجانے کا سامان ہے ( یعنی شرعا اس کی ممانعت ہے۔ اس طرح گویا اس کی کوئی مالیت ہی نہیں ہے)۔ اور قرآن مجید کے چرانے میں بھی ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا اگر چہ اس پر سونے یا چاندی کا چڑھاؤ ہو۔ لیکن امام مالک و شافعی رحمہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے اس کے چرانے سے بھی ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا کیونکہ وہ تو قیمتی مال ہے اسی بناء پر اس کی بیع و شراء بھی جائز ہے اور ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ علیہ سے بھی ایسی ہی روایت ہے اور امام ابو یوسف رحمہ اللہ سے دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ اگر قرآن کریم پر سونے کا جڑاؤ دس درہم تک کی قیمت کا ہو تو ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہاں وہ زیور قرآن میں سے نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا تنہا اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور ظاہر الروایتہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن مجید کو لے جانے والا اس وقت یہ تاویل کرنے لگے گا کہ میں نے تو اس کو تلاوت کرنے اور دیکھنے کے لئے لیا ہے اور اس لئے بھی کہ مصحف پاک میں جو کچھ لکھا ہے اس کے اعتبار سے اس جلد کی کوئی مالیت نہیں ہے۔ حالانکہ اس کو محفوظ کرنا اسی اعتبار سے ہے اور اس کی جلد یا اس کے ورقوں یا اس کے جڑاؤ کے اعتبار سے نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ یہ چیزیں تو اس کے توابع میں سے ہیں۔ جبکہ تابع چیزوں کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے کہ ایک شخص نے شراب بھرا ہوا ایک ایسا پیالہ چرایا جس کی قیمت دس درہم سے بھی زائد ہے۔ (اس لئے اس کا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا ہے ۔ کیونکہ اس وقت پیالہ تابع ہے اور اصل مقصود جو کہ شراب ہے اس کی کوئی قیمت نہیں ہے)۔

تشريح . قَالَ وَلَا فِي الطَّنْبُورِ لِأَنَّهُ مِنَ الْمَعَازِفِ وَلَا فِي سَرْقَةِ الْمُصْحَفِ ... الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
The hand will not be cut for stealing a tanbur. He said: There is no amputation for the tanbur because it is from the instruments of entertainment (ma'azif), and there is no amputation for stealing the mushaf even if it has gold/silver ornaments. Al-Shafi'i said: The hand is cut because it is valuable property, and its sale is permissible. A similar view is reported from Abu Yusuf. Also from Abu Yusuf there is another narration that the hand is cut if the ornament reaches nisab, because it is not part of the mushaf and is considered independently. The apparent (zahir ar-riwaya) reasoning is that the taker will claim he took it for recitation and looking, and because there is no property value in the written content; it is preserved for its own sake, not for the leather, papers, or ornament. The ornament is merely a subsidiary, and subsidiaries are not considered—like one who steals a vessel containing wine, where the vessel's value exceeds nisab. Translation: It is said that the hand is not cut for stealing a tanbur because it is equipment for play and amusement (i.e., prohibited by shari'a, so it has no property value). For stealing the Quran, the hand is not cut even if it has gold or silver ornamentation. But Imam Malik and Shafi'i said the hand is cut because it is valuable property, hence its sale is permissible. Similarly, Abu Yusuf has a like narration. Abu Yusuf has another narration that if the golden ornament on the Quran reaches ten dirhams in value, the hand is cut because the ornament is not part of the Quran, so it is considered independently. The reasoning of the apparent (zahir ar-riwaya) is that the one who takes it will claim that he took it for recitation and looking, and because the mushaf has no property value in its content; it is preserved for that purpose, not for the skin, pages, or ornament. These things are subsidiaries, and subsidiaries are not considered—like one who steals a vessel containing wine, where the vessel's value is more than ten dirhams. Commentary: The meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings: (1) The theft of a tanbur (a musical instrument) does not require amputation because it is considered a 'ma'azif'—an instrument of idle amusement which is prohibited in shari'a, and therefore it lacks legal property value (maliyyah). (2) The theft of a Quran (mushaf) does not require amputation even if it has gold or silver ornamentation. The author presents the Hanafi position (zahir ar-riwaya) and then the opposing views. Imam Shafi'i holds that amputation applies because the mushaf is valuable property, and its sale is permissible. Imam Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one agreeing with Shafi'i, and another that if the ornament alone reaches nisab (10 dirhams), then amputation is applied for the ornament because it is independent of the Quran. The Hanafi response is that the thief may claim he took the Quran for recitation, creating a legal doubt (shubhah). Additionally, the property value is attributed to the written content, not the physical materials; the ornament is a subsidiary (tabi') and is not given independent consideration, just like a vessel containing wine—the vessel's value is ignored because the primary substance (wine) is not property.

Key Terms
طنبور (tanbūr): A musical instrument, considered from ma‘āzif (instruments of idle entertainment), hence not legally property.
مصحف (muṣḥaf): The Quran in book form, including its binding, pages, and any ornamentation.
تابع (tābi‘): A subsidiary or accessory that follows the primary object in legal rulings.
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt that repels the application of hadd punishment.
معازف (ma‘āzif): Musical instruments or objects of idle entertainment prohibited in Sharī‘ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the hand not cut for stealing a Quran with a gold ornament worth more than nisāb?
A) Because the gold ornament is not part of the Quran and is considered separately
B) Because the thief can claim he took it for recitation, creating a doubt, and the ornament is a subsidiary that is not independently considered
C) Because the Quran is not property at all
D) Because the nisāb for amputation does not apply to religious texts

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies the principle that doubt repels hadd and that subsidiaries are not independently considered, so amputation is not applied for stealing a tanbur or a mushaf even with ornaments.

Theft of Doors of Masjid al-Haram and the Condition of Ihraz
Gives the Hanafi ruling that doors of the Sacred Mosque are not subject to amputation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that amputation is not required for stealing the doors of Masjid al-Haram, and identify the condition of ihraz that must be satisfied for the hadd to apply.

Core Idea
Theft from a non-secure place does not trigger amputation — the mosque door is not a guard.

In this lesson, we examine a specific application of the Hanafi condition of ihraz (secure custody) to the doors of Masjid al-Haram. While the doors are valuable property, their public and non-securing function means that stealing them does not meet the threshold for the hadd of theft. This ruling illustrates how the Hanafi school ties the severe punishment of amputation to the breach of a protected space, not merely the act of taking.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is stealing the doors of Masjid al-Haram. The ruling is: no amputation is required.
2
Locate the key condition
The condition of ihraz (secure custody) is absent for the mosque doors. The doors do not function to secure the mosque's contents.
Ihraz is a prerequisite for the hadd of theft in the Hanafi school.
3
Compare with a house door
A house door secures the contents inside; therefore, stealing it would be a breach of security. In contrast, the mosque door is merely a passage and does not secure anything.
The passage says 'faṣāra ka bāb al-dār' – it becomes like a house gate, but even more so because the house gate actually secures.
4
Apply the rule
Since there is no ihraz, the hadd of amputation does not apply. This ruling extends also to other contents of the mosque.
5
Note the cross-madhhab implication
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider the doors as regular property and thus apply amputation. The Hanafi position is based on the rationale of ihraz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسجد حرام کے دروازے کو چوری کرنے میں ہاتھ کا ٹا جائے گا یا نہیں

وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِي أَبْوَابِ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ لِعَدَمِ الإِحْرَازِ فَصَارَ كَبَابِ الدَّارِ بَلْ أَوْلَى لِأَنَّهُ يُحْرَزُ بِبَابِ الدَّارِ مَا فِيهَا وَلَا يُحْرَزُ بِبَابِ الْمَسْجِدِ مَافِيهِ حَتَّى لَا يَجِبَ الْقَطِعُ بِسَرْقَةِ مَتَاعِهِ

ترجمہ اور مسجد حرام کا دروازہ چرانے میں بھی ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اسے کسی بھی جگہ میں محفوظ کرنا مقصود نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ دروازہ کسی حاطہ کے پھاٹک کے حکم میں بلکہ اس سے بھی بڑھ کر ہوگیا۔ کیونکہ گھر کے دروازہ سے گھر کا مال و اسباب محفوظ کرنا مقصود ہوتا ہے اور مسجد کے دروازہ سے مسجد کا اسباب محفوظ کرنا مقصود نہیں ہوتا ہے اس بناء پر مسجد کا اسباب چہانے سے ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا۔
Will the hand be cut for stealing the doors of Masjid al-Haram? He said: There is no amputation for the doors of Masjid al-Haram because of lack of secure custody (ihraz). So it becomes like the gate of a house, nay more so, because by the house door what is inside is secured, but by the mosque door what is inside is not secured. Hence there is no obligation of amputation for stealing its contents. Translation: For stealing the door of Masjid al-Haram, the hand is not cut because it is not intended to secure anything in it. So it is like the gate of an enclosure, but even more so, because the house door secures the contents, whereas the mosque door does not secure the mosque contents. Therefore, stealing the mosque contents does not require amputation.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling without direct scriptural proof but with a rational explanation. The Hanafi position is that amputation is not required for stealing doors of Masjid al-Haram because these doors are not intended to serve as secure custody (ihraz) for the mosque's contents. The door of a house or private property is meant to protect and secure the goods inside; therefore, tampering with it is considered a breach of security. However, the doors of the Sacred Mosque are open to all and do not function to secure property; they are merely passageways. Thus, stealing them is not akin to theft from a secure place, and the hadd punishment does not apply. The author compares it to a gate of an enclosure (bab al-dar), but says it is even more so because a house door actually secures what is inside, whereas a mosque door does not. Consequently, even stealing other items from within the mosque does not incur amputation due to the lack of proper hiraz.

Key Terms
إحراز (ihraz): Secure custody: the state of being in a protected place such that unauthorized taking constitutes theft subject to amputation
مسجد حرام (Masjid al-Haram): The Sacred Mosque in Makkah, which has unique rulings due to its openness and lack of private ownership

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school hold that amputation is not required for stealing the doors of Masjid al-Haram?
A) Because the doors are not valuable
B) Because the doors do not serve to secure the mosque's contents, so they lack the condition of hiraz
C) Because the mosque is public property and has no owner
D) Because the thief can claim he intended to use them elsewhere

Key Takeaway
Amputation for theft requires that the stolen property be taken from a place of secure custody (ihraz); the open and public nature of Masjid al-Haram means its doors and contents are not in such a secure place.

No Hand-Cutting for Theft of Masjid al-Haram Doors
Ruling on no cutting for stealing mosque doors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on theft of mosque doors and explain why the condition of hirz is not fulfilled.

Core Idea
A mosque door is not a hirz; without hirz, hadd is not wajib.

The Hanafi school applies the hadd penalty for theft only when specific conditions are met, including that the stolen item was taken from a secure place (hirz). This lesson examines why stealing doors from the Masjid al-Haram does not trigger hand-cutting, and extends the same reasoning to other mosque property. The key distinction is functional: a mosque door does not serve to secure the contents of the mosque, unlike a house door.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is stealing doors of Masjid al-Haram. The ruling is that there is no hand-cutting (hadd is not wajib).
The ruling is absolute, not conditional on nisab or other factors in this passage.
2
Identify the missing condition
The condition for hadd is hirz (secure place). The text states 'adam al-ihraz' (lack of securing). The door is not a hirz because it does not secure the mosque's interior.
The door itself is not intended to secure the mosque's contents.
3
Compare with a house door
The author compares: the mosque door is like a house door, but even more so because a house door secures the house's contents, while a mosque door does not.
This analogy clarifies why the ruling is even stronger (bal awla) for mosque doors.
4
Apply the reasoning to furnishings
The text says 'such that cutting is not wajib for stealing its furnishings.' So the same lack of hirz applies to items inside the mosque.
This expands the scope beyond doors to all mosque property not secured in a locked space.
5
Extract the legal principle
Hirz is defined by function, not by sanctity. The purpose of hirz is to secure valuables; a mosque door does not serve that purpose.
This principle can be applied to other cases of theft from public or semi-public places.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِي أَبْوَابِ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ لِعَدَمِ الإِحْرَازِ فَصَارَ كَبَابِ الدَّارِ بَلْ أَوْلَى لِأَنَّهُ يُحْرَزُ بِبَابِ الدَّارِ مَا فِيهَا وَلَا يُحْرَزُ بِبَابِ الْمَسْجِدِ مَا فِيهِ حَتَّى لَا يَجِبَ الْقَطْعُ بِسَرْقَةِ مَتَاعِهِ
ترجمہ اور مسجد حرام کا دروازہ چرانے میں بھی ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اسے کسی بھی جگہ میں محفوظ کرنا مقصود نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یہ دروازہ کسی حاطہ کے پھاٹک کے حکم میں بلکہ اس سے بھی بڑھ کر ہوگیا۔ کیونکہ گھر کے دروازہ سے گھر کا مال و اسباب محفوظ کرنا مقصود ہوتا ہے اور مسجد کے دروازہ سے مسجد کا اسباب محفوظ کرنا مقصود نہیں ہوتا ہے اس بناء پر مسجد کا اسباب چہانے سے ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جاتا۔
And there is no cutting for the doors of the Sacred Mosque due to lack of hirz (secure place), so it becomes like the door of a house, rather more so, because with the door of a house what is inside is secured, but with the door of a mosque what is inside is not secured, such that cutting is not wajib for stealing its furnishings.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This is a ruling statement that the hand is not cut for stealing doors of Masjid al-Haram. The reason given is 'adam al-ihraz' (lack of securing/fortification). The commentary explains that the door of a mosque is not intended to secure the contents of the mosque; it is like a gate to a courtyard or even less. In contrast, a house door is meant to secure the property inside, so stealing a house door may incur hadd if other conditions are met. The ruling is based on the concept of hirz: for hadd to apply, the stolen item must be taken from a secure place (hirz). Since mosque doors are not for securing, they are not considered hirz for hadd purposes. This ruling also implies that if someone steals the furnishings of the mosque, cutting is not applied because the mosque itself is not a hirz for its contents, as stated in the final phrase.

Key Terms
إحراز (iḥrāz): The condition of the stolen item being in a secure place (hirz) that prevents easy theft; also the act of securing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason the hand is not cut for stealing doors of Masjid al-Haram according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the doors are not made of valuable material.
B) Because there is a lack of hirz (secure enclosure) since the door does not serve to secure the mosque's contents.
C) Because the mosque is public property and cannot be stolen.
D) Because the nisab for mosque property is higher.

Key Takeaway
The hand is not cut for stealing mosque doors because the door does not serve as a secure place (hirz) for the mosque's contents.

No Hand-Cutting for Gold Cross, Chess, and Backgammon Theft
Ruling on no cutting for stealing a gold cross, chess, or backgammon due to ta'wil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to EXPLAIN why the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah) does not apply hand-cutting for stealing a gold cross, chess, or backgammon, and DISTINGUISH the exception of Imam Abu Yusuf based on hirz.

Core Idea
Ta'wil of breaking prohibited objects creates shubha that repels hadd.

The hadd penalty for theft is a severe punishment, but Islamic law erects safeguards to prevent its application in cases of doubt. This passage from Al-Hidayah examines three items—a gold cross, a chess set, and backgammon—that are not ordinary property. The Hanafi school holds that the thief can plausibly claim he intended to destroy them as forbidden objects, creating a shubha (doubt) that blocks the penalty. Yet Imam Abu Yusuf introduces a nuanced exception based on location and security. Let's dissect this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three items and the general ruling
Locate in the passage the three specific items: a gold cross, chess, and backgammon. Note the ruling: no hand-cutting (لا يقطع). This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa.
The items are all associated with prohibited acts: shirk (cross), gambling (chess/backgammon).
2
Understand the reason: ta'wil of breaking
The textual basis: 'because the taker can claim (ta'wil) that he took them to break them, forbidding the evil.' The thief may argue he intended to destroy the prohibited object, not to own it. This claim is plausible because the items are themselves prohibited (munkar).
This is a rational argument (dalil aqli) based on the principle that hudud are repelled by doubts.
3
Compare with the dirham with an image
The passage contrasts the ruling for a dirham that bears an image of a living being. The hand is cut because the image is not an object of worship, so the ta'wil of breaking is not plausible. The thief cannot claim a lawful intention.
This contrast highlights that the plausibility of ta'wil depends on the item's religious or legal status.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's distinction for the cross
Imam Abu Yusuf adds a condition based on hirz (secure place). If the gold cross is in a church (musalla), it is not cut due to lack of hirz; if in a private house, it is cut because both mal (property value) and hirz are complete.
Abu Yusuf's reasoning: the ta'wil is less plausible when the item is properly secured, because the thief would expect to be caught and the intent to break is not the primary motive.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the Zahir al-Riwayah: no cutting for these items. The difference between the two views (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a judge following Abu Yusuf would cut for a gold cross stolen from a secure house, while a judge following the main view would not.
Al-Marghinani favors the Zahir al-Riwayah, but Abu Yusuf's view is also recorded as a valid opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا الصَّلِيبِ مِنَ الذَّهَبِ وَلَا الشَّطْرَنجِ وَلَا النَّرْدِ لِأَنَّهُ يَتَأَوَّلُ مَنْ أَخَذَهَا الْكَسْرَ نَهْيًا عَنِ الْمُنْكِرِ بِخِلَافِ الدِّرْهَمِ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ التِّمْثَالُ لِأَنَّهُ مَا أُعِدَّ لِلْعِبَادَةِ فَلَا يَثْبُتُ شُبْهَةُ إِبَاحَةِ الْكَسْرِ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ الصَّلِيبُ فِي الْمُصَلَّى لَا يُقْطَعُ لِعَدَمِ الْحِرْزِ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي بَيْتٍ آخَرَ يُقْطَعُ لِكَمَالِ الْمَالِيَةِ وَالْحِرْزِ
ترجمہ کہا، اگر کسی نے سونے کی صلیب یا شطرنج یا نرد (نون اور راء کے فتحہ کے ساتھ) چرالی تو اس کا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ چور اس کے لینے میں یہ تاویل کرلے گا کہ میں نے لوگوں کو شرعی ممنوع چیز سے روکنے کا ارادہ کیا تھا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر ایسا درہم چرالیا جس پر کسی کی تصویر بنی ہوئی ہو اور وہ مقدار نصاب ہو تو اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تصویر عبادت کے واسطے نہیں بنائی گئی ہے اس لئے اس کے بارے میں یہ شبہ نہ رہا کہ اسے توڑ دینا جائز ہے۔ یعنی اس کے چراتے وقت چور یہ بہانہ نہیں بنا سکتا ہے کہ میں نے اسے توڑنے کے واسطے لیا تھا اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ اگر سونے کی صلیب ان کی گرجا گھر میں ہو تو وہاں سے چرانے میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ محفوظ مکان میں نہیں ہے اور اگر کسی نصرانی کے کمرہ میں ہو یعنی محفوظ ہو تو ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس کی مالیت بھی پوری ہے اور حفاظت بھی پوری موجود ہے۔
He said: And no (cutting) for a gold cross, nor for chess, nor for backgammon, because the taker can claim (ta'wil) that he took them to break them, forbidding the evil. Contrary to a dirham on which is an image, because it was not prepared for worship, so the doubt of permissibility of breaking is not established. And from Abu Yusuf: if the cross is in the place of prayer (church), it is not cut due to lack of hirz; if it is in another house, it is cut due to complete property value and hirz.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf) regarding the theft of prohibited items. The Hanafi ruling (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that the hand is not cut for stealing a gold cross, chess set, or backgammon set because the thief can plausibly claim he intended to break them as an act of forbidding evil (nahi anil munkar). This creates a shubha (doubt) that prevents hadd. In contrast, if a dirham with an image (depicting a living being) is stolen, the hand is cut because the image is not an object of worship; thus, there is no shubha of permissible breaking. Imam Abu Yusuf has a different view: for the gold cross, he distinguishes based on location. If the cross is in a church (musalla), it is not cut because the church is not a secure place (hirz) for a cross? Actually the text says 'adam al-hirz' — the cross is not properly secured. If it is in a private house, then cutting applies because the conditions of property and hirz are complete. The commentary explains that the thief cannot claim ta'wil for a dirham with an image because it is not used for worship. This ruling highlights the importance of the thief's possible excuse (ta'wil) and the requirement of both mal and hirz for hadd.

Key Terms
صليب (ṣalīb): A cross, specifically made of gold, used in Christian worship; considered a prohibited object (munkar) in Islam.
تاویل (ta'wīl): A plausible excuse or interpretation that the thief can offer to claim a lawful intent, such as breaking a prohibited object.
شبہ (shubha): Doubt; here, the possibility that the thief had a lawful intention (ta'wil) creates a doubt about the criminal intent required for hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah) not cut the hand for stealing a gold cross, while it does cut for stealing a dirham with an image?
A) Because a gold cross is not worth the nisab, but a dirham is.
B) Because the thief can claim he intended to break the cross as an act of forbidding evil, but for the dirham the image is not an object of worship, so no such claim is plausible.
C) Because a gold cross is considered property only for non-Muslims, but a dirham is universal property.
D) Because the Quran explicitly prohibits cutting for religious symbols.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school repels the hadd penalty when the thief can claim a plausible ta'wil of destroying a prohibited object, even if the item has monetary value, prioritizing shubha over property considerations.

No Hand-Cutting for Theft of a Free Child – The Hanafi Ruling and Proofs
Ruling on no cutting for stealing a free child even with jewelry due to ta'wil and child being non-mal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on theft of a free child, explain the two main proofs (free person not mal and ta'wil), and distinguish the intra-Hanafi difference of Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A free child is not property; the thief's plausible excuse blocks the hadd; jewelry is subordinate.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific nuance in theft (sariqa) law: what if someone steals an infant who is wearing valuable jewelry? The Hanafi school holds that the hand is not cut, based on two key principles. Understanding this ruling clarifies the limits of property (mal) and the role of doubt (shubha) in Islamic criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is theft (sariqa) of a free child (ṣabiyy ḥurr) who is wearing jewelry. The ruling according to Zahir al-Riwayah is that no hadd (hand-cutting) is imposed.
2
State the first proof – free person is not property
The passage states: 'because the free person is not property.' The stolen object must be mal, and a free human is not mal, so the condition for hadd is absent.
This is a foundational principle: a free person cannot be owned.
3
State the second proof – subordinate rule (tab')
The jewelry on the child is subordinate (tab') to the child. Since the child is not mal, the subordinate follows the primary in ruling – no hadd.
The principle al-tābi‘ tābi‘ (the subordinate follows) applies.
4
State the third proof – ta'wil (plausible excuse)
The thief can claim he took the child to quiet him or to carry him to his wet nurse. This creates a doubt (shubha) that prevents hadd.
Ta'wil is a recognized defense in hadd cases when there is a reasonable alternative explanation.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference and the mufta bihi
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that if the jewelry alone reaches nisab, the hand is cut because the jewelry is considered the primary object. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view (Zahir al-Riwayah) – no cutting.
This difference only applies to an infant who cannot walk or speak. Consensus: if the child can walk/talk, no cutting; if the child is a slave, cutting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا قَطْعَ عَلَى سَارِقِ الصَّبِيِّ الْحُرِّ وَإِنْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ حُلِيٌّ لِأَنَّ الْحُرَّ لَيْسَ بِمَالٍ وَمَا عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الْحُلِيِّ تَبْعٌ لَهُ وَلِأَنَّهُ يَتَأَوَّلُ فِي أَخْذِهِ الصَّبِيَّ إِسْكَاتَهُ أَوْ حَمَلَهُ إِلَى مُرْضِعَتِهِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يُقْطَعُ إِذَا كَانَ عَلَيْهِ حُلِيٌّ وَهُوَ نَصْبٌ لِأَنَّهُ يَجِبُ الْقَطْعُ بِسَرْقَتِهِ وَحْدَهُ فَكَذَا مَعَ غَيْرِهِ وَعَلَى هَذَا إِذَا سَرَقَ إِنَاءَ فِضَّةٍ فِيهِ نَبِيذٌ أَوْ ثَرِيدٌ وَالْخِلَافُ فِي بِي لَا يَمْشِي وَلَا يَتَكَلَّمُ كَيْلَا يَكُونَ فِي يَدِ نَفْسِهِ
ترجمہ اور آزاد بچہ کے چرانے والے کا بھی ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ اگر چہ اس کے بدن پر زیور بھی ہو کیونکہ آزاد آدمی مال نہیں ہوتا ہے اور جو زیور اس پر ہے وہ اس کے تابع ہے اور اس لئے بھی کہ اسے لینے والا یہ تاویل کرے گا کہ میں نے اسے روتا دیکھ کر چپ کرنے کے لئے اٹھا لیا ہے۔ یا اس کے دودھ پلائی تک پہنچانے کے لئے اٹھایا ہے لیکن امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر اس کے بدن پر اس درہم کے وزن کا زیور ہو تو اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ صرف اتنا زیور ہی چرانے میں تو ہاتھ کاانا واجب ہوتا ہے۔ تو دوسری چیزوں کے ساتھ چرانے میں بھی واجب ہوگا۔ اسی طرح اگر چاندی کا کوئی ایسا برتن چرایا جس میں شراب یا ثرید ہو تو اس میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہوگا۔ یہ اختلاف ایسے لڑکے کے بارے میں ہے جو چلتا اور بولتا نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے ذاتی اختیار میں نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ فائدہ اگر لڑکا چلا اور بولتا ہو تو بالاتفاق اس کے چور کا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ اور اگر اتنے چھوٹے غلام کو چرایا جو بولتا نہ ہو تو بالاتفاق اس کا هاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔
And there is no cutting on the thief of a free child even if there is jewelry on him, because the free person is not property, and the jewelry on him is subordinate to him, and because the taker can claim (ta'wil) that he took the child to quiet him or to carry him to his wet nurse. And Abu Yusuf said: Cutting is applied if there is jewelry on him and it is a nisab, because cutting is wajib for stealing it alone, so likewise with others. And similarly, if he steals a silver vessel containing wine or tharid (soup). And the disagreement is regarding one who does not walk or speak, so that he is not in his own control.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof for theft of a free child. The Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that the hand is not cut because: (1) a free person is not property (mal), (2) any jewelry on the child is subordinate to the child, and (3) the thief can claim a plausible excuse (ta'wil) that he intended to soothe the child or take him to his nurse. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: if the child has jewelry reaching nisab, cutting is applied because stealing the jewelry alone would incur cutting, so stealing it with the child also incurs cutting. The passage then analogizes to stealing a silver vessel containing wine or tharid (soup) — the same intra-Hanafi difference applies. A key detail: this dispute is only for a child who cannot walk or speak (i.e., an infant). The Urdu commentary adds a benefit (fa'idah): if the child can walk and talk, then by consensus the thief's hand is not cut (because the child can resist or is more independent). If a young slave who cannot speak is stolen, then by consensus the hand is cut (because a slave is property). This highlights the conditions of mal and ta'wil in hadd cases.

Key Terms
حر (ḥurr): Free person, as opposed to a slave. A free person is not considered property (mal) for the purposes of hadd penalties.
تبع (tab'): Subordinate; the jewelry on a child is considered subordinate (tabi') to the child, so its value is not considered independently for hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, why is the hand not cut for stealing a free infant even if it wears jewelry worth nisab?
A) Because the infant cannot give consent to the theft.
B) Because the free child is not property and the jewelry is subordinate; also the thief can claim a plausible excuse like comforting the child.
C) Because the jewelry is considered part of the child's clothing and not separate property.
D) Because the nisab for jewelry worn by a child is higher than usual.

Key Takeaway
When a free child is stolen, the hand is not cut even if wearing valuable jewelry, because the child is not property and the jewelry is subordinate; the thief's plausible excuse (ta'wil) also creates a doubt that blocks the hadd.

The Shubha of Ta'wil: When Hadd is Averted in Theft
Ruling statement with rational proof, including a contrast.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stealing a gold cross, chessboard, or backgammon and explain how the thief's possible ta'wil (interpretation) creates a shubha (doubt) that prevents the hadd penalty.

Core Idea
A plausible legitimate intention (ta'wil) creates shubha, averting hadd in theft.

In Hanafi criminal law, the hadd penalty for theft is not applied mechanically. The texts consider not only the act and value but also the intent and possibility of a valid excuse. This lesson explores a key example: items that could be taken for a religious purpose (forbidding evil) fall under shubha, even if they have monetary value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items and ruling
List the three items mentioned: gold cross, chessboard, and backgammon. The text states the hand is not cut for stealing them.
The ruling is 'no hadd' (mubah in the sense of no penalty).
2
Extract the dalil (proof)
The proof is the phrase 'because the taker can claim the interpretation (ta'wil) that he took them to break and forbid evil.' This is the key reasoning.
The proof is a rational argument (dalil aqli) based on the principle that hudud are averted by doubts.
3
Understand the mechanism of shubha
The possibility of a valid intention (ta'wil) creates doubt about the criminal intent. Since hadd requires certainty, this doubt (shubha) blocks the penalty.
Hanafis apply the maxim: 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' (hudud are averted by doubts).
4
Contrast with the dirham example
A dirham with an image is not prepared for worship, so no shubha of permissibility of breaking exists. Hence, if nisab is reached, hadd applies.
This contrast highlights that the shubha is specific to objects associated with false worship or idle play.
5
Note the overall principle
In Hanafi fiqh, any plausible legitimate intention (ta'wil) that the thief could claim negates the certainty required for hadd, unless the object's nature precludes such intent.
This is a unique feature of Hanafi law compared to other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يقطع فيه و مالا يقطع .
تشریح وَلَا يُقْطَعُ فِي أَبْوَابِ الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ لِعَدَمِ الْإِحْرَازِ فَصَارَ الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
سونے کی صلیب، شطرنج اور نرد کی چوری پر ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔
قَالَ وَلَا الصَّلِيبِ مِنَ الذَّهَبِ وَلَا الشَّطْرَنجِ وَلَا النَّرْدِ لَانَّهُ يَتَأَوَّلُ مَنْ اَخَذَهَا الْكَسْرَنَهْيَا عَنِ الْمُنْكِرِ بِخِلَافِ الدرهم الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الحِمْثَالُ [؟] لأَنَّهُ مَا أُعِدَّ لِلْعِبَادَةِ فَلَا يَثْبُتُ شُبْهَهُ إِبَاحَةِ الْكَسْرِ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ الصَّلِيْبُ فِي الْمُصَلَّى لَا يُقْطَعُ لِعَدَمِ الْحِرْزِ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي بَيْتِ اخَرَ يُقْطَعُ لِكُمَالِ الْمَالِيَةِ وَالْحِرْزِ ترجمہ کہا، اگر کسی نے سونے کی صلیب یا شطرنج یا نزد نون اور راء کے فتحہ کے ساتھ ) چرالی تو اس کا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ چور اس کے لینے میں یہ تاویل کرلے گا کہ میں نے لوگوں کو شرعی ممنوع چیز سے روکنے کا ارادہ کیا تھا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر ایسا درہم چرالیا جس پر کسی کی تصویر بنی ہوئی ہو اور وہ مقدار نصاب ہو تو اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تصویر عبادت کے واسطے نہیں بنائی گئی ہے اس لئے اس کے بارے میں یہ شبہ نہ رہا کہ اسے توڑ دینا جائز ہے۔ یعنی اس کے چراتے وقت چور یہ بہانہ نہیں بنا سکتا ہے کہ میں نے اسے توڑنے کے واسطے لیا تھا اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ اگر سونے کی صلیب ان کی گرجا گھر میں ہو تو وہاں سے چرانے میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ محفوظ مکان میں نہیں ہے اور اگر کسی نصرانی کے کمرہ میں ہو یعنی محفوظ ہوتو ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس کی مالیت بھی پوری ہے اور حفاظت بھی پوری موجود ہے۔
تشريح قَالَ وَلَا الصَّلِيبِ مِنَ الذَّهَبِ وَلَا الشَّطْرَنجِ وَلَا النَّرْدِ لأَنَّهُ يَتَأَوَّلُ مَنْ الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Chapter on what the hand is cut for and what not. Explanation: And the hand is not cut for stealing the doors of the Sacred Mosque due to lack of secure enclosure. The meaning is clear from the translation. The hand will not be cut for stealing a gold cross, chessboard, or backgammon. He said: And not for a gold cross, nor chessboard, nor backgammon, because the taker can claim the interpretation that he took them to break and forbid evil, unlike a dirham on which there is an image, because it was not prepared for worship, so the doubt of permissibility of breaking is not established. And from Abu Yusuf: If the cross is in a place of worship, the hand is not cut due to lack of secure enclosure; and if in another house, the hand is cut due to complete monetary value and secure enclosure. Translation: He said, if someone stole a gold cross or chessboard or backgammon, his hand will not be cut. Because the thief can claim the interpretation that he intended to prevent people from something legally prohibited. In contrast, if he stole a dirham on which someone's image is engraved and it reaches the nisab, his hand will be cut. Because this image was not made for worship, so there remains no doubt that breaking it is permissible. That is, at the time of stealing, the thief cannot make the excuse that he took it to break. And from Imam Abu Yusuf, a narration that if the gold cross is in their church, stealing from there does not require cutting the hand because it is not in a secure place; and if in a Christian's room, i.e., secure, then the hand is cut because its monetary value is complete and its preservation is complete. Explanation: He said: And not for a gold cross, nor chessboard, nor backgammon, because the taker can claim the interpretation — the meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on theft of items that have a potential religious or permissible use. The core principle is that if the stolen object can be interpreted as being taken for a legitimate purpose (like destroying an object of false worship to forbid evil), then the hadd penalty of cutting the hand is not applied due to shubha (doubt). This is a ruling statement with proof. The author begins by stating that the hand is not cut for stealing the doors of the Sacred Mosque due to lack of hirz (secure enclosure). Then he moves to the specific items: a gold cross, chessboard, and backgammon. The reasoning is that the thief could claim he intended to break them to prevent evil, creating a shubha that negates the hadd. In contrast, a dirham with an image engraved on it is not prepared for worship, so no such shubha exists, and the hadd applies if the nisab is met. Imam Abu Yusuf adds a condition: if the cross is in a church, it is not properly secured (because churches are open), so no hadd; but if it is in a private secure room, the hadd applies because it has both full monetary value and secure enclosure. The commentary (sharh) reiterates that the meaning is clear from the translation.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of hadd penalties in theft.
تاویل (ta'wil): An interpretation or excuse that the thief could claim to justify his action as permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hand not cut for stealing a gold cross according to the matn?
A) Because gold is not considered property worthy of protection.
B) Because the thief can claim he intended to break it to forbid evil, creating a shubha.
C) Because crosses are not stored in secure enclosures.
D) Because the cross has no monetary value.

Key Takeaway
A plausible legitimate intention (ta'wil) creates shubha, and under Hanafi law, any doubt averts the hadd penalty for theft.

Abu Yusuf's Nuance: Hirz and Monetary Value in Theft of Crosses
Intra-Hanafi dispute with conditional ruling based on hirz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding theft of a gold cross, and apply the condition of hirz (secure enclosure) to determine when hadd applies.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf adds hirz: if secured, hadd; if not, no hadd, even with shubha.

While the primary Hanafi position holds that shubha from ta'wil always negates hadd for certain objects, Imam Abu Yusuf introduced a refinement based on the security of the place (hirz). This lesson examines that intra-madhhab difference and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Recall the matn's ruling
The matn states: no hadd for stealing a gold cross, regardless of location, because of the shubha of ta'wil.
This is the ruling from Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah).
2
Identify Abu Yusuf’s variant
The text adds: 'And from Abu Yusuf: if the cross is in a place of worship (musalla), the hand is not cut due to lack of hirz; if in another house, the hand is cut due to complete monetary value and hirz.'
This is a conditional ruling based on security.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Yusuf treats hirz as a necessary condition for hadd. If the cross is in a secure private room, it has complete value and protection, so hadd applies. If in an open church, it lacks hirz, so even with value, no hadd.
This suggests Abu Yusuf prioritizes hirz over shubha in secure locations.
4
Determine the conflict
The matn’s ruling seems to ignore hirz: even if the cross is secured, the shubha still prevents hadd. Abu Yusuf disagrees: in a secure place, the shubha is outweighed by complete value and hirz.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is the matn’s (no hadd regardless of hirz), as it is from Zahir al-Riwayah. Abu Yusuf’s view is recorded but not the primary fatwa.
However, some later Hanafi fatwa may consider Abu Yusuf’s view in cases where hirz is clear.

Source Text

سونے کی صلیب، شطرنج اور نرد کی چوری پر ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔
قَالَ وَلَا الصَّلِيبِ مِنَ الذَّهَبِ وَلَا الشَّطْرَنجِ وَلَا النَّرْدِ لَانَّهُ يَتَأَوَّلُ مَنْ اَخَذَهَا الْكَسْرَنَهْيَا عَنِ الْمُنْكِرِ بِخِلَافِ الدرهم الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الحِمْثَالُ [؟] لأَنَّهُ مَا أُعِدَّ لِلْعِبَادَةِ فَلَا يَثْبُتُ شُبْهَهُ إِبَاحَةِ الْكَسْرِ وَعَنْ أَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنَّهُ إِنْ كَانَ الصَّلِيْبُ فِي الْمُصَلَّى لَا يُقْطَعُ لِعَدَمِ الْحِرْزِ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي بَيْتِ اخَرَ يُقْطَعُ لِكُمَالِ الْمَالِيَةِ وَالْحِرْزِ ترجمہ کہا، اگر کسی نے سونے کی صلیب یا شطرنج یا نزد نون اور راء کے فتحہ کے ساتھ ) چرالی تو اس کا ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ چور اس کے لینے میں یہ تاویل کرلے گا کہ میں نے لوگوں کو شرعی ممنوع چیز سے روکنے کا ارادہ کیا تھا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر ایسا درہم چرالیا جس پر کسی کی تصویر بنی ہوئی ہو اور وہ مقدار نصاب ہو تو اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ تصویر عبادت کے واسطے نہیں بنائی گئی ہے اس لئے اس کے بارے میں یہ شبہ نہ رہا کہ اسے توڑ دینا جائز ہے۔ یعنی اس کے چراتے وقت چور یہ بہانہ نہیں بنا سکتا ہے کہ میں نے اسے توڑنے کے واسطے لیا تھا اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ اگر سونے کی صلیب ان کی گرجا گھر میں ہو تو وہاں سے چرانے میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ محفوظ مکان میں نہیں ہے اور اگر کسی نصرانی کے کمرہ میں ہو یعنی محفوظ ہوتو ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس کی مالیت بھی پوری ہے اور حفاظت بھی پوری موجود ہے۔
تشريح قَالَ وَلَا الصَّلِيبِ مِنَ الذَّهَبِ وَلَا الشَّطْرَنجِ وَلَا النَّرْدِ لأَنَّهُ يَتَأَوَّلُ مَنْ الخ مطلب ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Chapter on what the hand is cut for and what not. Explanation: And the hand is not cut for stealing the doors of the Sacred Mosque due to lack of secure enclosure. The meaning is clear from the translation. The hand will not be cut for stealing a gold cross, chessboard, or backgammon. He said: And not for a gold cross, nor chessboard, nor backgammon, because the taker can claim the interpretation that he took them to break and forbid evil, unlike a dirham on which there is an image, because it was not prepared for worship, so the doubt of permissibility of breaking is not established. And from Abu Yusuf: If the cross is in a place of worship, the hand is not cut due to lack of secure enclosure; and if in another house, the hand is cut due to complete monetary value and secure enclosure. Translation: He said, if someone stole a gold cross or chessboard or backgammon, his hand will not be cut. Because the thief can claim the interpretation that he intended to prevent people from something legally prohibited. In contrast, if he stole a dirham on which someone's image is engraved and it reaches the nisab, his hand will be cut. Because this image was not made for worship, so there remains no doubt that breaking it is permissible. That is, at the time of stealing, the thief cannot make the excuse that he took it to break. And from Imam Abu Yusuf, a narration that if the gold cross is in their church, stealing from there does not require cutting the hand because it is not in a secure place; and if in a Christian's room, i.e., secure, then the hand is cut because its monetary value is complete and its preservation is complete. Explanation: He said: And not for a gold cross, nor chessboard, nor backgammon, because the taker can claim the interpretation — the meaning is clear from the translation.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on theft of items that have a potential religious or permissible use. The core principle is that if the stolen object can be interpreted as being taken for a legitimate purpose (like destroying an object of false worship to forbid evil), then the hadd penalty of cutting the hand is not applied due to shubha (doubt). This is a ruling statement with proof. The author begins by stating that the hand is not cut for stealing the doors of the Sacred Mosque due to lack of hirz (secure enclosure). Then he moves to the specific items: a gold cross, chessboard, and backgammon. The reasoning is that the thief could claim he intended to break them to prevent evil, creating a shubha that negates the hadd. In contrast, a dirham with an image engraved on it is not prepared for worship, so no such shubha exists, and the hadd applies if the nisab is met. Imam Abu Yusuf adds a condition: if the cross is in a church, it is not properly secured (because churches are open), so no hadd; but if it is in a private secure room, the hadd applies because it has both full monetary value and secure enclosure. The commentary (sharh) reiterates that the meaning is clear from the translation.

Key Terms
حِرْز (hirz): A secure place where property is stored, affecting the applicability of hadd in theft.
تاویل (ta'wil): An interpretation or excuse that the thief could claim to justify his action as permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only if the cross is in a church.
C) Only if the cross is in a private secure room.
D) Never, because gold crosses are not subject to hadd.

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, the primary position (matn) negates hadd for stealing a gold cross due to shubha, but Abu Yusuf adds a condition of hirz that can lead to hadd in secure locations.

Theft of a Free Child: No Hadd Even with Jewelry
Ruling on theft of a free child: no hadd, with intra-Hanafi dispute based on child's mobility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stealing a free child wearing jewelry and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the application of hadd.

Core Idea
A free person is not property, so theft of a free child does not incur hadd, even if the child wears jewelry.

The passage examines a nuanced scenario in hadd al-sariqa: what if someone steals a free infant wearing valuable jewelry? While theft of property triggers the hadd, the Hanafi school argues that the free child's person is immune from being considered stolen property. Furthermore, the jewelry is subsidiary (tabi') to the child, and the thief might claim a legitimate excuse (shubha). However, Imam Abu Yusuf dissents when the child is immobile and the jewelry alone would have triggered hadd. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being stolen? A free infant with jewelry. The ruling: no cutting of hand.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The free person is not mal (property) – a key principle in Hanafi fiqh.
Quran and Sunnah establish that only property can be stolen for hadd.
3
Understand the subsidiary (tabi') principle
The jewelry is subsidiary to the child, so theft of the child with jewelry is not theft of jewelry independently.
4
Examine the shubha (legal doubt)
The thief could have taken the child for a permissible purpose (silencing crying, returning to nurse) – this creates doubt that averts hadd.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf argues that if the child is immobile and the jewelry alone meets nisab, hadd applies for the jewelry. The text analogizes to stealing a silver vessel containing wine/tharid. Note: The dispute is only for infants who cannot walk/talk; if the child is mobile, consensus on no hadd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا قَطعَ عَلَى شَارِقِ الصَّبِيِّ الْحُرِّوَانْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ حُلِيٌّ لِاَنَّ الْحُرَّلَيْسَ بِمَالٍ وَمَاعَلَيْهِ مِنَ الْحُلِيِّ تَبْعٌ لَهُ وَلَانَّهُ يَتَأَوَّلُ فِى أَخْذِهِ الصَّبِيِّ إِسْكَاتَهُ اَوْ حَمَلَهُ إِلى مُرْضِعَتِهِ وَ قَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ يُقْطَعُ إِذَا كَانَ عَلَيْهِ حُلِيٌّ وَهُوَ نَصْبٌ لِأَنَّهُ يَجِبُ الْقَطْعُ بِسَرْقَتِهِ وَحْدَهُ فَكَذَا مَعَ غَيْرِهِ وَعَلَى هَذَا إِذَا سَرَقَ إِنَاءَ فِضَّةٍ فِيْهِ نَبِيِّذْأُوْثَرِيْدٌ وَالْخِلَافُ فِي بِي لَا يَمْشِي وَلَا يَتَكَلَّمُ كَيْلَا يَكُونَ فِي يَدِنَفْسِهِ ترجمہ اور آزاد بچہ کے چرانے والے کا بھی ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ اگر چہ اس کے بدن پر زیور بھی ہو کیونکہ آزاد آدمی مال نہیں ہوتا ہے اور جو زیور اس پر ہے وہ اس کے تابع ہے اور اس لئے بھی کہ اسے لینے والا یہ تاویل کرے گا کہ میں نے اسے روتا دیکھ کر چپ کرنے کے لئے اٹھا لیا ہے۔ یا اس کے دودھ پلائی تک پہنچانے کے لئے اٹھایا ہے لیکن امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر اس کے بدن پر اس درہم کے وزن کا زیور ہو تو اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ صرف اتنا زیور ہی چرانے میں تو ہاتھ کا انا واجب ہوتا ہے۔ تو دوسری چیزوں کے ساتھ چرانے میں بھی واجب ہوگا۔ اسی طرح اگر چاندی کا کوئی ایسا برتن چرایا جس میں شراب یا ثرید ہو تو اس میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہوگا۔ یہ اختلاف ایسے لڑکے کے بارے میں ہے جو چلتا اور بولتا نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے ذاتی اختیار میں نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ فائدہ اگرلڑ کا چلا اور بولتا ہوتو بالا جماع اس کے چور کا ہاتھ نہیں کا نا جائے گا الحط ۔ اور اگر اتنے چھوٹے غلام کو چرایا جو بولتا نہ ہوتو بالاتفاق اس کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔
And there is no cutting of the hand on the stealer of a free child, even if there is jewelry on him, because the free person is not property, and what jewelry is on him is subsidiary to him, and because he can claim interpretation in taking the child: to silence him or to carry him to his wet nurse. And Abu Yusuf said: The hand is cut if there is jewelry on him and it is a nisab, because the cutting is obligatory by stealing it alone, so also with other things. And similarly, if he steals a silver vessel in which there is wine or tharid, and the dispute is regarding a child who does not walk or talk, so that he is not in his own control. Translation: And the hand of the stealer of a free child will also not be cut, even if there is jewelry on his body, because a free person is not property, and the jewelry on him is subsidiary. And also because the taker will make the interpretation that he saw him crying and picked him up to quiet him, or to take him to his wet nurse. But Imam Abu Yusuf said: If there is jewelry on his body equal to the weight of a dirham (nisab), then his hand will be cut, because cutting is obligatory for stealing that jewelry alone, so also when stolen with other things. Similarly, if he steals a silver vessel containing wine or tharid, the same dispute applies. This dispute is regarding a child who does not walk or talk, because he is not under his own control. Benefit: If the child walks and talks, then by consensus the thief's hand is not cut. And if a minor slave who does not talk is stolen, then by consensus his hand is cut.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage rules on theft of a free child. The main ruling is that no hadd is applied because a free person is not property, and any jewelry on the child is subsidiary. Additionally, a thief could claim he picked up the child to calm him or take him to his nurse, creating a shubha. Imam Abu Yusuf differs: if the child is wearing jewelry of nisab value, the hadd applies for the jewelry, and if the child is immobile (does not walk or talk), the hadd applies. The commentary clarifies that if the child is mobile (walks and talks), there is consensus that no hadd. The dispute only applies to infants who cannot move or speak. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
تابع (tabi'): Subsidiary; the jewelry is considered subsidiary to the child's person, so its theft does not independently incur hadd.
شبهة (shubha): Legal doubt; here, the thief's possible innocent intention creates doubt that averts the hadd penalty.
مال (mal): Property; only theft of property can incur the hadd penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The child must be wearing gold jewelry.
B) The child must be an infant who does not walk or talk.
C) The child must be a slave.
D) The child must be asleep.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, theft of a free child does not incur hadd because a free person is not property and any accompanying items are subsidiary, creating a legal doubt.

Hadd for Theft of a Slave: Adult vs Minor
Distinguishes between theft of an adult slave (no hadd) and a minor slave (hadd applies)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on theft of a minor slave and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, including the role of istihsan.

Core Idea
A minor slave is pure property; an adult slave is not — theft of the former incurs hadd.

This lesson examines the fine distinction between stealing an adult slave and a minor slave in Hanafi hudud law. While theft of property normally incurs the hadd of amputation, slaves occupy a unique category because they are both human and property. The Hanafi school splits on how to treat a minor slave who cannot reason or speak, with Abu Yusuf invoking istihsan to avoid the hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Note the two-part ruling: theft of an adult slave → no hadd (it is ghasp or khida'); theft of a minor slave → hadd applies, except if the slave can express himself (then no hadd).
The exception makes the minor equal to an adult in terms of control over his own hand.
2
Analyze the proof for the majority
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that a minor slave is absolute property because benefit is taken from him now or expected in the future. The attached 'human' aspect does not negate his proprietary nature.
This is a rational (dalil aqli) argument based on the purpose of property.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's istihsan
Abu Yusuf says the hand is not cut for a minor slave who cannot reason or speak, by istihsan. Because the slave is both human and property, a shubha (doubt) exists that prevents the hadd.
Istihsan is used to avoid the harshness of analogy (qiyas).
4
Resolve the dispute
The text indicates that the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (wa lahuma) is relied upon, as the slave's property aspect is dominant. The hadd is applied.
This is the mufta bihi position.

وَلَا قَطعَ فِي سَرْقَةِ الْعَبْدِ الْكَبِيرِ لأَنَّهُ غَضَبٌ اَوْخِدَاعٌ وَيُقْطَعُ فِي سَرْقَةِ الْعَبْدِ الصَّغِيْرِ لِتَحَقُّقِهَا بِحَدِهَا إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ يُعَتِرُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ وَالْبَالِغُ سَوَاءٌ فِي اِعْتِبَارِيَدِهِ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ لَا يُقْطَعُ وَإِنْ كَانَ صَغِيرً ا لَا يَعْقِلُ وَلَا يَتَكَلَّمُ اِسْتِحْسَانُ لِأَنَّهُ ادَمِيٌّ مِنْ وَجْهِ مَالٌ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ مَالٌ مُطْلَقٌ لِكَوْنِهِ مُنْتَفِعَابِهِ أَوْ بِعَرْضِ أَنْ يَصِيرَ مُنْتَفِعَابِهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ انْضَمَّ إِلَيْهِ مَعْنَى الْأَدَمِيَّةِ ترجمہ اور بالغ غلام کے چرانے میں ہاتھ کاٹنے کا حکم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ غصب یا دھوکہ ہے۔ لیکن نابالغ کے چرانے میں ہاتھ کا ٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس میں چوری کی پوری تعریف پائی جاتی ہے۔ لیکن اگر اتنا چھوٹا غلام ہو کہ وہ اپنا نام بتلا سکتا ہوتو ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا کیونکہ وہ فی الحال اپنے قابو میں ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ اور ایک بالغ دونوں برابر ہوں گے اور امام ابو یوسف رحمتہ اللہ علیہ نے کہا ہے کہ چھوٹے غلام کی چوری میں ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ اگر چہ وہ اتنا چھوٹا ہو کہ وہ نہ تو کچھ سجھتا ہواور نہ باتیں کرتا ہو۔ یہ حکم استحسانی ہے کیونکہ وہ ایک اعتبار سے آدمی ہے تو دوسرے اعتبار سے مال ہے اور امام ابوحنیفہ محمد رحمہم اللہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ نفع اٹھانے کے لائق مال ہے خواہ فی الحال ہو یا آئندہ چل کر ہو۔ اگر چہ اس کے ساتھ آدمی کا نام ملا دیا گیا ہے تو اس کے ساتھ نام ملا دینے سے مال کی مالیت میں کچھ فرق نہیں آیا۔ اس لئے چور کا ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔
And there is no cutting in theft of an adult slave, because it is usurpation or deception. And cutting is applied in theft of a minor slave due to its realization with its definition, except when he can express himself, because then he and the adult are equal in consideration of his hand. And Abu Yusuf said: The hand is not cut even if he is a minor who does not reason or speak, as istihsan, because he is a human from one aspect and property from another. And for the two of them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), he is absolute property because benefit is taken from him or it is expected that benefit will be taken from him, except that the meaning of humanity is joined to him. Translation: And the hand is not cut for theft of an adult slave, because it is usurpation or deception. But for theft of a minor slave, the hand is cut because the complete definition of theft applies. However, if the slave is so young that he can state his name, then the hand is not cut, because he is under his own control like an adult. And Imam Abu Yusuf said: The hand is not cut for theft of a minor slave, even if he is so young that he neither understands nor speaks. This ruling is istihsan, because he is from one aspect a human and from another aspect property. And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is that he is absolute property because benefit is taken from him now or will be taken in the future, and even though the name 'human' is attached to him, it does not remove his proprietary nature. Therefore, the thief's hand is cut.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage addresses theft of slaves. The main ruling: theft of an adult slave does not incur hadd because it is considered ghasp (usurpation) or khida' (deception), not theft. However, theft of a minor slave does incur hadd because it fulfills the complete definition of theft. An exception is if the minor slave can express himself (speak and understand), then no hadd. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that even a minor slave who does not reason or speak should not incur hadd, by istihsan, because a slave is both human and property. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two) argue that a minor slave is absolute property because benefit is derived from him, and the aspect of humanity does not negate his status as property. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute with clear arguments.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasp): Usurpation; taking property by force without right, distinct from theft (sariqa) which requires stealth.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; Abu Yusuf uses it to prefer no hadd for a minor slave despite the apparent analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the ruling on theft of a minor slave who cannot reason or speak?
A) No hadd because the slave is both human and property.
B) Hadd applies because the minor slave is absolute property.
C) No hadd because the slave cannot be owned.
D) Hadd applies only if the minor slave is valuable.

Key Takeaway
A minor slave is treated as pure property for hadd purposes; only if he can express himself does he become like an adult slave, removing the hadd.

Theft of Registers and Books: When Hadd Applies
Explains that stealing registers does not incur hadd unless the registers are account books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion of intent (maqsud) to distinguish cases where theft of written materials incurs the hadd penalty.

Core Idea
If the content is the purpose, no hadd; if the paper itself is the target, hadd applies.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Hanafi fiqh on the theft of registers and books. The general rule is that stealing such items does not incur the hadd of amputation because the intended purpose is the content, which is not considered property. However, an exception exists for account books, where the paper itself is the intended object. Through this ruling, we learn how Hanafi jurists evaluate the nature of the stolen item, focusing on what the thief actually intended to take.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
The passage states: 'No cutting in all registers.' This is the default position – theft of any register or book does not incur the hadd penalty.
Hadd is the prescribed punishment for theft (amputation of the hand).
2
Understand the Rationale
The reason given is that 'the intended purpose is what is in them, and that is not property.' In other words, the thief's goal is the content (writing), not the paper itself. The content is not considered mal (property) for the purposes of hadd.
Mal in Hanafi usul is something that has material value and is legitimately owned.
3
Identify the Exception
The exception is 'registers of accounts.' Why? Because in these, the content (numbers) is not the target; the thief wants the physical paper. Thus, the object taken is mal, and hadd applies.
The Urdu commentary explains that account books are stolen for their paper value or as evidence.
4
Apply the Criterion to New Cases
Using the same logic, assess other written materials. Religious books, newspapers, novels – if the content is the purpose, no hadd. Official documents, registries, secret papers – if the paper itself is valuable, hadd applies.
The criterion depends on the thief's intent, as inferred from custom and circumstance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا قَطعَ فِي الدَّفَاتِرِ كُلِهَا لِاَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مَافِيْهَا وَذَالِكَ لَيْسَ بِمَالٍ إِلَّا فِى دَفَاتِرِ الْحِسَابِ لِأَنَّ مَافِيهَا لَا يُقْصَدُ بِالْاخْذِفَكَانَ الْمَقْصُودُ وَهُوَ الْكَوَاعِدُ ترجمہ اور کل دفتروں (رجسٹروں اور کاپیوں) کے چرانے سے بھی ہاتھ نہیں کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس سے مقصود وہ تحریر ہوتی ہے جو اس میں پائی جاتی ہے۔ حالانکہ وہ مال نہیں ہے۔ سوائے اہل حساب کے دفتر کے یعنی اس کی چوری سے ہاتھ کاٹا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ جو کچھ اس دفتر اور کاپی میں لکھا گیا ہے اس کا لینا مقصود نہیں ہے تو یہی کا پیاں اور کاغذات ہی مقصود ہوئے۔
تشريح وَلَا قَطعَ فِي الدَّفَاتِرِ كُلَّهَا لِاَنَّ الْمَقْصُودُ مَا فِيهَا وَذَالِكَ لَيْسَ بِمَالٍ إِلَّا في الخ کا غذات یا تو مذہبی کتابوں قرآن پاک، حديث ، تصوف تغییر وغیرہ کی کتابیں ہوں یا علماء کی اصلاحی تقریریں یا کیسٹیں وغیرہ ان کی چوری پر قطع ید نہیں کہ یہ مال نہیں بلکہ ان کا مقصد تحقیق مطالعہ اور اصلاح ہوتی ہے۔ اس طرح غیر مذہبی کتابیں اخبارات ناولیں وغیرہ پر بھی قطع ید نہیں ایسے کاغذات جو عدالتوں کچہریوں میں استعمال ہوتے ہیں یا بطور ریکارڈ ہوتے ہیں جیسے مکانات و دکانوں کی رجسٹریاں وغیرہ یا کسی ملک یا عظیم شخصیت کے راز ان کا غذات میں ہوں ایسے کاغذات کی چوری پر حد واجب ہے ۔ اس طرح ملکی تعمیر اور اہم کام منصوبوں کے کاغذات کی چوری پر بھی حد سرقہ ہے۔
And there is no cutting in all registers, because the intended purpose is what is in them, and that is not property, except in registers of accounts, because what is in them is not intended by taking, so the intended thing is the papers. Translation: And the hand is also not cut for stealing all registers (ledgers and books), because the purpose is the writing found in them, and that is not property. Except for the books of accountants, i.e., stealing them incurs cutting the hand, because what is written in those books is not the intended object; rather, the papers themselves are the intended object. Explanation: And no cutting in all registers, because the intended purpose is what is in them, and that is not property, except in... So either they are religious books (Qur'an, hadith, tasawwuf, etc.) or scholars' reformist speeches or tapes, etc. For stealing these, there is no cutting because they are not property; their purpose is research, study, and reform. Similarly, for non-religious books, newspapers, novels, etc., there is no cutting. Such papers that are used in courts or as records, like registries of houses and shops, or that contain secrets of a country or a great personality, for stealing such papers, the hadd is obligatory. Similarly, for stealing papers of national construction and important projects, the hadd of theft applies.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage rules on theft of registers and books. The general principle is that if the content (writing) is the main purpose, the paper itself is not considered property, so no hadd. However, if the paper itself is the intended object (like account books where the figures are not the target), then hadd applies. The Urdu commentary elaborates: religious books, reformist materials, newspapers, novels — no hadd because content is the purpose. But official documents, registries, secret papers — hadd applies because the paper itself is valuable. This is a ruling statement without explicit proof, but the reasoning is based on the nature of property.

Key Terms
دفاتر (dafatir): Registers or books containing writing; the material medium is not always considered property.
مقصود (maqsud): Intended object or purpose; the criterion for determining if hadd applies in theft of written materials.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, which of the following would incur the hadd penalty for theft?
A) Stealing a stack of religious pamphlets from a mosque.
B) Stealing a novel from a bookstore when the thief intends to read it.
C) Stealing an accountant's ledger book from a company.
D) Stealing a newspaper from a newsstand.

Key Takeaway
The hadd punishment for theft does not apply to registers and books when the content is the intended purpose, but it applies when the physical medium itself is the target, as in account books and official documents.

Hadd for Stealing a Dog or Cheetah
Begins ruling that theft of a dog or cheetah does not incur hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school does not apply hadd for stealing a dog or cheetah and identify the legal principle of shubha in property.

Core Idea
Theft of a dog or cheetah incurs no hadd because their species includes mubah al-asl — originally permissible and undesired.

The Hudud punishments are severe and reserved for clear violations of protected rights. This passage addresses a specific case: stealing a dog or cheetah. The Hanafi ruling is that no hadd applies. The reasoning is tied to the nature of these animals — they are from a species that includes animals which are originally permissible and not typically desired as property. This creates a doubt (shubha) regarding their status as owned property, and hadd is not applied when such doubt exists. Let us examine the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is stealing (sariqa) a dog or a cheetah. The ruling is that no hadd (amputation) is incurred.
The hadd is the fixed punishment for theft.
2
Understand the first reason: mubah al-asl
The text says 'because from their species exists that which is originally permissible and not desired.' This means there are wild dogs or cheetahs that are not owned. So the stolen animal's status as property is doubtful.
Mubah al-asl refers to animals that are not inherently owned.
3
Understand the second reason: ikhtilaf (dispute)
The passage begins to mention a dispute (al-ikhtilaf bayna...) but cuts off. Likely there is a disagreement about whether these animals can be owned. This further strengthens the shubha.
The incomplete sentence suggests a disagreement with another school.
4
Apply the principle of shubha
In Hanafi fiqh, hadd is not applied when there is any reasonable doubt (shubha) regarding the rightness of the act or the status of the property. Here, the doubt comes from the animal's species including mubah al-asl.
Shubha blocks the hadd even if the animal is privately owned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This incomplete passage begins the ruling that theft of a dog or cheetah does not incur hadd. The reasoning given is that these animals are from a species that is originally permissible (mubah) and not generally desired as property. The passage cuts off mid-sentence, indicating a dispute with another school or scholar. The full ruling would typically include the conclusion that no hadd applies due to these factors.

Key Terms
مباح الأصل (mubah al-asl): Originally permissible; animals like dogs and cheetahs are not inherently owned, so theft of them does not violate property rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
No hadd for stealing a dog or cheetah because their genus includes mubah al-asl, creating a doubt about their property status.

Hadd for Stealing a Slave: Mature vs Minor
States ruling on hadd for stealing slaves, with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd for stealing a minor slave and identify the intra-madhhab disagreement with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A mature slave's theft is non-hadd due to ghasb/khidā‘; a minor's theft incurs hadd unless he can defend himself.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a key hudud distinction: stealing a mature slave does not trigger the hadd amputation because the taking is considered usurpation (ghasb) or deception (khidā‘), not stealthy theft (sariqa). For a minor slave who cannot understand or speak, the full hadd applies because the slave is pure property (mal mutlaq). However, the ruling shifts if the minor can defend himself, and Abu Yusuf holds that no hadd applies to any minor infant, citing the slave's humanity.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish mature vs minor slaves
Identify the two categories: mature slave (baligh) who can act independently, and minor slave who cannot understand or speak. The ruling hinges on the slave's capacity to be taken by force or deception rather than stealth.
A mature slave is considered to have agency, so taking him is ghasb (open seizure) or khidā‘ (trickery), not sariqa.
2
Apply the ruling to each category
State: no cut for a mature slave; cut for a minor slave who cannot defend himself. If the minor can defend himself (e.g., can speak or ward off an attack), then no cut, like the adult.
The exception for a minor who can defend himself aligns him with the adult in ruling.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf disagrees: even a minor infant who cannot understand or speak is not subject to hadd, on basis of istihsan, because the slave is human in one respect and property in another, creating doubt (shubha).
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (lahuma) hold that the slave is absolute property (mal mutlaq) since benefit is derived from him.
4
Analyze the underlying reasoning (ta'lil)
The majority view: the human aspect (ma‘nā al-ādamiyya) does not nullify the property status; it is merely an attached quality. For Abu Yusuf, the humanity creates doubt that precludes the hadd.
The dispute centers on whether the slave's humanity generates a shubha sufficient to drop the hadd.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position of the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: hadd applies to a minor slave who cannot defend himself.
This is the view adopted in the authoritative works (zahir al-riwaya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا قَطعَ فِي سَرْقَةِ الْعَبْدِ الْكَبِيرِ لأَنَّهُ غَضَبٌ اَوْخِدَاعٌ وَيُقْطَعُ فِي سَرْقَةِ الْعَبْدِ الصَّغِيْرِ لِتَحَقُّقِهَا بِحَدِهَا إِلَّا إِذَا كَانَ يُعَتِرُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ لِأَنَّهُ هُوَ وَالْبَالِغُ سَوَاءٌ فِي اِعْتِبَارِيَدِهِ وَقَالَ أَبُويُوسُفَ لَا يُقْطَعُ وَإِنْ كَانَ صَغِيرً ا لَا يَعْقِلُ وَلَا يَتَكَلَّمُ اِسْتِحْسَانُ لِأَنَّهُ ادَمِيٌّ مِنْ وَجْهِ مَالٌ مِنْ وَجْهِ وَلَهُمَا أَنَّهُ مَالٌ مُطْلَقٌ لِكَوْنِهِ مُنْتَفِعَابِهِ أَوْ بِعَرْضِ أَنْ يَصِيرَ مُنْتَفِعَابِهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ انْضَمَّ إِلَيْهِ مَعْنَى الْأَدَمِيَّةِ
And there is no cutting in the theft of a mature slave because it is usurpation or deception. And cutting is imposed in the theft of a minor slave because the theft is realized in its full definition, unless he can defend himself, because he and the adult are equal in consideration of his control. And Abu Yusuf said: No cutting is imposed even if he is a minor who does not understand and does not speak, by istihsan, because he is human from one aspect and property from another. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that he is absolute property because he is benefited from him or in the hope of benefiting from him, except that the meaning of humanity is attached to him.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on stealing slaves. The author first gives the rule: there is no hadd for stealing a mature slave because the act is considered ghasb (usurpation) or khiyana (breach of trust) since a mature slave can be moved by his own will, thus the taking lacks the secrecy and stealth necessary for full theft. For a minor slave who cannot defend himself, the hadd applies because the taking meets all conditions of theft. However, if the minor can speak and identify himself, he is like an adult and no cutting. Abu Yusuf disagrees and says no cutting even for a non-speaking infant, using istihsan: such a slave is both human (thus cannot be owned in the full sense of theft) and property. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the slave is absolute property (mal mutlaq) because one benefits from him now or in future, so the hadd applies. The passage is a ruling statement with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
غَصَب (ghasb): Usurpation; taking property openly by force or coercion, not stealthily.
خِدَاع (khidā‘): Deception; taking by trickery, not by stealth.
مَال مُطْلَق (māl muṭlaq): Absolute property; an object that is purely property without any countervailing legal status.
اِسْتِحْسَان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that allows departing from strict analogy due to a stronger consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, why does the hadd apply for stealing a minor slave who cannot understand or speak?
A) Because the slave is worth more than the nisab.
B) Because the slave is absolute property (mal mutlaq).
C) Because the taking is done by stealth.
D) Because the slave is not considered a human.

Key Takeaway
Hadd for theft of a slave depends on the slave's capacity: no hadd for a mature slave (ghasb/khidā‘), hadd for a minor slave who cannot defend himself (mal mutlaq), with Abu Yusuf dissenting on the minor infant.
